The Condition of General Permission (Idhn al-'Amm) for Jumu'ah
A condition for Jumu'ah: public permission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of general permission for Jumu'ah and explain its authority status within the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah must be performed publicly; closed-door Jumu'ah is invalid.

This passage from the commentary on al-Kanz clarifies an additional condition for Jumu'ah: that it must be accessible to the public. While not mentioned in the core Hanafi texts (zahir al-riwayah), this condition is upheld in later fatwa works. Understanding its basis helps you appreciate how Hanafi fiqh evolves through the Nawadir.

Guided Path
1
State the condition and its rationale
Identify the fifth condition of Jumu'ah in al-Kanz: general public permission. Note the reason: Jumu'ah is a public symbol of Islam and must be performed openly.
The condition is 'idhn al-'amm'.
2
Apply the rule to the case of closed doors
If the imam closes the door of the place of prayer, even if he prays with a group, the Jumu'ah is invalid because it loses the public character.
The ruling is 'lam yajuz' (not permissible).
3
Differentiate total closure vs. granting access
If the imam closes the door but permits people to enter upon request, the Jumu'ah is valid. However, if a congregational mosque exists, closing its door is makruh.
The validity depends on actual public access, not just permission.
4
Identify the authority level
Al-Hidayah did not mention this condition because it is not in the zahir al-riwayah. It is from the Nawadir (rare transmissions). Later works like al-Kanz adopted it, and it is relied upon in fatwa.
This shows the role of Nawadir in supplementing the madhhab.
5
Recognize cross-madhhab difference
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) do not require public permission; they consider Jumu'ah valid as long as it is performed in congregation, even in a private space.
This condition is specific to Hanafi mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) الخامس من شروط صحة الجمعة الإذن) (العام) كذا في الكنز لأنها من شعائر الإسلام، وخصائص الدين فلزم إقامتها على سبيل الاشتهار والعموم حتى لو غلق الإمام باب قصره أو المحل الذي يصلي فيه بأصحابه لم يجز وإن أذن للناس بالدخول فيه صحت ولكن لم يقض حق المسجد الجامع فيكره ولم يذكر في الهداية هذا الشرط لأنه غير مذكور في ظاهر الرواية، وإنما هو رواية النوادر قلت اطلعت على رسالة للعلامة ابن الشحنة
(And) the fifth condition for the validity of Jumu'ah is general permission, as in al-Kanz, because it is among the symbols of Islam and specificities of the religion, so it must be performed in a way that is public and common. So much so that if the imam closes the door of his palace or the place where he prays with his companions, it is not permissible. And if he permits the people to enter, it is valid, but he has not fulfilled the right of the congregational mosque, and it is disliked. Al-Hidayah did not mention this condition because it is not mentioned in the zahir al-riwayah; rather it is a narration of the Nawadir. I said: I have seen a treatise by the scholar Ibn al-Shahna.
Source pages p. 510

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement about the fifth condition of Jumu'ah according to the hadith work al-Kanz: general public permission (idhn al-'amm). Jumu'ah is a public symbol of Islam and must be performed openly. If the imam closes the doors and prays only with his group, the Jumu'ah is invalid because it is not public. However, if he opens the doors and permits entry, even if no one enters, it is valid. But if there is a designated congregational mosque, closing its doors is makruh (disliked). The commentator notes that this condition is not mentioned in al-Hidayah because it is not from the zahir al-riwayah (the six core books of Imam Muhammad) but from the Nawadir (rare transmissions). The commentator also references a treatise by the Hanafi scholar Ibn al-Shahna on this topic.

Key Terms
الإذن العام (al-idhn al-'amm): General public permission, meaning that Jumu'ah must be held in a place accessible to the public, not behind closed doors.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did al-Hidayah not mention the condition of general permission for Jumu'ah?
A) Because it is not a valid condition.
B) Because it is from the Nawadir, not the zahir al-riwayah.
C) Because al-Hidayah only covers optional prayers.
D) Because the author forgot.

Key Takeaway
General public permission is a valid condition for Jumu'ah in the Hanafi school, upheld from the Nawadir, despite not being in the six core books.

Conditions for the Friday Sermon and General Permission
Explaining the five conditions of the Friday sermon and the condition of general permission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five conditions of the Friday sermon according to the Hanafi school and distinguish the relied-upon view regarding the minimum number of attendees. You will also be able to explain the condition of general permission and evaluate its application in a modern context.

Core Idea
The Friday sermon requires five conditions; the relied-upon view mandates at least one attendee, and general permission is a Nawadir-based condition.

This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya clarifies the conditions for the validity of the Friday sermon and then addresses the controversial condition of general permission (idhn 'aam). The author resolves an intra-Hanafi dispute about the minimum number of attendees and critiques a fatwa regarding Friday prayer in a locked citadel. Understanding these conditions is essential for ensuring the validity of the Friday prayer in various scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions of the Friday sermon
The text lists five or six conditions. List them: the sermon must be before the prayer, with intention, within the time, with at least one attendee (in the relied-upon view), and no separating act. Some add a sixth: that the separating act be physically interrupting.
Note that the condition of ‘being in Arabic’ is assumed but not mentioned here.
2
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on the minimum number of attendees
Two narrations: one from Abu Hanifa and his two companions allows zero attendees; the other requires at least one. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is the second, requiring one attendee.
This is an example of tarjih within the madhhab.
3
Understand the condition of general permission
This condition is from the Nawadir, not Zahir al-Riwayah. It requires that Friday prayer be public and not exclusive. If the imam locks the mosque to the public, the prayer is invalid. Allowing entry makes it valid but disliked if the right of the congregational mosque is not fulfilled.
Al-Hidayah did not mention this condition because it is not in Zahir al-Riwayah.
4
Apply the reasoning to the Citadel of Cairo case
Al-Tahtawi argues that the reason for invalidity (exclusivity) is absent because other mosques exist, so Friday in the citadel is valid even if locked.
This is a critical refinement of the condition, showing its contextual application.
5
Evaluate practical implications
Consider modern cases where a congregation might be restricted (e.g., workplace prayers). Determine validity based on the condition of general permission: if the public is prevented from attending freely, the prayer is invalid unless alternative mosques are available.
The presence of alternative venues can lift the harm of exclusivity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يشترط سماع جماعة فتصح الخطبة (ولو) كان الحاضر (واحداً) وروي عن الإمام وصاحبيه صحتها وإن لم يحضره أحد و (في) الرواية الثانية عنهم يشترط حضور واحد في (الصحيح) ويشترط أن لا يفصل بين الخطبة والصلاة بأكل وعمل قاطع، واختلف في صحتها لو ذهب لمنزله لغسل، أو وضوء فهذه خمس شروط، أو ست لصحة الخطبة فليتنبه لها (و) الخامس من شروط صحة الجمعة الإذن) (العام) كذا في الكنز لأنها من شعائر الإسلام، وخصائص الدين فلزم إقامتها على سبيل الاشتهار والعموم حتى لو غلق الإمام باب قصره أو المحل الذي يصلي فيه بأصحابه لم يجز وإن أذن للناس بالدخول فيه صحت ولكن لم يقض حق المسجد الجامع فيكره ولم يذكر في الهداية هذا الشرط لأنه غير مذكور في ظاهر الرواية، وإنما هو رواية النوادر قلت اطلعت على رسالة للعلامة ابن الشحنة وقد قال فيها بعدم صحة الجمعة في قلعة القاهرة لأنها تقفل وقت صلاة الجمعة، وليست صراً على حدتها، وأقول في المنع نظر ظاهر لأنّ وجه القول بعدم صحة صلاة الإمام بقفله قصره اختصاصه بها دون العامة والعلة مفقودة في هذه القضية فإن القلعة، وإن قفلت لم يختص الحاكم فيها بالجمعة لأنّ عند باب القلعة عدة جوامع في كل منها خطبة لا يفوت من منع من دخول القلعة الجمعة، بل لو بقيت القلعة مفتوحة لا يرغب في طلوعها للجمعة لوجودها فيما هو أسهل من التكلف بالصعود لها، وفي كل محلة . من المصر عدة من الخطب فلا وجه لمنع صحة الجمعة بالقلعة عند قفلها
And it is not a condition that a group hears [the sermon]; thus the sermon is valid even if the attendee is one person. And it is narrated from the Imam and his two companions that it is valid even if no one attends. In the second narration from them, the presence of one is required [in the correct view]. And it is required that there be no separation between the sermon and the prayer by eating or an interrupting action. And there is disagreement about its validity if he went to his house for ghusl or wudu. So these are five or six conditions for the validity of the sermon, so be mindful of them. And the fifth condition for the validity of Friday prayer is general permission. Thus in al-Kanz, because it is from the symbols of Islam and distinctive features of the religion, so it must be performed in a public and widespread manner, such that if the imam locks the door of his castle or the place in which he prays with his companions, it is not valid. But if he permits people to enter, it is valid, but the right of the Friday mosque is not fulfilled, so it is disliked. Al-Hidayah did not mention this condition because it is not mentioned in the apparent narration; it is only a narration from the Nawadir. I said: I came across a treatise by the scholar Ibn al-Shihnah, who said in it the invalidity of Friday prayer in the Citadel of Cairo because it is locked at the time of Friday prayer, and it is not a separate city. And I say: the prohibition is apparently problematic, because the basis of the ruling of invalidity when the imam locks his castle is his exclusivity with it excluding the public, and this reason is absent in this case. For the citadel, although locked, the ruler does not have exclusive Friday prayer, because at the gate of the citadel there are several congregational mosques each with a sermon; no one prevented from entering the citadel misses Friday prayer. Rather, if the citadel remained open, no one would desire to ascend it for Friday prayer due to easier alternatives, and in every district of the city there are several sermons, so there is no basis for preventing the validity of Friday prayer in the citadel when it is locked.
Source pages p. 510

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya discusses the conditions for the validity of the Friday sermon (khutba) and the condition of general permission (idhn 'aam) for Friday prayer. The author, al-Tahtawi, begins by stating that it is not a condition for the sermon to be heard by a group; it is valid even if only one person is present. However, there is a known narration from Imam Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani that it is valid even if no one attends, while another narration requires the presence of one person. The relied-upon view, as stated in al-Diraya and al-Muntaqa, is that one person is required. Then conditions are listed: the sermon must be before the prayer, with the intention of delivering a sermon, within the time of Friday, with at least one attendee (who is among those for whom Friday is obligatory), and no separation by an interrupting act like eating or sexual intercourse followed by ghusl. Some add a sixth: that the separating act be physically interrupting (qaati'). Then the author moves to the fifth condition for the validity of Friday prayer itself: general permission from the ruler (or his deputy), because Friday is a public symbol of Islam. This condition is not from the Zahir al-Riwayah but is a narration from the Nawadir. The text discusses an example: if the imam locks his mosque or castle to the public, Friday is not valid. But if he allows entry, it is valid though disliked if the mosque's right of being a jamig (congregational mosque) is not fulfilled. The commentator then discusses a fatwa about the Citadel of Cairo by Ibn al-Shihnah, who deemed Friday invalid there because it was locked during prayer. Al-Tahtawi argues that the reason for invalidity (exclusivity) is absent, as there are other mosques outside the citadel, so locking does not prevent general attendance. Therefore, Friday in the citadel should be valid.

Key Terms
الخطبة (al-khutbah): The sermon delivered before Friday prayer, consisting of praise, admonition, and supplication.
الإذن العام (al-idhn al-'aam): General permission from the ruler or his deputy allowing public attendance at Friday prayer.
الجمعة (al-jumu'ah): The Friday congregational prayer that replaces the noon prayer and is obligatory on every free, adult, resident Muslim male.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani; constitutes the primary transmitted corpus of the Hanafi school.
النوادر (al-nawadir): Rare or less-transmitted narrations from Abu Hanifa and his companions, often used for fatwa in specific circumstances.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view in the text, what is the minimum number of attendees required for the Friday sermon?
A) None
B) One
C) Two
D) Three

Key Takeaway
The Friday sermon has five conditions, including at least one attendee (relied-upon view), and the condition of general permission from Nawadir requires that Friday prayer be public, not exclusive.

Minimum Congregation for Friday Prayer: Hanafi Dispute
Resolving minimum congregation for Friday within Hanafi school

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three positions within the Hanafi school regarding the minimum congregation for Friday prayer and apply the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view.

Core Idea
Friday prayer requires three men besides the imam; Abu Yusuf permitted two.

The validity of Friday prayer hinges on the presence of a congregation. While all scholars agree that an individual cannot perform Jumu'ah alone, they differ on the minimum number. Within the Hanafi school, Imams Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani require three men besides the imam, while Abu Yusuf holds that two suffice. This lesson examines the evidence and practical consequence of this internal dispute.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: three men besides the imam are required for Friday prayer to be valid.
This is the position of the majority of the school.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognise that Abu Yusuf (a leading Hanafi jurist) holds a different view: two men besides the imam suffice.
Abu Yusuf's view is also transmitted within the school.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand Abu Yusuf's evidence: the dual form (muthanna) in Arabic conveys the meaning of social gathering (ijtima'), so two plus the imam achieve the purpose.
He relies on linguistic usage.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad argue that true plurality (jam' sahih) is only three, and the word 'jumu'ah' derives from jam' (collection), implying a multitude.
They prioritise the literal minimum for plural.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Consider a town with only two eligible men besides the imam. Under Abu Yusuf, Friday is valid; under Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, it is not, and they must pray Zuhr instead.
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the majority view of three, due to its strength in Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) السادس ( الجماعة) لأن الجمعة مشتقة منها ولأن العلماء أجمعوا على أنها لا تصح من المنفرد (و) اختلفوا في الجماعة وعندنا هم ثلاثة رجال وإن لم يحضروا الخطبة وقد جاؤا فانصرف من شهدها وصلى بهم الإمام جاز من غير إعادة الخطبة في ظاهر الرواية وهم (غير الإمام) عند الإمام الأعظم ومحمد وقال أبو يوسف إثنان سوى الإمام لما في المثنى من معنى الاجتماع ولهما أن الجمع الصحيح إنما هو الثلاثة ( ولو كانوا عبيداً ، أو مسافرين أو مرضى) أو مختلطين
And the sixth [condition] is congregation, because Friday prayer is derived from it and because the scholars are unanimous that it is not valid from an individual. And they differed concerning the congregation. According to us, they are three men even if they did not attend the sermon; if they come and those who witnessed the sermon leave and the imam prays with them, it is permissible without repeating the sermon in the apparent narration. And they are besides the Imam according to the greatest Imam and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: two besides the imam, because in the dual there is meaning of congregation. And for them [the two imams] is that true plurality is only three. [It is valid] even if they are slaves, travelers, or sick, or mixed.
Source pages p. 511

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya addresses the sixth condition for the validity of Friday prayer: the presence of a congregation (jama'ah). The author notes that Friday prayer is derived from 'congregation' and that there is scholarly consensus (ijma') that it cannot be performed by an individual alone. However, the minimum number required is disputed within the Hanafi school. Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that three men besides the imam are necessary, because true plurality (al-jam' al-sahih) is only found in three. Abu Yusuf argues that two besides the imam suffice, as the dual (al-muthanna) also conveys the meaning of social gathering. The text notes that in the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah), the Friday prayer is valid even if those attending did not hear the sermon, provided three come later and the imam leads them. The congregation may include slaves, travelers, or sick persons, as long as they are male and meet the conditions for Friday obligation. The dispute is practical: a community with only two men besides the imam would be valid according to Abu Yusuf but invalid according to the other two imams.

Key Terms
الجماعة (al-jama'ah): A group of Muslims praying together; for Friday, a minimum number is required.
المنفرد (al-munfarid): A person praying alone, which is not valid for Friday prayer by consensus.
الجمع الصحيح (al-jam' al-sahih): True plurality, defined by Hanafis as three or more.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi), what is the minimum number of men besides the imam required for Friday prayer?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Four

Key Takeaway
Friday prayer requires a congregation of at least three men besides the imam according to the relied-upon Hanafi view, and if fewer are present, the prayer is invalid and must be performed as Zuhr.

Friday Prayer in a Locked Fortress: The ʿIllah of Exclusivity
Commentary refuting invalidation of Friday prayer in a locked fortress

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of ʿillah analysis to determine the validity of Friday prayer in a restricted-access location.

Core Idea
A locked gate does not invalidate Friday prayer if the general public is not excluded.

This lesson examines a critical refinement by Al-Tahtawi regarding Friday prayer in a locked fortress. The commentator refutes the view that the prayer is invalid, arguing that the underlying cause (ʿillah) for invalidation—exclusivity to the ruler—is absent due to accessible mosques outside.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Contested Ruling
State the view that Friday prayer is invalid in a locked fortress and the commentator's disagreement.
The original ruling claimed the prayer is invalid because the fortress is locked and not a full city.
2
Locate the Proposed ʿIllah
Find the effective cause (ʿillah) used to justify invalidation: exclusivity to the ruler.
The ʿillah is that locking the gate restricts the prayer to the ruler alone.
3
Test the ʿIllah Against the Facts
Check if the ʿillah is present in the fortress case. Note that there are multiple mosques just outside the gate.
Since people can pray outside, exclusivity does not hold.
4
Apply the Correct Condition: Idhn ʿĀmm
Recognize that the real condition for validity is general permission (idhn ʿāmm) from the ruler, not the absence of a lock.
The ruler gives general permission; locking is for security, not to exclude.
5
Conclude the Muftā Bihī Ruling
State the relied-upon Hanafi position: Friday prayer in a locked fortress is valid.
This is based on istiḥsān and later fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد قال فيها بعدم صحة الجمعة في قلعة القاهرة لأنها تقفل وقت صلاة الجمعة، وليست مصراً على حدتها، وأقول في المنع نظر ظاهر لأنّ وجه القول بعدم صحة صلاة الإمام بقفله قصره اختصاصه بها دون العامة والعلة مفقودة في هذه القضية فإن القلعة، وإن قفلت لم يختص الحاكم فيها بالجمعة لأنّ عند باب القلعة عدة جوامع في كل منها خطبة لا يفوت من منع من دخول القلعة الجمعة، بل لو بقيت القلعة مفتوحة لا يرغب في طلوعها للجمعة لوجودها فيما هو أسهل من التكلف بالصعود لها، وفي كل محلة من المصر عدة من الخطب فلا وجه لمنع صحة الجمعة بالقلعة عند قفلها. قوله: (في قلعة القاهرة أي ونحوها قوله وليست مصراً على حدتها فإنه وإن كان فيها الجوانيت، والسكك، وغير ذلك إلا أنها لم تستوف جميع ما ذكر في حد المصر من القاضي، ونحوه قوله: (في المنع) أي منع صحة الجمعة. قوله: (اختصاصه بها دون العامة) فيه نظر فإن الناس لو أغلقوا باب مسجد وصلوها لا تجوز لهم فالعلة الأذن، ولذا قال في مجمع الأنهر نافلاً عن عيون المذاهب، ولا يضر غلق باب القلعة لعدو، أو عادة قديمة لأن الإذن العام حاصل لأهله وغلق الباب ليس لمنع المصلي، ولكن عدم غلقه أحسن قوله: (لم يختص الحاكم الخ) هو يقول بعدم الصحة، وإن كان الحاكم يجمع خارجها، وما ذاك إلا لعدم الإذن العام لا للإختصاص فتدبر. قوله: (لأن عند باب القلعة) أي خارجه. قوله: (لا يفوت من منع الخ) هي لا منع فيها قبل غلقها، وإنما تغلق للعادة. قوله: (فيما هو أسهل من التكلف) الأوضح أن يقول فيما هو أسهل منها للتكلف بالصعود إليها. قوله: (وفي كل محلة الخ) أي فلا اختصاص بها لمن بالقلعة
And it has been said therein that Friday prayer is not valid in the fortress of Cairo because it is locked at the time of Friday prayer, and it is not a city (misr) by itself. I say: there is apparent consideration in prohibiting it, because the basis for saying that the imam's prayer is invalid due to its locking is his exclusivity to it without the general public, and this cause is absent in this case. For the fortress, even if locked, the ruler does not have exclusivity in it for Friday prayer, because at the gate of the fortress there are several congregational mosques, in each of which there is a sermon; the one who is prevented from entering the fortress does not miss Friday prayer. Rather, even if the fortress remained open, one would not desire to ascend to it for Friday prayer due to the existence of what is easier than the trouble of climbing up to it. And in every locality of the city there are several sermons, so there is no basis for prohibiting the validity of Friday prayer in the fortress when it is locked.
Source pages p. 511

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement from Al-Tahtawi's Hashiyah on the Maraqi al-Falah. It addresses the issue of the validity of Friday prayer in a fortress (such as the Cairo citadel) when its gates are locked during prayer time. The text first quotes a previous ruling that Friday prayer is invalid in such a situation because the fortress is not a full-fledged city and because locking the gates prevent general access. The commentator, however, argues against this prohibition. He explains that the underlying cause (ʿillah) for invalidation, according to some scholars, is that locking the gates would restrict the prayer exclusively to the ruler. But in the case of the Cairo fortress, this cause is absent because there are many congregational mosques right outside the gate, so no one is deprived of the Friday prayer—they can simply pray outside. Therefore, the prayer inside the fortress remains valid even when locked. The commentary then elaborates on each word of the original text, clarifying that the real condition is general permission (idhn ʿamm), not exclusivity, and that a longstanding custom of locking does not invalidate. The overall Hanafi position is that the prayer is valid, and it is based on istiḥsān (juristic preference) considering the ease for people, especially the ruler and officials inside.

Key Terms
قلعة (qal'a): A fortress or citadel, specifically the Cairo citadel.
إذن عام (idhn ʿamm): General permission for all to attend the prayer, a key condition for validity.
علة (illah): The effective cause behind the ruling; here, exclusivity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Al-Tahtawi's commentary, why is Friday prayer valid in the Cairo fortress when its gates are locked?
A) Because the fortress is a full city (misr).
B) Because the ruler allows it.
C) Because there are other mosques outside, so no one is deprived.
D) Because the lock is only for security, not to exclude worshippers.

Key Takeaway
A Friday prayer in a locked venue is valid if the general public can attend another Friday prayer elsewhere; the ʿillah is exclusivity, not the lock.

The Minimum Number for Friday Congregation: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the minimum number for Friday congregation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the minimum congregation for Friday prayer, explain the linguistic proof used, and identify the practical consequence of the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Friday prayer requires a true plural — three men besides the imam; the dual does not suffice.

Friday prayer (salat al-jumu'ah) is a weekly obligation that requires congregation. But what is the minimum number that constitutes a valid congregation? Within the Hanafi school, there is a well-known difference between the two senior students: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani require three men besides the imam, while Abu Yusuf accepts two. This lesson unpacks the linguistic and legal reasoning behind each position and identifies the mufta bihi (relied-upon) ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Friday prayer is the act under discussion. Congregation (jama'ah) is a condition (shart) for its validity. Without a valid congregation, the prayer is not accepted.
Congregation is not just recommended; it is a necessary condition for Friday prayer.
2
State the Hanafi positions
Within the Hanafi school, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad require three men besides the imam. Abu Yusuf holds that two men besides the imam suffice.
All three imams agree that the imam himself is not counted in the minimum; they differ on the number of followers.
3
Examine the proof (dalil) for each
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad argue linguistically: the word 'jumu'ah' is derived from 'jam'' (gathering), which implies a plural of three or more. Also, the Quranic command 'fa-s'aw ila dhikrillah' uses a plural verb form (waw al-jama'ah), indicating at least three. Abu Yusuf argues that the dual (ithnan) also conveys the meaning of social gathering.
The verb 'fa-s'aw' is imperative addressed to a group, and in Arabic the plural form (waw) is used for three or more.
4
Determine the Hanafi response
The majority response is that the dual is not a true plural (jama' sahih) in Arabic. The grammatical rule is that the plural is specific to three or more, and the dual has its own form. Therefore, the minimum for a valid 'gathering' linguistically is three.
This is a usul al-fiqh principle: the true collective is three; the dual is a different category.
5
Extract the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if only two men (besides the imam) are present, according to Abu Hanifa the Friday prayer is invalid and must be prayed as Zuhr, while according to Abu Yusuf it is valid. The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position is three men besides the imam.
In fatwa, the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is adopted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) السادس ( الجماعة) لأن الجمعة مشتقة منها ولأن العلماء أجمعوا على أنها لا تصح من المنفرد (و) اختلفوا في الجماعة وعندنا هم ثلاثة رجال وإن لم يحضروا الخطبة وقد جاؤا فانصرف من شهدها وصلى بهم الإمام جاز من غير إعادة الخطبة في ظاهر الرواية وهم (غير الإمام) عند الإمام الأعظم ومحمد وقال أبو يوسف إثنان سوى الإمام لما في المثنى من معنى الاجتماع ولهما أن الجمع الصحيح إنما هو الثلاثة ( ولو كانوا عبيداً ، أو مسافرين أو مرضى) أو مختلطين. قوله: (لأن الجمعة مشتقة منها) أي مأخوذة، فإنّ من المصادر أي والأصل مراعاة المعاني اللغوية إذا لم يتحقق نقل. قوله: (فانصرف من شهدها قد تقدم قول أنه لا يشترط حضور أحد لسماعها، وصحح. قوله: (ولهما أن الجمع الصحيح إنما هو الثلاثة وأيضاً طلب الحضور في قوله عز وجل: (فاسعوا إلى ذكر الله ) [الجمعة / ٦٢] متعلق بلفظ الجمع، وهو الواو، والذكر المسند إليه السعي يستلزم ذاكراً وهو غير الجمع المطلوب حضوره، فلزم أن يكون مع الإمام جمع وما دون الثلاثة ليس جمعاً متفقاً عليه فليس بجمع مطلق، والمشروط هنا ظناً . مطلق، وبيان ما ذكره المصنف أن أقل الجمع ثلاثة حقيقة لمخالفة صيغته الدالة عليه صيغة التثنية والواحد، والإثنان وإن كان جمعاً من وجه نظراً إلى الاشتقاق فهو مجاز والعمل بالحقيقة هو الأصل
And the sixth [condition] is congregation, because Friday prayer is derived from it, and because the scholars have unanimously agreed that it is not valid for an individual. And they differed regarding the congregation. According to us, they are three men, even if they did not attend the sermon. If they come and those who witnessed it leave, and the imam prays with them, it is permissible without repeating the sermon according to the apparent transmission. They are besides the imam according to the Greatest Imam and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: Two besides the imam, because in the dual there is a meaning of social gathering. And for them [Abu Hanifa and Muhammad], the true collective is only three. (And if they are slaves, travelers, or sick) or mixed.
Source pages p. 511

Commentary
This passage is a expansion probe from Al-Tahtawi's commentary on Maraqi al-Falah, explaining the condition of congregation (jamaʿah) for Friday prayer. It clarifies that Friday prayer is not valid without a congregation, the minimum of which is three men besides the imam according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Abu Yusuf holds that two men besides the imam suffice, citing the dual form implying social gathering. The commentator then discusses the derivation of the word 'Jumuʿah' from 'jamaʿ' (gathering) and argues that the true collective (jamaʿ sahih) is three, as anything less is considered dual or singular. He also mentions that these three can be slaves, travelers, or sick, as long as they are capable of following the imam. The commentary also addresses that the congregation need not have heard the sermon; they can join after the sermon if they leave and return for prayer. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: three men besides the imam.

Key Terms
جماعة (jamaʿah): The minimum number of people required for Friday prayer congregation.
مثنى (muthanna): Dual form in Arabic grammar.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi requires at least three men besides the imam for a valid Friday congregation, based on the linguistic meaning of jama'ah and the plural form in the Quranic command.

The Validity of Slaves, Travelers, and the Sick in the Friday Congregation
Ruling on the permissibility of slaves and others as part of the Friday congregation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the permissibility of slaves, travelers, and sick individuals forming part of the Friday congregation and identify the underlying legal principle (al-aqli).

Core Idea
Slaves, travelers, and the sick may validly form the Friday congregation because they are fit to lead prayer.

This lesson examines a concise ruling in the Hanafi school regarding who can constitute the congregation for Jumu'ah prayer. While these individuals may not be obligated to attend, their presence is sufficient to complete the required number. The reasoning is based on a legal analogy: those competent to lead are even more competent to follow.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories
Note the three categories explicitly mentioned: slaves (عبيد), travelers (مسافرين), and sick individuals (مرضى), as well as mixed groups (مختلطين).
These are individuals who may be exempt from the obligation of Jumu'ah in some cases.
2
State the ruling
The text rules that these individuals are valid as part of the Friday congregation. Their presence fulfills the condition of the required number (e.g., three persons besides the imam in the Hanafi school).
The ruling is that their iqtida' (following) is valid.
3
Understand the legal reasoning
The proof is a 'first principle' (awla) argument: since these individuals are fit to lead the prayer (imamah), they are even more fit to follow (iqtida'). Leadership requires greater qualifications, so competent leaders are clearly competent followers.
This is a form of qiyas awlawi (a fortiori analogy).
4
Distinguish obligation vs. validity
Note that the exemption from the obligation of Jumu'ah does not disqualify one from being part of the congregation. The ruling separates the personal obligation from the validity of the congregational act.
For example, a slave is not obligated to attend Jumu'ah, but if he does attend and prays behind the imam, his prayer counts for the congregation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
( ولو كانوا عبيداً ، أو مسافرين أو مرضى) أو مختلطين لأنهم صلحوا للإمامة، فأولى أن يصلحوا للإقتداء
And even if they were slaves, travelers, or sick, or mixed, because they are fit for leadership, so it is more appropriate that they be fit for following.
Source pages p. 511

Commentary
This passage states that the individuals who form the congregation for Friday prayer can be slaves, travelers, sick persons, or a mixture of these categories. The reason given is that such individuals are themselves eligible to lead the prayer (imamah), so they are certainly eligible to follow an imam (iqtida'). The Hanafi school does not require that all attendees be free, resident, or healthy, as long as they are valid followers. The obligation of Friday prayer may be reduced for slaves, travelers, and the sick (it is not fard 'ayn upon them), but they can complete the congregation for others.

Key Terms
إقتداء (iqtida'): Following the imam in prayer.
إمامة (imamah): Leading the prayer.
أولى (awla): More appropriate; a fortiori reasoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why are slaves, travelers, and sick individuals considered valid followers in the Friday congregation?
A) Because they are obligated to attend Friday prayer.
B) Because they are fit to lead prayer.
C) Because they are free and resident.
D) Because the imam permits them.

Key Takeaway
Slaves, travelers, and sick individuals are valid members of the Friday congregation because they are fit to lead; their exemption from the obligation does not disqualify them from being followers.

Condition of Congregation for Friday Prayer: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the condition of congregation for Friday prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the three Hanafi positions on the duration of congregation required for Friday prayer and identify the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
For Friday prayer, congregation is required at the start; continuation after first prostration is not required by the relied-upon view.

This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya clarifies a subtle but important intra-Hanafi dispute about Friday prayer. The key question is: must the congregation remain with the imam throughout the prayer, or is it sufficient that they were present at the beginning? The answer affects the validity of the prayer if followers leave early.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
List the views of Abu Hanifa, the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), and Zufar regarding the condition of congregation for Friday prayer.
Abu Hanifa: congregation must stay until first prostration. Sahibayn: only at commencement. Zufar: entire prayer.
2
Understand the key distinction
Explain the difference between 'inʿiqād al-adāʾ' (validity of performance) and 'inʿiqād al-taḥrīmah' (validity of commencement). Abu Hanifa conditions the former; the Sahibayn condition the latter.
Performance (adāʾ) includes the first prostration; commencement (taḥrīmah) is just the initial takbir.
3
Apply to a scenario
Consider a situation where followers leave before the first prostration. Determine the ruling according to each view.
Abu Hanifa: invalid. Sahibayn: valid, imam completes alone. Zufar: invalid.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
State which position is relied upon for fatwa and why (practicality, ease).
The Sahibayn's view is mufta bihi.
5
Note the agreed case
Recognize that all three imams agree that if followers leave after the first prostration, the imam completes the prayer alone as Friday prayer.
This is the point of agreement mentioned in the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والشرط عند الإمام لانعقاد أدائها بهم بقاؤهم محرمين مع الإمام ولو كان اقتداؤهم في حال ركوعه قبل رفع رأسه حتى يسجد السجدة الأولى فان نفروا أي أفسدوا صلاتهم بعد سجوده أي الإمام أتمها وحده جمعة باتفاق أئمتنا الثلاثة وقال زفر يشترط دوامهم كالوقت إلى تمامها وإن نفروا أو بعضهم ولم يبق سوى إثنان من الرجال إذ لا عبرة بالنساء والصبيان الباقين قبل سجوده أي الإمام بطلت عند أبي حنيفة لأنه يقول الجماعة شرط انعقاد الأداء وعندهما يتمها وحده لأن الجماعة شرط انعقاد التحريمة
And the condition according to the Imam [Abu Hanifa] for the validity of its performance with them is that they remain in the state of ihram with the imam, even if their following occurred during his bowing before he raises his head, until he prostrates the first prostration. If they break away (i.e., invalidate their prayer) after his prostration, he completes it alone as Friday prayer by agreement of our three imams. Zufar said: their continuance is required like the time until its completion. And if they break away, or some of them, and only two men remain—since women and boys are not counted—before his prostration, it is invalid according to Abu Hanifa because he says congregation is a condition for the validity of the performance (adāʾ). According to them [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], he completes it alone because congregation is a condition for the validity of the commencement (taḥrīmah).
Source pages p. 512

Commentary
This passage discusses the condition that the congregation must remain with the imam until the first prostration (sajdah ūlā) for the Friday prayer to be validly performed according to Abu Hanifa. The reasoning is that the performance (adāʾ) of the prayer is only complete with the first prostration. If all followers break away after the imam's prostration, the imam can complete the prayer alone as a valid Friday prayer, and this is agreed upon by Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad. However, Zufar holds that the followers must stay until the end of the prayer. If they break away before the prostration, leaving only two men (women and children not counted), Abu Hanifa says the Friday prayer is invalid because the condition for valid performance was not met. The two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that it is still valid because the condition for commencement (taḥrīmah) was met. According to them, the congregation is required only at the start. The mufta bihi is the view of the Sahibayn, as it is easier and more practical.

Key Terms
انعقاد الأداء (inʿiqād al-adāʾ): Validity of the performance of the prayer, tied to completing at least the first prostration.
انعقاد التحريمة (inʿiqād al-taḥrīmah): Validity of the commencement of prayer, i.e., the initial takbir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view (Sahibayn), if the entire congregation leaves the Friday prayer before the imam's first prostration, what happens?
A) The Friday prayer is invalid.
B) The imam completes it alone as a valid Friday prayer.
C) The imam must stop and repeat the prayer.
D) The prayer becomes a regular zuhr prayer.

Key Takeaway
For Friday prayer, the relied-upon Hanafi view is that the congregation condition is fulfilled at the commencement, so the imam can complete the prayer alone if followers leave early.

Definition of a City (Misr) for Friday Prayer
Definition ruling on what constitutes a city for Friday prayer validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of misr for Friday prayer and identify the three required officials.

Core Idea
Friday prayer is only valid in a city with a resident mufti, amir, and judge.

Friday prayer has specific conditions, one of which is that it must be held in a city (misr). This lesson presents Abu Hanifa's definition of what constitutes a misr: a place with three key officials residing there. Understanding this definition is essential for determining where Friday prayer is valid.

Guided Path
1
Recognize misr as a condition
Realize that the validity of Friday prayer depends on the location being a misr. This is a shart (condition) for the prayer to be obligatory and valid.
Other schools have different criteria; here we focus on the Hanafi view.
2
Identify the three officials
Memorize the three required officials: a mufti (jurisconsult), an amir (governor who enforces justice), and a judge (qadi) who executes rulings and hudud punishments.
All three must be residents; visiting officials do not suffice.
3
Apply the definition
When evaluating a location, check whether it has these three officials residing. If any is missing, the place is not a misr and Friday prayer is not valid there.
This definition is strict; later Hanafis debated extensions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمصر عند أبي حنيفة كل موضع أي بلد له مفتي يرجع إليه في الحوادث وأمير ينصف المظلوم من الظالم وقاضي ينفذ الأحكام ويقيم الحدود مقيمون بها
And the city (misr) according to Abu Hanifa is every place, i.e., town, which has a mufti to whom reference is made in events, and an amir who does justice to the oppressed from the oppressor, and a judge who executes judgments and establishes the hudud, who are residents in it.
Source pages p. 512

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'misr' (city/town) as a requirement for Friday prayer. According to Abu Hanifa, a place qualifies as a misr if it has three officials: a mufti (jurist who issues fatwas), an amir (governor/leader who enforces justice), and a judge (qadi) who implements legal rulings and carries out hudud punishments. All three must be residents of that place. This definition ensures that the congregation is established in a stable urban center with proper authority. The commentary notes that this is the view of Abu Hanifa and that Abu Yusuf also adopted it, and it is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) as it is the most practical. Other definitions (like size or market) are not considered because they do not apply to the original cities of Mecca and Medina.

Key Terms
مصر (misr): A city or town with specific administrative and religious officials.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) A sultan, a vizier, and a qadi.
D) A mufti and a judge only.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of misr for Friday prayer requires the residence of a mufti, an amir, and a judge.

Conditions of Congregation for Jumu'ah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on congregation timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the condition of congregation in Jumu'ah and identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
For Abu Hanifa, Jumu'ah requires congregation until the first sajdah; for the Sahibayn, only the initial takbir requires it.

This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya presents a key disagreement within the Hanafi school: Must the congregation remain throughout the Jumu'ah prayer or only at its start? The answer determines whether a Jumu'ah prayer is valid if followers leave early. Understanding this ikhtilaf is crucial for deriving the correct ruling in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the condition
The act under discussion is the Jumu'ah prayer. The condition in dispute is the presence of the congregation: when exactly must the followers be present for the prayer to be valid?
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that the congregation must remain in prayer with the imam until the first prostration (sajdah). If they leave before that, the Jumu'ah is invalid.
He considers the condition (shart) for the validity of performance (ada') to extend to the actual prayer acts.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the congregation is only required at the initial takbir (tahrimah). After that, if followers leave, the imam may complete the prayer alone, and it remains valid as Jumu'ah.
For them, the condition attaches to the commencement (in'iqad) of prayer, not its continuity.
4
Note Zufar's position
Zufar goes further: the congregation must remain throughout the entire prayer, similar to the time condition.
This is the most stringent view and is not adopted by the majority.
5
Determine the practical difference
The thamarah al-khilaf is whether a Jumu'ah prayer is valid if a follower leaves after the tahrimah but before the first sajdah. If valid, the imam continues alone; if invalid, the prayer must be repeated as Zuhr.
The text does not specify which view is mufta bihi; in later Hanafi practice, the Sahibayn's view often prevails.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والشرط عند الإمام) لانعقاد أدائها بهم (بقاؤهم) محرمين (مع الإمام) ولو كان اقتداؤهم في حال ركوعه قبل رفع رأسه (حتى يسجد السجدة الأولى فان) نفروا) أي أفسدوا صلاتهم (بعد سجوده) أي الإمام (أتمها وحده جمعة) باتفاق أئمتنا الثلاثة وقال زفر يشترط دوامهم كالوقت إلى تمامها (وإن نفروا) أو بعضهم ولم يبق سوى إثنان من الرجال إذ لا عبرة بالنساء والصبيان الباقين (قبل سجوده) أي الإمام (بطلت) عند أبي حنيفة لأنه يقول : الجماعة شرط انعقاد الأداء وعندهما يتمها وحده لأنّ الجماعة شرط انعقاد التحريمة (ولا تصح) أي لا تنعقد الجمعة (بامرأة أو رجلين) لعدم صلاحية الصبي والمرأة للإمامة (وجاز للعبد والمريض والمسافر أن يؤم فيها بالإذن أصالة أو نيابة صريحاً، أو دلالة كما تقدم لأهليتهم للإمامة وإنما سقط عنهم وجوبها تخفيفاً
And the condition according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) for the validity of its performance with them (the congregation) is their staying in the state of ihram with the imam, even if they followed him while he was bowing before raising his head, until he performs the first prostration. If they (i.e., they invalidate their prayer) after his (the imam's) prostration, (the imam) completes it alone as Jumu'ah, by agreement of our three imams. Zufar says: their continuity is required like the time until its completion. And if they or some of them leave, and only two men remain (since women and minors are not considered), before his (the imam's) prostration, (the Jumu'ah) is invalid according to Abu Hanifa because he says: the congregation is a condition for the validity of the performance. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he completes it alone because the congregation is a condition for the validity of the initial takbir (tahrimah). And (Jumu'ah) is not valid with a woman or two men, due to the lack of fitness of the minor and woman for imamah. And it is permissible for a slave, a sick person, and a traveler to lead in it with permission, originally or by proxy, explicitly or implicitly, as previously mentioned, due to their fitness for imamah; their obligation (of Jumu'ah) is only waived as a concession.
Source pages p. 512

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya of al-Tahtawi comments on the conditions for the validity of Jumu'ah prayer. It addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the requirement of the congregation remaining. The imam (Abu Hanifa) holds that the congregation must stay until the first sajdah for the Jumu'ah to be valid; if they leave before that, the prayer is invalid. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) disagree, stating that the congregation is only required for the initial takbir, so if they leave, the imam may complete it alone. Zufar goes further, requiring them to stay until the end. The passage also clarifies that women and minors do not count toward the required congregation, and that a slave, sick person, or traveler may lead Jumu'ah with permission.

Key Terms
التحريمة (al-tahrimah): The initial takbir that begins the prayer, making it sacred.
السجدة الأولى (al-sajdah al-ula): The first prostration in the prayer, used by Abu Hanifa as the cutoff for the congregation's requirement.
الأداء (al-ada'): Performance of the prayer, which Abu Hanifa ties to the actual prayer acts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, when does the congregation's presence become a condition for Jumu'ah validity?
A) Only at the initial takbir
B) Until the imam's first prostration
C) Throughout the entire prayer
D) Only for the khutbah

Key Takeaway
The condition of congregation in Jumu'ah is disputed within the Hanafi school: Abu Hanifa requires it until the first prostration, while the Sahibayn require it only at the initial takbir.

Defining the City for Jumu'ah (Hanafi Definition)
Defines the Hanafi conditions for a valid Jumu'ah city.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three functional conditions for a city (misr) according to Abu Hanifa, identify the physical requirement, and apply the definition to evaluate whether Jumu'ah is valid in a given locale.

Core Idea
A city for Jumu'ah requires a mufti, amir, and judge — not mere size or population.

In this passage, al-Tahtawi clarifies the Hanafi definition of a city (misr) sufficient for the Friday prayer. The definition is contested, but he presents the soundest view: a town must have three offices — mufti, amir, and judge — and its buildings must reach a certain size. He also addresses the special case of Mina during Hajj, where an intra-Hanafi dispute arises.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of the passage
The author is defining the legal concept of 'misr' for Jumu'ah. Note that the definition is contested among many opinions; he selects the soundest one.
2
Extract the three functional requirements
List the three offices: a mufti to issue fatwas, an amir to administer justice, and a judge to execute judgments and enforce hudud. These must reside in the town.
The judge must be capable of executing punishments, not just arbitration.
3
Note the physical requirement
The buildings of the town must reach the size of the buildings of Mina. This is from the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) and is the relied-upon view per Qadikhan.
This is a secondary condition; the primary are the three offices.
4
Examine the consolidation rule
If one person holds multiple roles (e.g., judge who is also mufti), it still suffices. The focus is on the function, not the number of individuals.
This emphasizes the importance of institutional capacity over headcount.
5
Analyze the Mina dispute
Jumu'ah at Mina during Hajj is valid for the caliph or amir of Hijaz according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, but Muhammad considers it a village, invalidating Jumu'ah. This shows how the definition applies in practice and generates ikhtilaf.
The dispute hinges on whether Mina becomes 'muttasir' (a city) during the season.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولما كان حد المصر مختلفاً فيه على أقوال كثيرة ذكر الأصح منها، فقال: (والمصر) عند أبي حنيفة كل موضع أي بلد (له مفتي يرجع إليه في الحوادث ( وأمير) ينصف المظلوم من الظالم (وقاضي) مقيمون بها وإنما قال: (ينفذ الأحكام ويقيم الحدود احترازاً عن المحكم والمرأة (و) الحال أنه موضع (بلغت أبنيته) قدر (أبنية منى) وهذا (في ظاهر الرواية قاله قاضيخان، وعليه الاعتماد (وإذا كان القاضي أو الأمير مفتياً أغني عن التعداد لأن المدار على معرفة الأحكام لا على كثرة الأشخاص وجازت الجمعة بمنى في الموسم للخليفة أو أمير الحجاز) لا أمير الموسم لأنه يلي أمر الحاج لا غير عند . أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف وقال محمد : لا يصح بها لأنها قرية وقالا تتمصر في الموسم
And since the definition of the city (misr) differs according to many opinions, he mentioned the soundest one, saying: (The city) according to Abu Hanifa is every place, i.e., a town, that has a mufti to whom one refers in incidents, and an amir who does justice to the oppressed from the oppressor, and a judge residing in it. And he said: (who executes judgments and establishes the hudud) as a precaution against the arbitrator and the woman. And (the condition is) that it is a place whose buildings have reached the size of the buildings of Mina. And this is in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah); Qadikhan said it, and upon it is reliance. And if the judge or amir is a mufti, he suffices for the count, because the reliance is on knowledge of rulings, not on the multiplicity of persons. And Jumu'ah is permitted at Mina during the season for the caliph or the amir of Hijaz, not the amir of the season (only). According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, Muhammad said it is not valid there because it is a village, but they said it becomes a city during the season.
Source pages p. 512

Commentary
This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya defines the conditions for a locale to be considered a city (misr) for the validity of Jumu'ah. According to Abu Hanifa, a city must have a mufti (for religious guidance), an amir (ruler) who establishes justice, and a judge who executes judgments and enforces hudud. These ensure the city's importance. Additionally, the buildings must reach the size of Mina's buildings (a specific measure). This is the relied-upon position from the apparent narration. If one person fills multiple roles (e.g., judge and mufti), it suffices. The passage also discusses Jumu'ah at Mina during Hajj: the caliph or amir of Hijaz may hold it, but not the mere amir of the season, according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf; Muhammad disagrees.

Key Terms
المصر (al-misr): A city large enough to hold Jumu'ah, with mufti, amir, and judge.
المفتي (al-mufti): A scholar qualified to issue legal opinions (fatwas).
الأمير (al-amir): A ruler or governor who administers justice and protects rights.
القاضي (al-qadi): A judge who executes judgments and enforces hudud.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The apparent or transmitted narration from the early Hanafi masters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT required for a place to be considered a city for Jumu'ah according to Abu Hanifa?
A) A mufti to issue fatwas
B) An amir to administer justice
C) A judge to implement punishments
D) A large mosque with minaret

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of a city for Jumu'ah requires three institutional roles (mufti, amir, judge) and a minimum physical size; reliance is on the apparent narration, and one person may fill multiple roles.

The Minimal Content of the Jumu'ah Khutbah
Explains the minimal sufficiency and recommended content of the Khutbah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimal content of the Jumu'ah khutbah that is valid (sahih) and explain why it is disliked (makruh tanzihi) according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A single word of dhikr suffices for khutbah but is disliked; the sunnah length is tashahhud.

The Jumu'ah khutbah is a wajib component of the Friday prayer. But what must be said? This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiyah clarifies the minimal sufficiency and the recommended length, showing that while a brief remembrance is legally valid, it falls short of the sunnah and is therefore disliked.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is restricting the khutbah to a brief remembrance. The ruling is that it is valid (sahih) but disliked (makruh tanzihi).
2
Locate the sunnah requirement
The sunnah is to give a longer khutbah; the Imam said a long mention called a khutbah is necessary, and its minimum is the length of the tashahhud including praise and salawat.
3
Understand the karahah
The dislike is due to abandoning the sunnah, not because the act is invalid. This is makruh tanzihi, not tahrimi.
4
Note the difference between validity and completeness
Valid but incomplete; the khutbah counts but one loses the sunnah reward.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصح الاقتصار في الخطبة على ذكر خالص الله تعالى (نحو تسبيحة أو تحميدة أو تهليلة أو تكبيرة لكن مع الكراهة لترك السنة عند الإمام، وقال : لا بد من ذكر طويل يسمى خطبة، وأقله قدر التشهد إلى قوله عبده ورسوله حمد وصلاة
And it is valid to restrict the khutbah to pure remembrance of Allah Almighty, such as a tasbih, tahmid, tahlil, or takbir, but with dislike (karahah) for abandoning the sunnah according to the Imam. And he said: A long mention called a khutbah is necessary, and its minimum is the amount of the tashahhud up to his saying 'His slave and messenger' – praise and prayers.
Source pages p. 513

Commentary
This passage discusses the minimal content of the Jumu'ah khutbah. According to the commentator (al-Tahtawi), it is valid to restrict the khutbah to a simple phrase glorifying Allah, such as 'SubhanAllah', 'Alhamdulillah', 'La ilaha illallah', or 'Allahu Akbar'. However, this is disliked (makruh tanzihan) because it abandons the sunnah of a longer sermon. The Imam (Abu Hanifa) required a longer speech that qualifies as a khutbah, the minimum of which is the length of the tashahhud up to 'ashhadu anna Muhammadan 'abduhu wa rasuluh', including praise and salawat.

Key Terms
الكراهة (al-karahah): Dislike (makruh tanzihi) for restricting khutbah to minimal, due to abandoning sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum length of the khutbah that avoids dislike according to the Imam?
A) One word of remembrance
B) The tashahhud up to 'His slave and messenger'
C) A full surah from the Quran
D) At least two sentences

Key Takeaway
A Jumu'ah khutbah is valid with any word of dhikr, but it is disliked to shorten it below the sunnah length of tashahhud.

Jumu'ah in Mina: The Condition of a Town (Misr)
Defines misr and applies to Mina during Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of misr for Jumu'ah and explain the relied-upon ruling for Jumu'ah in Mina during the Hajj season.

Core Idea
Mina becomes a town during Hajj; Jumu'ah is valid for the Caliph or Amir of Hijaz.

The validity of Friday prayer (Jumu'ah) depends on it being held in a proper town (misr). But what constitutes a town? This lesson examines the Hanafi definition and a key application: Jumu'ah in Mina during the Hajj season. The passage resolves an intra-madhhab dispute and establishes the operative ruling for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key condition for Jumu'ah
The text explains that a misr is required, defined functionally by the presence of an authority capable of executing hudud (Islamic penal punishments). This excludes smaller settlements like villages.
Note the use of 'hudud' as a criterion: the ability to enforce, not actual enforcement, is what matters.
2
Understand the dispute over Mina
Imam Muhammad argues Jumu'ah in Mina is invalid because it is normally a village (qaryah). Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf respond that Mina becomes a town (tatamassar) during the season due to the large gathering and presence of authority.
The opposing school is internal: Imam Muhammad vs. the two elder imams.
3
Identify the relied-upon position
The text states that the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf is relied upon (alayhi al-i'timad), with authority from Qadikhan and zahir al-riwayah.
Thus, the mufta bihi is that Jumu'ah in Mina during Hajj is valid for the Caliph or Amir of Hijaz.
4
Determine the practical scope
The ruling applies only during the Hajj season (mawsim) and only for the highest authorities (Caliph or Amir of Hijaz), not the regular amir of the pilgrimage.
Outside the season, Mina reverts to a village, so Jumu'ah would not be valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحدود احترازاً عن المحكم والمرأة وذكر الحدود يغني عن القصاص (و) الحال أنه موضع (بلغت أبنيته) قدر (أبنية منى) وهذا (في ظاهر الرواية قاله قاضيخان، وعليه الاعتماد (وإذا كان القاضي أو الأمير مفتياً أغني عن التعداد لأن المدار على معرفة الأحكام لا على كثرة الأشخاص وجازت الجمعة بمنى في الموسم للخليفة أو أمير الحجاز) لا أمير الموسم لأنه يلي أمر الحاج لا غير عند . أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف وقال محمد : لا يصح بها لأنها قرية وقالا تتمصر في الموسم
The hudud (penalties) as a restriction against the arbitrator and the woman, and mentioning the hudud suffices from the qisas. And (the situation) that it is a place (its buildings reached) the measure of (the buildings of Mina). And this (in zahir al-riwayah, Qadikhan said it, and upon it is reliance). (And if the judge or the amir is a mufti, it suffices from counting, because the criterion is knowledge of rulings, not the multitude of persons). And Jumu'ah is valid in Mina during the season for the Caliph or the Amir of Hijaz, not the Amir of the season, because he manages the affairs of the pilgrims only, according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. And Muhammad said: It is not valid there because it is a village, and they (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) said: It becomes a town (misr) during the season.
Source pages p. 513

Commentary
This passage is a legal commentary on the conditions for the validity of Jumu'ah, specifically focusing on the requirement that the congregation be held in a proper town (misr). The text begins by explaining that the phrase 'al-hudud' (penalties) is mentioned to exclude a hakam (arbitrator) and a woman, who can execute judgments but not establish hudud. The mention of hudud suffices and makes explicit mention of qisas unnecessary. It then discusses the case of Mina: scholars in zahir al-riwayah state that if a place's buildings reach the size of those in Mina, it qualifies as a misr. There is reliance on this view. Furthermore, if the judge or amir is himself a mufti, there is no need for a separate mufti, because the essential matter is knowledge of legal rulings, not the number of people. Jumu'ah is valid in Mina during the Hajj season for the Caliph or the Amir of Hijaz (the governor of Mecca), but not for the Amir of the season (the official in charge of pilgrims), because the latter only oversees the pilgrims. This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani disagrees, saying Jumu'ah is not valid in Mina because it is a village, not a permanent town. The rejoinder of the two imams is that even though Mina is normally a village, it effectively becomes a town during the Hajj season due to the large gathering. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Key Terms
المصر (al-misr): A town or settlement that has an authority capable of executing judgments and establishing hudud; it is a condition for the validity of Jumu'ah.
الحدود (al-hudud): Legally prescribed punishments (e.g., for theft, adultery) which only a qualified authority can execute.
الموسم (al-mawsim): The Hajj season, during which Mina temporarily functions as a misr.
التّمَصُّر (al-tamassur): The process of becoming a town (misr); used here to describe Mina's temporary transformation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, when is Jumu'ah valid in Mina?
A) Only during the Hajj season for the Caliph or Amir of Hijaz
B) Any time of the year if an amir is present
C) Only if it is a permanent settlement
D) Only for the Amir of the season

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah is valid in Mina during Hajj season because it becomes a temporary town (misr) with authority to enforce hudud, per the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Minimum Content of the Friday Sermon and Its Sunnahs
Determining the minimal requirement for the khutbah and listing its recommended practices

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimal requirement for a valid Friday khutbah according to the Hanafi school and distinguish it from the sunnah elements.

Core Idea
The Friday khutbah is valid with any dhikr of Allah, even one word, but a fuller sermon is the sunnah.

The Friday sermon (khutbah) is a wajib component of Jumu'ah, but what is the least that can be said? This lesson clarifies the bare minimum that makes the khutbah valid, the proofs for it, and the sunnah practices that elevate it. Understanding this prevents unnecessary invalidation of Jumu'ah and helps khateebs know their options.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the Friday khutbah. The ruling: it is valid (sahih) even if restricted to pure dhikr like tasbih, but disliked (makruh) for abandoning the sunnah.
Dislike is tanzihi, not tahrimi.
2
Locate the dalil for minimal validity
The proof is the Quranic verse 'Fas'aw ila dhikr Allah' (62:9) and the incident of Caliph Uthman who said only 'Alhamdulillah' and descended, with no Companion objecting (consensus).
The verse is general; the incident shows practical application.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The word 'dhikr' in the verse is general (amm), not specifying length or form. Therefore any dhikr, even minimal, fulfills the command and makes the khutbah valid.
The specific practice of a longer khutbah indicates sunnah, not obligation.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Hanifa insists on a lengthy discourse called 'khutbah' with minimum like tashahhud plus praise, salawat, and supplication. The two students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) agree with the minimal view.
This is a legitimate difference within the school.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the minimal view, because the Quranic evidence is stronger and the incident of Uthman shows practical consensus.
Hence a khateeb may deliver a very short khutbah, though it is better to follow the sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصح الاقتصار في الخطبة على ذكر خالص الله تعالى (نحو تسبيحة أو تحميدة أو تهليلة أو تكبيرة لكن مع الكراهة لترك السنة عند الإمام، وقال : لا بد من ذكر طويل يسمى خطبة، وأقله قدر التشهد إلى قوله عبده ورسوله حمد وصلاة ودعاء للمسلمين والتسبيحة، ونحوها لا تسمى خطبة وله قوله تعالى : فاسعوا إلى ذكر الله ، من غير فصل بين كونه ذكراً طويلاً يسمى خطبة، أو لا ولقضية عثمان رضي الله عنه لما قال : الحمد الله فارتج عليه، ثم نزل وصلى بهم ولم ينكر عليه أحد منهم فكان إجماعاً منهم وسنن الخطبة التي في ذات الخطيب، والتي في نفس الخطبة (ثمانية عشر شيئاً) بل يزاد عليها فمن السنة أن يكون جلوس الخطيب في مخدعه عن يمين المنبر، أو جهته لابساً السواد، أو البياض ومنها (الطهارة) حال الخطبة لأنها ليست صلاة ولا كشطرها، وتأويل (حمد وصلاة ودعاء) بدل من قوله : ذكر طويل في السفتاقي الخطبة الأولى فيها أربع فرائض التحميد والصلاة والوصية بتقوى الله، وقراءة آية وكذا في الثانية إلا أن الدعاء في الثانية بدل قراءة الآية في الأولى كذا في شرح المقدسي، وظاهر أن هذا لا يتمشى على قوله : وهو ظاهر، ولا على قولهما لأنهما لا يشترطان الثانية ولا الآية وما ذكره مذهب الشافعي رضي الله عنه. قوله: (فاسعوا إلى ذكر الله) وهو مطلق فكان الشرط الذكر الأعم بالقاطع، وكون المأثور الذكر المسمى خطبة إنما يفيد الوجوب، أو السنية لا أنه هو شرط الذي لا يجزىء غيره. قوله: (ولقضية عثمان الخ ذكر في المحيط والمبسوط وملتقى البحار وشرح البخاري لابن بطال، وشرح مسلم لصدر الدين الخلاطي، والمؤرخون أن عثمان . رضي الله عنه أول جمعة ولي الخلافة صعد المنبر فقال : الحمد الله فأرتج عليه فقال : إن أبا بكر وعمر كانا يعدان لهذا المقام مقالاً، وإنكم إلى إمام فعال أحوج منكم إلى إمام قوال، وستأتيكم الخطب بعد، وأستغفر الله العظيم لي ولكم .اهـ. قال في النهاية : ولم يعن عثمان بقوله : وإنكم الخ تفضيل نفسه على الشيخين، بل على الخلفاء الذين يكونون بعد الراشدين فإنهم يكونون على كثرة في مع قبح الفعال، فكأنه يقول أنا وإن لم أكن قوالاً مثلهم فأنا على الخير دون الشر اهـ. قوله: (فأرتج) بضم الهمزة وسكون الراء المهملة وكسر المثناة من فوق، وبالجيم كاغلق مبنياً للمفعول وزناً، ومعنى أي استغلق عليه الكلام فلم يقدر على إتمامها. قوله: (وسنن الخطبة الخ) منها أن تكون خطبتان تشتمل كل منهما على حمد وتشهد وصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم والأولى على تلاوة آية وعلى ،وعظ والثانية على دعاء للمؤمنين والمؤمنات عوض الوعظ كما ذكره قوله : (بل يزاد عليها الخ زاد على ما ذكره نحو سنتين والعدد لا مفهوم له. قوله: (أو جهته أي المنبر أي إن لم يكن له مخدع كما في الشرح. قوله : (أو البياض) فهو مخير ولا يلزمه اختصاص السواد كما في الشرح وتكره صلاته في المحراب قبل الخطبة قهستاني، وغيره ويكره التفاته يميناً وشمالاً وما يفعله المؤذنون حال الخطبة من الصلاة على النبي ، والترضي عن الصحابة والدعاء للسلطان بالنصر ينبغي أن يكون مكروهاً اتفاقاً. قوله: (الطهارة) فلو خطب محدثاً أو جنباً جاز، ويكره ويستحب إعادتها إذا كان جنباً إلا أذانه زيلعي، وإن لم يعد أجزأ إن لم يطل الفصل بأجنبي. قوله : (لأنها ليست صلاة) بل ذكر
And it is valid to restrict the khutbah to pure dhikr of Allah (such as a tasbihah, or a tahmidah, or a tahlilah, or a takbirah) but with karahah (dislike) for leaving the sunnah according to Imam (Abu Hanifa). And he (Imam) said: There must be a lengthy dhikr called a khutbah, and its minimum is the amount of the tashahhud up to his saying 'His servant and His Messenger', with praise, salawat, and supplication for the Muslims. And the tasbihah and the like are not called a khutbah. And for him (Imam) is the saying of Allah Most High: 'So hasten to the remembrance of Allah', without distinction between it being a lengthy dhikr called a khutbah or not. And due to the incident of Uthman (may Allah be pleased with him) when he said: 'All praise is due to Allah' and then he was at a loss for words, then he descended and led them in prayer, and no one among them objected to him, so it was consensus among them. And the sunnahs of the khutbah related to the khateeb himself and those in the khutbah itself are eighteen things, nay, more are added. Among the sunnah is that the khateeb sit in his chamber (makhda') to the right of the minbar or in its direction, wearing black or white. And among them is purity (tahara) during the khutbah, because it is not prayer nor half of it. And the interpretation of 'praise, salawat, and supplication' is a substitute for his saying 'lengthy dhikr' in al-Siftaqi. The first khutbah has four obligatory acts: praising Allah, salawat, advising taqwa of Allah, and recitation of a verse. Similarly in the second, except that supplication in the second replaces the recitation of a verse in the first, as in the commentary of al-Maqdisi. And it is apparent that this is not consistent with his (Imam's) saying – which is apparent – nor with their saying (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) because they do not require the second khutbah nor the verse. And what he mentioned is the school of al-Shafi'i (may Allah be pleased with him). His saying: 'So hasten to the remembrance of Allah' – it is absolute, so the condition is the general dhikr definitively, and that the transmitted dhikr called khutbah only indicates obligation or sunnah, not that it is a condition that nothing else suffices. His saying: (And the incident of Uthman) – it is mentioned in al-Muhit, al-Mabsut, Multaqa al-Bihar, Sharh al-Bukhari by Ibn Battal, Sharh Muslim by Sadr al-Din al-Khilati, and the historians that Uthman (may Allah be pleased with him) on the first Friday after becoming caliph ascended the minbar and said: 'All praise is due to Allah' and he was at a loss for words, then said: 'Abu Bakr and Umar used to prepare speech for this occasion, and you are in more need of an effective leader than a vocal leader, and sermons will come to you later. I ask Allah the Mighty for forgiveness for me and for you.' End quote. He said in al-Nihayah: Uthman did not mean by his saying 'and you are...' to prefer himself over the two shaykhs (Abu Bakr and Umar), but over the caliphs who would come after the rightly-guided ones, for they would be abundant in evil deeds; he was saying that even if I am not as eloquent as them, I am upon good not evil. End quote. His saying: (fa'rtija) – with dammah on the hamzah, sukun on the ra', kasrah on the tha', and jim, like 'aghlaqa' (locked) in form and meaning, i.e., speech became locked (closed) upon him so he could not complete it. His saying: (And the sunnahs of the khutbah etc.) – among them is that there be two khutbahs, each comprising praise, tashahhud, salawat upon the Prophet (peace be upon him), and the first includes recitation of a verse and admonition, and the second includes supplication for the believing men and women in place of admonition, as he mentioned. His saying: (Nay, more are added) – he added to what he mentioned about two sunnahs, and the number is not restrictive. His saying: (or its direction) i.e., of the minbar, i.e., if he does not have a chamber, as in the commentary. His saying: (or white) – he is free to choose, and he is not obliged to restrict himself to black, as in the commentary. And it is disliked for him to pray in the mihrab before the khutbah, according to Qahistani and others. And it is disliked for him to turn right and left. And what the mu'adhdhins do during the khutbah of sending salawat upon the Prophet, being pleased with the companions, and supplicating for the ruler for victory should be disliked by agreement. His saying: (purity) – if he delivers the khutbah in a state of minor impurity or major impurity, it is permissible but disliked, and it is recommended to repeat it if he was in major impurity, except for his adhan according to al-Zayla'i. And if he does not repeat it, it suffices as long as the interval is not prolonged by something extraneous. His saying: (Because it is not prayer) – but rather dhikr.
Source pages p. 513

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition on the Friday sermon (khutbah). It begins by stating the valid minimum: restricting the khutbah to pure remembrance of Allah, such as saying 'SubhanAllah' or 'Alhamdulillah' or 'La ilaha illa Allah' or 'Allahu Akbar'. While this renders the khutbah valid, it is disliked (makruh tanzihan) because it abandons the sunnah. Imam Abu Hanifa insists that the khutbah must be a lengthy discourse called 'khutbah', with a minimum length similar to the tashahhud up to 'wa rasuluh', and must include praise of Allah, salawat on the Prophet, and supplication for the Muslims. Simple tasbih does not qualify as a khutbah. The proof for this is the Quranic verse 'So hasten to the remembrance of Allah' (62:9) – which does not specify the form of remembrance, and the incident of Caliph Uthman who, after ascending the minbar for the first Friday of his caliphate, said only 'Alhamdulillah', then was unable to continue, descended, and led the prayer. The Companions present did not object, so this is considered a consensus that an abbreviated khutbah is sufficient. The passage then enumerates the sunnahs of the khutbah: eighteen acts, with more possible. Among them: the khateeb sits in his private room (makhda') to the right of the minbar or facing it, wearing black or white; he should be in a state of ritual purity (tahara) during the khutbah – if he is impure, the khutbah is valid but disliked, and it is recommended to repeat it if he was in major impurity, unless the interval is long. The commentary includes a note that the four obligatory elements (fara'id) of the first khutbah according to some are: praising Allah, sending salawat, advising taqwa, and reciting a verse; the second khutbah replaces the verse with supplication. However, this scheme is not consistent with the positions of Abu Hanifa and his two students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), who do not require the second khutbah or the verse – it actually reflects the Shafi'i school. The text clarifies that the verse 'Fas'aw ila dhikr Allah' is general, so any dhikr fulfills the condition, and the specific practice of a longer khutbah indicates obligation or sunnah but does not restrict validity. Additional sunnahs include: giving two khutbahs, each containing praise, tashahhud, and salawat – the first includes a verse and admonition, the second includes supplication instead of admonition. The number eighteen is not fixed; more can be added. The khateeb may wear white or black; he should not pray in the mihrab before the khutbah, nor turn excessively. The actions of mu'adhdhins during the khutbah (sending salawat, etc.) are disliked by agreement. Purity is not a condition for validity; a khutbah given in impurity is valid but disliked.

Key Terms
الخطبة (al-khutbah): The Friday sermon delivered before the Jumu'ah prayer, consisting of remembrance of Allah.
الذكر (al-dhikr): Remembrance of Allah, which minimally suffices for the khutbah (e.g., tasbih, tahmid, tahlil, takbir).
الكراهة (al-karahah): Dislike (makruh tanzihi) – the act is valid but abandoning the better practice is disliked.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum that makes a Friday khutbah valid according to the relied-upon Hanafi view?
A) Any dhikr of Allah, such as saying 'SubhanAllah' once
B) A specific length like the tashahhud
C) Must contain praise, salawat, and advice
D) It must be two separate sermons

Key Takeaway
The Friday khutbah is valid with any remembrance of Allah, but following the sunnah of a longer sermon is recommended and its abandonment is disliked.
