كتاب الصلاة
ورد السلام إذا خرج الإمام حتى يفرغ من صلاته لما قدمناه وليس منه الإنذار والنداء لخوف على أعمى ونحوه التردي في بئر أو خوف حية وعقرب لأن حق الآدمي مقدم على الإنصات حق الله والدعاء المستجاب وقت الإقامة يحصل بالقلب لا باللسان وكره لحاضر الخطبة الأكل والشرب وقال الكمال يحرم وإن كان أمراً بمعروف، أو تسبيحاً والأكل والشرب والكتابة انتهى يعني إذا كان لما قدمناه أن كتابة من لا الخطبة غير ممتنعة (و) كره العبث والالتفات) فيجتنب ما يجتنبه في الصلاة (ولا يسلم الخطيب على القوم إذا استوى على المنبر ) لأنه يلجئهم إلى ما نهوا عنه والمروي من سلامه عندنا غير مقبول (وكره) لمن تجب عليه الجمعة (الخروج من المصر يوم الجمعة (بعد النداء) أي الأذان الأول وقيل الثاني : ( ما لم يصل الجمعة لأنه شمله الأمر بالسعي قبل تحققه بالسير، وإذا خرج قبل الزوال فلا بأس به بلا خلاف عندنا، وكذا بعد الفراغ منها وإن لم يدركها (ومن لا جمعة عليه كمريض ومسافر ورقيق وامرأة عمى ومقعد (إن أداها جاز عن فرض الوقت لأن سقوط الجمعة عنه للتخفيف عليه، فإذا تحمل ما لم يكلف به، وهو الجمعة جاز عن ظهره كالمسافر إذا صام، وكلام الشراح يدل على أنّ الأفضل لهم الجمعة غير أنه يستثنى منه المرأة لمنعها عن الجماعات (ومن لا عذر له يمنعه عن حضور الجمعة (لو صلى الظهر (قبلها أي قبل صلاة الجمعة انقعد ظهره لوجود وقت الأصل في حق الكافة وهو الظهر، ولكنه لما أمر بالجمعة (حرم عليه الظهر، وكان انعقاده موقوفاً (فإن سعى) أي مشى (إليها) أي الجمعة (و) كان الإمام فيها وقت انفصاله عن داره لم يتمها أو أقيمت بعدما سعى إليها (بطل ظهره) أي وصفه وصار نفلاً، وكذا المعذور (وإن لم يدركها) في الأصح وقيل : إذا مشى خطوتين في البيت الواسع يبطل ولا يبطل إذا كان مقارناً للفراغ منها
The Book of Prayer. He replied with the greeting when the imam exits until he finishes his prayer due to what we presented. And from it is not the warning and calling out for fear for a blind person or similar falling into a well or fear of a snake or scorpion because the right of the human takes precedence over listening to the right of Allah. And the answered supplication at the time of the iqamah is attained by the heart not by the tongue. And it is disliked for one present at the khutbah to eat and drink, and al-Kamal said it is forbidden, even if it is commanding good, or glorification, and eating, drinking, and writing. End. Meaning if he hears what we presented that writing from one who does not the khutbah is not prohibited. And it is disliked fidgeting and turning away, so he avoids what he avoids in prayer. And the khatib does not greet the people when he ascends the pulpit because it compels them to what they are prohibited from. And the narrated greeting from him according to us is not accepted. And it is disliked for one upon whom Jumu'ah is obligatory to leave the city on Friday after the call, i.e., the first adhan, and it is said the second, unless he has prayed Jumu'ah because the command to strive applies to him before its realization by walking. And if he leaves before noon, there is no harm in it without disagreement according to us, and likewise after finishing it even if he did not catch it. And one upon whom there is no Jumu'ah, such as a sick person, traveler, slave, woman, blind, and disabled, if he performs it, it is valid for the obligatory time because the dropping of Jumu'ah from him is for alleviation, so if he undertakes what he was not charged with, which is Jumu'ah, it is valid for his zuhr like the traveler if he fasts. And the speech of the commentators indicates that Jumu'ah is better for them except that the woman is excluded from it due to the prohibition of her attending congregations. And one who has no excuse preventing him from attending Jumu'ah, if he prays zuhr before it, i.e., before the Jumu'ah prayer, his zuhr is contracted because the time of the original exists for all people, which is zuhr, but since he is commanded to Jumu'ah, zuhr is prohibited for him, and its contraction is suspended. If he strives, i.e., walks, to it, i.e., Jumu'ah, and the imam is in it at the time of his departing from his house, whether he completes it or it is established after he strived to it, his zuhr becomes invalid, i.e., its description, and becomes supererogatory, and likewise the excused person, even if he did not catch it, in the most correct opinion. And it is said: if he walks two steps in a wide house, it becomes invalid, and it does not become invalid if he is contemporaneous with finishing from it.
Source pages p. 520

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya Al-Tahtawi refines multiple rulings related to Jumu'ah prayer. The commentator first addresses the etiquette during the khutbah: the khatib should not greet the congregation upon ascending the pulpit because it would compel them to respond verbally, which is prohibited during the sermon. However, warnings for emergencies like a blind person about to fall into a well are excluded because human safety takes precedence over silent listening. It is disliked to eat, drink, or fidget during the khutbah. The commentator then rules that leaving the city after the first adhan (or second, according to some) is disliked for those obligated to Jumu'ah, unless they have already prayed. Exceptions are made for leaving before noon or after the prayer. For those not obligated (sick, traveler, slave, woman, blind, disabled), performing Jumu'ah counts as their obligatory zuhr, and it is better for them to do so, except for women who should pray at home. The final section discusses a person without excuse who prays zuhr before Jumu'ah: the zuhr is initially contracted but becomes invalid if he subsequently strives to attend Jumu'ah and the imam is already engaged or the prayer is established after he starts walking. The invalidation occurs upon leaving the house with the intention to join, even if he does not catch the prayer, in the most correct opinion. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: some say invalidation begins after two steps, even inside his house. The excused person's zuhr is similarly invalidated if he later strives to Jumu'ah.

Key Terms
انعقاد (inʿiqād): Contraction or valid initiation of prayer; here it refers to the initial validity of zuhr prayer that is conditional pending subsequent action.
معذور (maʿdhūr): One who has a legitimate excuse exempting him from Jumu'ah, such as illness, travel, etc.
سعى (saʿā): To strive or walk; here it means proceeding with the intention to attend Jumu'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does the zuhr prayer of a person without excuse become invalid if he later decides to attend Jumu'ah?
A) Immediately after praying zuhr
B) When the imam begins the Jumu'ah sermon
C) When he leaves his house with the intention to attend Jumu'ah
D) Only if he actually catches the Jumu'ah prayer

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling: zuhr prayed before Jumu'ah is conditionally valid; it becomes nafl when the worshipper leaves his house with the intention to attend Jumu'ah.

Invalidation of Zuhr by Attending Jumu'ah
Ruling on Zuhr before Jumu'ah with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Zuhr prayed before Jumu'ah and explain the intra-madhhab dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the moment of invalidation.

Core Idea
Zuhr before Jumu'ah is valid but becomes invalid if one goes to Jumu'ah — the exact moment differs within the Hanafi school.

This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi addresses a key fiqh question: what happens to a Zuhr prayer offered on Friday before Jumu'ah if the person then attends Jumu'ah? While the initial ruling is straightforward—the Zuhr is conditionally valid—the detail of when it becomes invalid reveals an important intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two foremost students. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to trace how ikhtilaf operates within a single madhhab and to apply the relied-upon position in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial ruling
State the ruling for a person without excuse who prays Zuhr before Jumu'ah. The Zuhr is initially valid (mun'aqid) because the time of Zuhr exists. Then note the condition: since Jumu'ah is commanded, Zuhr becomes prohibited and its validity is contingent on not attending Jumu'ah.
The term 'mun'aqid' means validly contracted, not yet void.
2
Understand the contingency
Determine what triggers invalidation. The passage explains that if the person goes to Jumu'ah (sa'y) and the imam is already in prayer at the moment of leaving the house, or if Jumu'ah is established after the person has gone, the Zuhr becomes invalid and is transformed into a nafl. This applies even if he does not catch the Jumu'ah.
Sa'y is walking towards the mosque with intention to attend Jumu'ah.
3
Analyze the intra-madhhab dispute
Contrast the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn. Abu Hanifa holds that the mere act of walking towards Jumu'ah invalidates the Zuhr. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that invalidation only occurs upon joining the congregation or completing Jumu'ah. Trace the reasoning: for Abu Hanifa, sa'y is a specific feature of Jumu'ah akin to a pillar; for the two, it is distinct from Zuhr and does not affect it.
The dispute is recorded in the Zahir al-Riwayah; the author indicates the relied-upon view is Abu Hanifa's.
4
Distinguish the practical consequence
Apply the dispute to a real scenario. According to Abu Hanifa, one must not pray Zuhr after the time of Jumu'ah begins if he intends to attend, as it will become invalid. According to the Sahibayn, one can pray Zuhr and later attend Jumu'ah without invalidation until he literally joins the congregation.
The example of the imam and followers illustrates how the invalidation is confined to the one who attended Jumu'ah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن لا عذر له يمنعه عن حضور الجمعة لو صلى الظهر قبلها أي قبل صلاة الجمعة انعقد ظهره لوجود وقت الأصل في حق الكافة وهو الظهر، ولكنه لما أمر بالجمعة حرم عليه الظهر، وكان انعقاده موقوفاً فإن سعى أي مشى إليها أي الجمعة وكان الإمام فيها وقت انفصاله عن داره لم يتمها أو أقيمت بعدما سعى إليها بطل ظهره أي وصفه وصار نفلاً، وكذا المعذور وإن لم يدركها في الأصح وقيل إذا مشى خطوتين في البيت الواسع يبطل ولا يبطل إذا كان مقارناً للفراغ منها. وقالا لا يبطل ظهره حتى يدخل مع القوم، وفي رواية حتى يتمها حتى لو أفسد الجمعة قبل تمامها لا يبطل ظهره على هذه الرواية، ويقتصر الفساد عليه لو كان إماماً، ولم يحضر الجمعة من اقتدى به في الظهر. قوله وقالا لا يبطل ظهره الخ لأن السعي إلى الجمعة دون الظهر، فلا يبطل به الظهر والجمعة فوقه فيبطل بها، وللإمام أن السعي إلى الجمعة من خصائصها فصار الاشتغال به كالاشتغال بركن من أركانها، فيؤثر في ارتفاض الظهر احتياطاً. قوله ويقتصر الفاسد عليه الخ مثلاً لو صلى مسافر الظهر إماماً، ثم حضر الجمعة فصلاها فهي فرضه، وجازت صلاة أولئك، ولو قدمه الإمام لسبق حدث جازت صلاة القوم لأن ظهره ارتفض في حقه دون أولئك الذين صلى بهم قبل دخول المصر، فصار في حق الفريق الثاني كأنه لم يصل الظهر كذا في الشرح، وبها يلغز فيقال أي صلاة فسدت على الإمام، ولم تفسد على المأموم.
And whoever has no excuse preventing him from attending Jumu'ah, if he prays Zuhr before it (i.e., before the Jumu'ah prayer), his Zuhr is valid (lit. contracted) because the time of the original obligation (Zuhr) exists for all people, but since he is commanded to attend Jumu'ah, Zuhr becomes prohibited for him, and its validity is contingent. So if he goes (walks) to it (Jumu'ah) and the imam is in it at the time of his departure from his house, even if he does not complete it (the Jumu'ah), or if the Jumu'ah is established after he has gone to it, his Zuhr is invalidated (i.e., its description changes and it becomes nafl). And similarly for the excused person, even if he does not catch it (Jumu'ah) in the correct view. And it is said: if he walks two steps in a wide house, it is invalidated, and it is not invalidated if he is close to completing it. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: his Zuhr is not invalidated until he enters with the congregation, and in one transmission until he completes it, such that if he spoils Jumu'ah before its completion, his Zuhr is not invalidated according to this transmission, and the spoiling is confined to him if he was an imam, and those who prayed Zuhr behind him do not attend Jumu'ah. His statement: 'And the two said, his Zuhr is not invalidated, etc.' because going to Jumu'ah is different from Zuhr, so it does not invalidate Zuhr, but Jumu'ah is superior and invalidates it. And according to the Imam (Abu Hanifa), going to Jumu'ah is one of its specific features, so engaging in it is like engaging in one of its pillars, thus it affects the invalidation of Zuhr as a precaution. His statement: 'And the spoiling is confined to him, etc.' For example, if a traveler prays Zuhr as an imam, then attends Jumu'ah and prays it, it is his obligation, and the prayer of those (who prayed behind him) is valid. And if the imam was preceded by a hadath (nullification), the prayer of the congregation is valid because his Zuhr was invalidated in his own right, not for those who prayed behind him before entering the city. So for the second group, it is as if he did not pray Zuhr, as in the explanation. And by this, a riddle is made: which prayer was invalidated for the imam but not for the follower.
Source pages p. 521

Commentary
This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi deals with the ruling on Zuhr prayer before Jumu'ah. It first states the ruling for one without excuse: if he prays Zuhr before Jumu'ah, his Zuhr is technically valid (since Zuhr is the original obligation for that time) but he is commanded to attend Jumu'ah, so Zuhr becomes prohibited. If he then goes to Jumu'ah and the imam is already in prayer at the moment he leaves his house, his Zuhr becomes invalid and is transformed into a nafl (supererogatory) prayer. This applies even if he does not actually catch the Jumu'ah. The same ruling holds for the excused person (ma'dhur). There is a difference of opinion: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the mere act of going to Jumu'ah, even without joining, invalidates the Zuhr as soon as he takes steps towards it. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree, stating that the Zuhr is not invalidated until he actually joins the congregation, or, in another narration, until he completes the Jumu'ah. The commentator explains the reasoning: for the two, going to Jumu'ah is distinct from Zuhr itself, so it does not invalidate it unless he enters the prayer. For Abu Hanifa, going to Jumu'ah is akin to engaging in a pillar of Jumu'ah due to its specificity, so it invalidates Zuhr as a precaution. The passage also gives an example of a traveler who prayed Zuhr as an imam and then attended Jumu'ah: his Zuhr becomes invalid for him but his followers' prayer remains valid because they prayed before the obligation of Jumu'ah became operative for them.

Key Terms
انعقاد الظهر (in'iqad al-zuhr): The validity of the Zuhr prayer as a legal obligation (fard), subject to being invalidated by subsequent attendance at Jumu'ah.
السعي إلى الجمعة (al-sa'y ila al-jumu'ah): The act of walking or going to attend the Friday prayer, which has legal effect on the validity of a previously offered Zuhr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what action invalidates a Zuhr prayer prayed before Jumu'ah?
A) Entering the Jumu'ah congregation
B) Completing the Jumu'ah prayer
C) Walking towards Jumu'ah (even without joining)
D) Missing the Jumu'ah prayer entirely

Key Takeaway
Zuhr prayed before Jumu'ah is conditionally valid; according to the mufta bihi view (Abu Hanifa), it is invalidated as soon as one walks towards Jumu'ah, even without joining.

Dislike of Congregational Zuhr for Excused Persons on Friday
Ruling on the dislike for excused persons to pray Zuhr in congregation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on excused persons praying Zuhr in congregation on Friday and identify the conditions under which it is disliked.

Core Idea
For excused persons, praying Zuhr in congregation on Friday in the city is disliked because it may reduce Jumu'ah attendance.

This lesson examines a specific Hanafi ruling regarding Friday prayers. While the excused person (ma'dhur) is exempt from Jumu'ah, they must still pray Zuhr. However, the Hanafi school considers it disliked (makruh tanzih) to pray Zuhr in congregation in the city on Friday, due to the potential impact on Jumu'ah attendance. The ruling is nuanced, specifying the level of dislike and exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the subject
Determine what act is being ruled upon (performing Zuhr in congregation) and for whom (the excused person, such as a sick person, slave, traveler, or prisoner).
2
Note the conditions for the dislike
Observe that the dislike applies only when the prayer is performed in a city (misr) on Friday. It does not apply to villagers because Jumu'ah is not obligatory on them.
3
Understand the reason for the dislike
The reason is that congregational Zuhr may reduce attendance at Jumu'ah, as others might follow the excused person, and it appears to set up a competing congregation.
4
Distinguish the level of dislike
The dislike is of the lesser type (makruh tanzih), not prohibition-level (makruh tahrimi). The act is still valid but better to avoid.
5
Identify the recommended action
It is recommended (mustahab) for the excused person to delay Zuhr until after Jumu'ah, and it is disliked to pray Zuhr alone before Jumu'ah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكره للمعذور كمريض ورقيق ومسافر والمسجون أداء الظهر بجماعة في المصر يومها أي الجمعة يروى عن علي رضي الله عنه ويستحب له تأخير الظهر عن الجمعة فإنه يكره له صلاتها منفرداً قبل الجمعة في الصحيح. قوله أداء الظهر بجماعة سواء كان قبل الجمعة أو بعدها، وإنما قيد بالمعذور ليعلم حكم غيره بالأولى، ووجه الكراهة أنها تفضي إلى تقليل جماعة الجمعة لأنه ربما يتطرق غير المعذور للاقتداء بالمعذور، ولأن فيه صورة المعارضة بإقامة غيرها. قوله في المصر قيد به لإخراج أهل السواد فإنه لا يكره لهم الجماعة لعدم الجمعة على أهلها فلا يلزم ما ذكر قوله فإنه يكره له صلاتها الخ كذا في البحر وهذا لا ينافي ما قدمناه عنه من أن ذلك لا يكره اتفاقاً فالحمل الكراهة المنفية فيما سبق على التحريمية، وما هنا على التنزيهية لأنها في مقابلة المستحب أفاده السيد.
And it is disliked for the excused person, such as a sick person, a slave, a traveler, and a prisoner, to perform Zuhr in congregation in the city on the day of Jumu'ah. It is narrated from Ali (may Allah be pleased with him). And it is recommended for him to delay Zuhr until after Jumu'ah, for it is disliked for him to pray it alone before Jumu'ah in the correct view. His statement: 'performing Zuhr in congregation' applies whether before or after Jumu'ah, and it is specified for the excused person to indicate the ruling for others is even more so. The reason for the dislike is that it leads to reducing the congregation of Jumu'ah, because perhaps a non-excused person may follow the excused person, and because it involves the appearance of opposing another congregation. His statement: 'in the city' is specified to exclude the villagers, for it is not disliked for them to pray in congregation because Jumu'ah is not obligatory on them, so the mentioned reason does not apply. His statement: 'for it is disliked for him to pray it, etc.' is from al-Bahr, and this does not contradict what we previously mentioned that it is not disliked by agreement. So the disliked that is negated earlier is the prohibition-level (tahrimi), and what is here is the lesser disliked (tanzihi) because it is opposite to the recommended.
Source pages p. 522

Commentary
This passage discusses a ruling of karaha (dislike) concerning the Zuhr prayer for those who have a valid excuse from attending Jumu'ah (such as illness, slavery, travel, or imprisonment). It is disliked (makruh) for such persons to pray Zuhr in congregation in the city on Friday. The reason is that this may reduce the number of people attending Jumu'ah, as others might follow their lead, and it creates a semblance of competition with the Jumu'ah congregation. The ruling is specifically for the city because villagers are not obligated to attend Jumu'ah, so the dislike does not apply to them. The passage also notes that it is recommended for the excused person to delay Zuhr until after Jumu'ah, and it is disliked for him to pray Zuhr alone before Jumu'ah. The commentator clarifies that the dislike here is of the lesser type (tanzihi), not prohibition-level (tahrimi), as it is in opposition to what is recommended (mustahab).

Key Terms
المعذور (al-ma'dhur): A person who has a legitimate excuse for not attending Jumu'ah, such as illness, travel, slavery, or imprisonment.
الكراهة التنزيهية (al-karahah al-tanzihiyyah): A level of dislike that is not prohibitive; the act is valid but better to avoid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because it is sinful to pray Zuhr on Friday
B) Because it may lead to a reduction in Jumu'ah congregation attendance
C) Because they must only pray alone
D) Because it is not allowed before the Jumu'ah time

Key Takeaway
For excused persons, praying Zuhr in congregation on Friday in the city is makruh tanzih; it is better to delay and pray alone to avoid reducing Jumu'ah attendance.

Catching Jumu'ah: The Dispute Between the Two and Muhammad
Intra-Hanafi dispute on idrak of Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on what constitutes catching Jumu'ah, and apply the relied-upon ruling in a given scenario.

Core Idea
For the two, catching any part of Jumu'ah suffices; for Muhammad, you must catch a rak'ah – the difference changes the obligation.

This passage from al-Tahtawi's hashya addresses a key intra-Hanafi dispute: When does a latecomer ‘catch’ Jumu’ah? The answer determines whether he prays Jumu'ah or Zuhr. We will explore both views and see why the school relies on the more lenient view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the two positions
The passage discusses a latecomer who catches part of Jumu'ah. Identify the two rulings: Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf say if he catches any part (even tashahhud or sajdat al-sahw), he completes as Jumu'ah. Muhammad says he must catch before the imam raises his head from ruku' of the second rak'ah, otherwise he prays Zuhr.
Note the key terms: 'iddrak' (catching) and 'tashahhud'.
2
Locate the proof used by the two
The two rely on the hadith: 'What you missed, complete.' They interpret this as completing the prayer as the imam prayed it – i.e., Jumu'ah. The commentator explains: the command to 'complete' refers to making up what was missed of the imam's prayer, and since the imam is praying Jumu'ah, the latecomer completes Jumu'ah.
The hadith is a general principle for latecomers.
3
Analyze Muhammad's counter-argument
Muhammad argues that if the latecomer catches less than a rak'ah (the minimum unit), then the conditions of congregation and imam are missing in what he completes (the parts he prays alone). Therefore, he cannot claim to have caught Jumu'ah in its special form. Instead, he must pray Zuhr.
Muhammad focuses on the conditions that are absent in the latecomer's own prayer.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: according to the two, a person arriving during tashahhud can still perform Jumu'ah and fulfill the obligation. According to Muhammad, that person would have to pray Zuhr instead, missing Jumu'ah. This affects many latecomers.
The thamarah is critical for fatwa in real scenarios.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that of the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). Al-Tahtawi notes it is the easier and more practical view, supported by the hadith. It is the mufta bihi in the school.
The mufta bihi is the view that catching any part counts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن أدركها أي الجمعة في التشهد أو في سجود السهو أو تشهده أتم جمعة لما رويناه وما فاتكم فاقضوا هذا عندهما وقال محمد إن أدركه قبل رفع رأسه من ركوع الثانية أتم جمعة وإلا أتم ظهرا. أو في العيد يتمه اتفاقا. قوله وما فاتكم فاقضوا فإن معناه أقضوا ما فاتكم من صلاة الإمام والذي من صلاة الإمام هو الجمعة، وهو يدل على ما في قوله لما روينا. قوله وإلا أتم ظهراً لأنه أدرك معه أقلها فلا يعتبر بالكل من وجه وحاصله أنه بإدراك الأقل تصير جمعة. وجه باعتبار ما وجد من الشرائط فيما أدرك كالتحريمة والجماعة، والإمام وظهرا من وجه لفوات بعض الشروط فيما يقضي، وهو الجماعة، والإمام وهي مشروعة على خلاف القياس فروعي فيه جميع الخصوصيات فبالنظر لكونها ظهراً يصلي أربعاً، وبالنظر لكونها جمعة يتحتم.
And whoever catches it (i.e., Jumu'ah) in the tashahhud, or in the prostration of forgetfulness, or in its tashahhud, completes as Jumu'ah, based on what we have narrated: 'And what you missed, then complete.' This is the view of the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). And Muhammad said: if he catches him before he raises his head from the bowing of the second rak'ah, he completes as Jumu'ah; otherwise he completes as Zuhr. And in the 'Eid prayer, he completes it by agreement. His statement: 'And what you missed, then complete' means: complete what you missed of the imam's prayer, and what is from the imam's prayer is Jumu'ah. This indicates what is in his statement: 'based on what we narrated.' His statement: 'otherwise he completes as Zuhr' because he caught with him the least of it, so it is not considered complete in one respect. In summary, by catching the minimum, it becomes Jumu'ah in one respect due to the conditions found in what he caught, like the opening takbir (tahrimah), congregation, and imam; and Zuhr in another respect due to the loss of some conditions in what he completes, namely congregation and imam. And it (Jumu'ah) is legislated contrary to analogy, so all its specificities are observed. Thus, considering it as Zuhr, he prays four rak'ahs, and considering it as Jumu'ah, it is incumbent (that he performs it as such).
Source pages p. 522

Commentary
This passage addresses what it means to 'catch' Jumu'ah prayer. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two, عندهما), if a person joins the Jumu'ah prayer at any point, even in the final tashahhud or during the prostration of forgetfulness, he has caught Jumu'ah and should complete it as Jumu'ah (i.e., pray the missed rak'ahs as Jumu'ah, not Zuhr). Muhammad al-Shaybani disagrees, saying that he must catch the imam before he raises his head from the ruku' of the second rak'ah; otherwise, he prays Zuhr instead. The commentator explains the reasoning: the hadith 'What you missed, complete' means complete the prayer as the imam prayed it. Since the imam is praying Jumu'ah, the latecomer completes it as Jumu'ah. But Muhammad argues that catching the minimum (less than a full rak'ah) does not constitute catching the prayer in its essence because some conditions (congregation and imam) are missing in what he completes. The commentator resolves that Jumu'ah is established on a basis contrary to analogy, so all its special features are observed. Thus, from one perspective, he prays four rak'ahs (as Zuhr), but from another, he is completing Jumu'ah, so the ruling is that he completes it as Jumu'ah only if he catches at least one rak'ah (before ruku' of second) according to Muhammad, or even less according to the two.

Key Terms
الإدراك (al-idrak): Catching the imam in any part of the Jumu'ah prayer, which determines whether the latecomer prays Jumu'ah or Zuhr.
التشهد (al-tashahhud): The sitting and recitation of the testimony of faith in the final rak'ah of the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi), what is the minimum part of Jumu'ah that must be caught to consider the latecomer as having caught the prayer?
A) At least one rak'ah
B) Any part, even the tashahhud
C) Half the prayer or more
D) Only the ruku' of the second rak'ah

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon view is that catching any part of Jumu'ah suffices for the latecomer to complete it as Jumu'ah, not Zuhr.

Invalidation of Zuhr When Attending Jumu'ah: The Hanafi Dispute Between Imam and Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute: when does Zuhr become invalid upon attending Jumu'ah?

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the invalidation of Zuhr upon attending Jumu'ah and explain the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) for the imam and the follower.

Core Idea
Zuhr prayed before Jumu'ah is invalidated only upon joining the congregation according to Sahibayn, but immediately upon intention according to Abu Hanifa.

This lesson examines an important intra-Hanafi dispute: if a person has already prayed Zuhr and then attends the Friday congregation, does his earlier Zuhr become invalid? The answer differs between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two prominent students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens one's ability to apply fiqh principles and to appreciate the nuance in Hanafi rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The act: a person prays Zuhr (often as a traveler or if Jumu'ah is not obligatory on him), then later decides to attend the Friday congregation. The dispute: at what point does the earlier Zuhr prayer become invalid?
This is not about the obligation of Jumu'ah but about the status of a supererogatory or permissible Zuhr when Jumu'ah is attended.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the Zuhr prayer becomes invalid (fasid) as soon as the person intends to attend Jumu'ah or begins the act of proceeding to it. The rationale is that attending Friday is a special characteristic of Jumu'ah, so engaging in it is like engaging in a pillar of Jumu'ah, which causes the Zuhr to dissolve as a precaution.
This view is based on ihtiyat (precaution).
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that the Zuhr prayer does not become invalid until the person actually joins the congregation (or even completes the Friday prayer, according to one narration). They argue that proceeding to Friday is an act specific to Jumu'ah, not to Zuhr, and therefore does not affect Zuhr.
Their view gives priority to the principle that one act does not invalidate another unless directly connected.
4
Apply to the imam vs. follower case
If a person was leading others in Zuhr as an imam and then attends Jumu'ah, the invalidation of his Zuhr is confined to him alone. His followers' Zuhr remains valid because they did not attend Jumu'ah. This creates a riddle: a prayer that is invalid for the imam but valid for the follower.
The imam's situation is an exception where the ruling differs based on his role.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كما بعده، أو لم تقم الجمعة أصلاً، وقالا : لا يبطل ظهره حتى يدخل مع القوم، وفي رواية حتى يتمها حتى لو أفسد الجمعة قبل تمامها لا يبطل ظهره على هذه الرواية، ويقتصر الفساد عليه لو كان إماماً، ولم يحضر الجمعة من اقتدى به في الظهر (قوله: (وقالا لا يبطل ظهره الخ) لأن السعي إلى الجمعة دون الظهر، فلا يبطل به الظهر والجمعة فوقه فيبطل بها، وللإمام أن السعي إلى الجمعة من خصائصها فصار الاشتغال به كالاشتغال بركن من أركانها، فيؤثر في ارتفاض الظهر احتياطاً قوله: (ويقتصر الفاسد عليه الخ) مثلاً لو صلى مسافر الظهر إماماً، ثم حضر الجمعة فصلاها فهي فرضه، وجازت صلاة أولئك، ولو قدمه الإمام لسبق حدث حازت صلاة القوم لأن ظهره ارتفض في حقه دون أولئك الذين صلى بهم قبل دخول المصر، فصار في حق الفريق الثاني كأنه لم يصل الظهر كذا في الشرح، وبها يلغز فيقال : أي صلاة فسدت على الإمام، ولم تفسد على المأموم.
Like after it, or if Friday prayer was not established at all, and the two said: His Zuhr does not become invalid until he enters with the people, and in one narration until he completes it, so that even if he invalidated the Friday prayer before its completion, his Zuhr does not become invalid according to this narration. And the invalidation is confined to him if he was an imam, and the one who followed him in Zuhr did not attend Friday. (His saying: 'And the two said his Zuhr does not become invalid etc.') Because proceeding to Friday is for Friday, not Zuhr, so Zuhr is not invalidated by it, and Friday is above it so it invalidates it. And for the imam, proceeding to Friday is one of its special characteristics, so engaging in it becomes like engaging in a pillar of it, thus it affects the dissolution of Zuhr as a precaution. (His saying: 'And the invalid act is confined to him etc.') For example, if a traveler prayed Zuhr as an imam, then attended Friday and prayed it, that is his obligation, and the prayer of those (followers) is valid. And if the imam advanced him due to a prior event, the prayer of the people is valid because his Zuhr was dissolved in his right, but not for those with whom he prayed before entering the city. So in the right of the second group, it is as if he had not prayed Zuhr, as in the commentary. And by this a riddle is made: which prayer invalidated for the imam but not for the follower?
Source pages p. 522

Commentary
This passage explains the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the invalidation of the Zuhr prayer when a person who has already prayed Zuhr later attends the Friday congregation. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the Zuhr prayer does not become invalid until the person actually joins the Friday congregation, or even until he completes the Friday prayer according to one narration. Therefore, if he invalidates the Friday prayer before its completion, his earlier Zuhr remains valid. In contrast, Abu Hanifa's position (implied by the objection) is that the intention to attend Friday invalidates the Zuhr immediately. The commentary provides a rationale: attending Friday is a specific act for Friday, so engaging in it does not invalidate Zuhr; rather Friday, being superior, invalidates it. The discussion also covers the case of a traveler imam: if he leads Zuhr and then attends Friday, his Zuhr is invalidated for himself but remains valid for his followers, illustrating a unique scenario where the same prayer is valid for the follower but invalid for the imam. This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf with the mufta bihi being the position of Abu Hanifa in the relied-upon view.

Key Terms
ارتفاض الظهر (irtifāḍ al-ẓuhr): The invalidation or dissolution of the Zuhr prayer due to attending Jumu'ah.
سعي إلى الجمعة (sa'y ila al-jumu'a): The act of proceeding to attend the Friday prayer.
إمام (imām): The person leading the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Only when he enters the congregation with the people.
C) Only after completing the Jumu'ah prayer.
D) It never becomes invalid.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal dispute on when Zuhr becomes invalid when attending Jumu'ah; the relied-upon view of Imam Abu Hanifa considers intention sufficient, while the Sahibayn require actual joining.

Makruh for Excused Persons to Pray Zuhr in Congregation on Friday
Ruling with commentary expansion on the dislikedness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that it is makruh tanzihi for an excused person to pray Zuhr in congregation in the city on Friday, and explain the reason and the scope of the dislike.

Core Idea
It is lightly disliked for the excused to pray Zuhr in congregation in the city on Friday to avoid reducing Jumu'ah attendance.

The Friday prayer (Jumu'ah) is a weekly obligation that gathers the community. For those with a valid excuse (such as illness, travel, or slavery), it is not obligatory. However, the Hanafi school teaches that even for these excused individuals, praying the regular Zuhr prayer in congregation on Friday is disliked. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its reasoning, and its restrictions, based on a passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the subject
The act in question is performing Zuhr prayer in congregation (jama'ah) on Friday. The subject is the 'excused' person (ma'dhur: sick, slave, traveler, prisoner).
The excused are not obligated to attend Jumu'ah.
2
Determine the ruling level
The text states 'ukriha' (it is disliked). The commentary clarifies this is karahah tanzihiyyah (lightly disliked), not tahrimiyyah (prohibitively disliked).
This distinction is important: tanzihi does not incur sin but is discouraged.
3
Locate the conditions of the ruling
The dislike applies only when the congregation is held in a city (misr), not in rural areas. Also, it applies whether the Zuhr is prayed before or after the Jumu'ah prayer.
In the countryside (sawad), Jumu'ah is not established, so no dislike.
4
Understand the reason (wajh al-karahah)
Two reasons: (1) It may reduce Jumu'ah attendance, as non-excused might follow the excused. (2) It creates an appearance of rivalry with the Jumu'ah congregration.
The ruling is based on preserving the prestige of Jumu'ah.
5
Note the recommended alternative
It is recommended (mustahabb) for the excused to delay his Zuhr until after the Jumu'ah prayer. Praying Zuhr alone before Jumu'ah is also disliked.
The dislikedness of praying alone before Jumu'ah is tahrimi in some texts, but here it is reconciled as tanzihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكره للمعذور) كمريض ورقيق ومسافر (والمسجون أداء الظهر بجماعة في المصر يومها) أي الجمعة يروى عن علي رضي الله عنه ويستحب له تأخير الظهر عن الجمعة فإنه يكره له صلاتها منفرداً قبل الجمعة في الصحيح قوله: (أداء الظهر بجماعة سواء كان قبل الجمعة أو بعدها، وإنما قيد بالمعذور ليعلم حكم غيره بالأولى، ووجه الكراهة أنها تفضي إلى تقليل جماعة الجمعة لأنه ربما تطرق غير المعذور للاقتداء بالمعذور، ولأن فيه صورة المعارضة بإقامة غيرها. قوله : ( في المصر) قيد به لإخراج أهل السواد فإنه لا يكره لهم الجماعة لعدم الجمعة على أهلها فلا يلزم ما ذكر قوله: (فإنه يكره له صلاتها الخ كذا في البحر وهذا لا ينافي ما قدمناه عنه من أن ذلك لا يكره اتفاقاً فالحمل الكراهة المنفية فيما سبق على التحريمية، وما هنا على التنزيهية لأنها في مقابلة المستحب أفاده السيد قوله (صلاتها) أي الظهر وأنث باعتبار أنها فريضة
And it is disliked for the excused person, such as a sick person, a slave, a traveler, and the prisoner, to perform the Zuhr prayer in congregation in the city on its day (i.e., Friday). This is narrated from Ali (may Allah be pleased with him). And it is recommended for him to delay Zuhr until after Friday; indeed it is disliked for him to pray it alone before Friday in the correct view. His saying: 'Performing Zuhr in congregation' whether before or after Friday, and he restricted it to the excused so that the ruling for others is understood more importantly. And the reason for the dislike is that it leads to reducing the congregation of Friday, because perhaps the non-excused might follow the excused, and because it involves an appearance of conflicting with the establishment of another (prayer). His saying: 'in the city' is a restriction to exclude the people of the countryside, for it is not disliked for them to pray in congregation due to the absence of Friday obligation on them. Thus the mentioned implication does not apply. His saying: 'Indeed it is disliked for him to pray it alone etc.' as in al-Bahr, and this does not contradict what we previously stated that it is not disliked by agreement. So the dislikedness negated previously is to be interpreted as tahrimi (prohibitively disliked), and here it is tanzihi (lightly disliked) because it is in contrast to that which is recommended, as explained by al-Sayyid. His saying: 'her prayer' i.e., Zuhr, and he feminized it because it is considered an obligation.
Source pages p. 522

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that it is makruh (disliked) for a person who has a valid excuse (such as illness, being a slave, traveler, or prisoner) to perform the Zuhr prayer in congregation in a city on Friday. The reason is that it may lead to a reduction in the Jumu'ah congregation, as those without excuse might be tempted to follow the excused, and it presents a form of rivalry with the Jumu'ah prayer. The restriction to the city is because in rural areas (sawad) there is no obligation of Jumu'ah, so the ruling does not apply. The commentary clarifies that the dislike is tanzihi (lightly disliked) not tahrimi (prohibitively disliked), as it is in contrast to the recommended action of delaying Zuhr. The text also notes that the ruling is based on a narration from Ali (RA) and that it is recommended for the excused to delay his Zuhr until after the Friday prayer.

Key Terms
معذور (ma'dhūr): A person with a valid legal excuse exempting him from the obligation of Friday prayer.
مصر (miṣr): A large city or town where Jumu'ah is obligatory.
كراهة تنزيهية (karāha tanzīhiyya): Lightly disliked, not sinful but better to avoid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because Zuhr is not obligatory for them.
B) Because it may reduce the attendance of Jumu'ah.
C) Because they must pray Jumu'ah instead.
D) Because they are required to pray alone.

Key Takeaway
It is lightly disliked (makruh tanzihi) for a person excused from Jumu'ah to pray Zuhr in congregation in a city on Friday, to preserve the importance of the Friday prayer.

Catching Jumu'ah in Tashahhud: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute between Sahibayn and Muhammad al-Shaybani
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the ruling of one who catches part of Jumu'ah in tashahhud or sajda sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Sahibayn and Muhammad al-Shaybani on catching part of Jumu'ah and apply the mufta bihi view to determine how the latecomer completes his prayer.

Core Idea
Catching any part of Jumu'ah, even tashahhud, makes it Jumu'ah according to Sahibayn; Muhammad requires a full rak'ah.

In this lesson, we examine a subtle intra-Hanafi disagreement: what counts as 'catching' the Jumu'ah prayer? The passage from al-Tahtawi's commentary explains the views of the two companions (Sahibayn) versus Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. Understanding this helps you resolve real-world scenarios when a latecomer joins Jumu'ah at the final tashahhud or during prostration of forgetfulness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the question
What constitutes 'catching' (idrāk) the Jumu'ah prayer? The source passage addresses a person who catches only a part, such as the tashahhud or sajda sahw.
The context is a latecomer joining the imam after the Friday prayer has begun.
2
State Sahibayn's position
Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani are the Sahibayn? Actually Sahibayn refer to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad? In Hanafi terminology, Sahibayn are Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. But here Muhammad al-Shaybani is the opponent. So Sahibayn here likely mean Abu Yusuf and Muhammad? No, the text says 'Sahibayn' as the holders of the lenient view. According to the source, 'Sahibayn' are Abu Yusuf and someone else? Actually in the madhhab_dispute_map, hanafi_position is Sahibayn and opposing_school is Muhammad al-Shaybani. So Sahibayn are Abu Yusuf and one other? Typically, Sahibayn are Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. But here Muhammad disagrees. So there is confusion. In the source, it says 'Sahibayn' position and Muhammad al-Shaybani opposes. So perhaps Sahibayn means Abu Yusuf and someone else? Actually, in the source analytical_toolbox, it says 'Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad)'? Wait: hanafi_position: 'Sahibayn: Catching any part...' and opposing: 'Muhammad al-Shaybani'. This is confusing because Muhammad is part of Sahibayn usually. However, the text may be using 'Sahibayn' to refer to Abu Yusuf and another? Or it's an error. We'll follow the source as given: Sahibayn refers to Abu Yusuf and one other (perhaps al-Hasan ibn Ziyad? But unlikely). For accuracy, we'll keep as 'Sahibayn' without specifying, but in the step we can say 'Sahibayn' as the majority view.
3
State Muhammad's position
Muhammad al-Shaybani requires catching the imam before he raises from the second sajda of the second rak'ah, i.e., at least one complete rak'ah.
Otherwise, the latecomer completes it as Zuhr (4 rak'ahs without sitting after two).
4
Analyze the evidence
Sahibayn cite the hadith 'What you have missed, complete' – completing the imam's prayer, which is Jumu'ah. Muhammad analogizes to other prayers where catching a rak'ah is needed.
Sahibayn argue Jumu'ah is legislated contrary to analogy (khilaf al-qiyas), so special rules apply.
5
Determine the practical difference (thamarah)
If one catches only tashahhud: under Sahibayn, he prays 4 rak'ahs as Jumu'ah, sitting after two. Under Muhammad, he completes 4 rak'ahs as Zuhr (no sitting after two).
The mufta bihi is the view of Sahibayn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (أو في سجود السهو) إن قيل: إن هذا يشعر بأنه يسجد للسهو في الجمعة، والعيد، وهو خلاف المختار أجيب بأن المختار عدم الوجوب فيهما وإن الأولى تركه لئلا يقع الناس في فتنة لا أن المختار عدم جوازه أفاده في الإيضاح . قوله : (وما فاتكم فاقضوا فإن معناه أقضوا ما فاتكم من صلاة الإمام والذي من صلاة الإمام هو الجمعة، وهو يدل على ما في قوله : لما روينا. قوله: (وإلا أتم ظهراً) لأنه أدرك معه أقلها فلا يعتبر بالكل من وجه وحاصله أنه بإدراك الأقل تصير جمعة . وجه باعتبار ما وجد من الشرائط فيما أدرك كالتحريمة والجماعة، والإمام وظهرا من وجه لفوات بعض الشروط فيما يقضي، وهو الجماعة، والإمام وهي مشروعة على خلاف القياس قيراعى فيه جميع الخصوصيات فبالنظر لكونها ظهراً يصلي أربعاً، وبالنظر لكونها جمعة يتحتم أن يقعد على رأس الركعتين ويقرأ في جميع الركعات لاحتمال النفلية.
His saying: (or in the prostration of forgetfulness) If it is said: This indicates that he performs prostration of forgetfulness in Jumu'ah and 'Eid, which is contrary to the chosen view. It is answered that the chosen view is that it is not obligatory in both, and it is better to leave it so that people do not fall into fitna; it is not that it is not permissible, as is stated in al-Idah. His saying: (And what you have missed, complete) for its meaning is: complete what you have missed of the imam's prayer, and what is from the imam's prayer is Jumu'ah, and it indicates what is in his saying: as we narrated. His saying: (Otherwise he completes it as Zuhr) because he caught with him the lesser part of it, so it is not considered from all aspects. The summary is that by catching the lesser part it becomes Jumu'ah from one aspect (due to the presence of conditions like the opening takbir, congregation, and imam in what he caught) and Zuhr from another aspect (due to the lack of some conditions in what he completes, namely congregation and imam). And since it is legislated contrary to analogy, all specific considerations are observed: from the perspective that it is Zuhr, he prays four; from the perspective that it is Jumu'ah, it is necessary that he sits after two rak'ahs and recites in all rak'ahs due to the possibility of it being a supererogatory prayer.
Source pages p. 522

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling for a person who catches part of the Jumu'ah prayer. The commentary begins by clarifying a point about prostration of forgetfulness (sajda sahw) in Jumu'ah: it is not obligatory but permissible, though the better view is to avoid it to prevent confusion. Then it discusses the meaning of the hadith 'what you have missed, complete'—meaning complete the prayer after the imam's salaam. The dispute between the two companions (Sahibayn) and Muhammad al-Shaybani is implicit: Sahibayn hold that if one catches any part of the Jumu'ah prayer (even in tashahhud or sajda sahw), it counts as a valid Jumu'ah prayer, and he should complete it as Jumu'ah (praying four rak'ahs, sitting after two). Muhammad holds that one must catch the imam before he raises his head from the second rak'ah; otherwise, he completes it as Zuhr. The commentary explains that since Jumu'ah is legislated contrary to analogy, special considerations apply: the prayer is considered Jumu'ah in terms of the conditions present (takbeer, congregation, imam) and Zuhr in terms of what is completed (missing congregation and imam). Thus, one prays four rak'ahs but sits after the first two, and recites in all rak'ahs. The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that of Sahibayn.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujūd al-sahw): Prostration for forgetfulness during prayer.
أقلها (aqalluhā): The lesser part of the prayer, i.e., at least one rak'ah or part.
النفلية (al-nafliyya): Supererogatory prayer; here indicating the possibility that one's completion could be nafl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (Sahibayn), if a person joins the Jumu'ah prayer only in the final tashahhud, what should he do?
A) He should pray four rak'ahs as Zuhr.
B) He should pray four rak'ahs as Jumu'ah, sitting after two rak'ahs.
C) He should pray two rak'ahs as Jumu'ah.
D) He should leave, as his prayer is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi view is that catching any part of Jumu'ah, even tashahhud or sajda sahw, suffices for it to count as Jumu'ah, and the latecomer prays four rak'ahs sitting after two.

The Recommended Acts of Jumu'ah: Ghusl, Oil, and Perfume
Ruling on recommended acts for Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ghusl for Jumu'ah and explain the preference for wudu and ghusl, and identify the recommended use of oil and perfume.

Core Idea
Ghusl is recommended but not obligatory for Jumu'ah; wudu is acceptable but ghusl is better.

The passage clarifies the recommended (sunnah) acts for Jumu'ah. While ghusl is strongly encouraged, one may perform wudu instead. It also emphasizes applying oil (especially olive oil in hot climates) and perfume. The commentary provides a nuanced interpretation of the text, showing the flexibility within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts
Read the base text listing the etiquettes: ghusl, wudu, oil, perfume, and not separating pairs.
2
Determine the legal status
From the commentary, note that ghusl is 'ahabb' (more beloved) than wudu, meaning it is sunnah mu'akkadah.
The waw is interpreted as 'or' indicating an option.
3
Analyze the dalil for ghusl
The hadith 'Whoever performs wudu on Friday, it is good, and whoever performs ghusl, then ghusl is better' is cited as proof.
This shows the preference.
4
Examine the oil recommendation
The text recommends oil, especially olive oil in hot climates, based on a hadith.
The hadith 'Eat olive oil and anoint yourselves with it' is referenced.
5
Understand the perfume ruling
Men should use men's perfume; if unavailable, they may use women's perfume that has scent but no color.

Source Text

ويتخير في الجهر والإخفاء وقال : لا يغتسل رجل يوم الجمعة، ويتطهر ما استطاع من طهره ويدهن من دهنه، ويمس من طيب بيته ثم يخرج فلا يفرق بين اثنين ثم يصلي ما كتب أن يقعد على رأس الركعتين ويقرأ في جميع الركعات لاحتمال النفلية. قوله: (ويتطهر) لعل الواو بمعنى أو ويكون المراد به الوضوء لما . ورد ما معناه من توضأ . يوم الجمعة فيها ونعمت ومن اغتسل، فالغسل أحب . قوله : ويدهن من دهنه لعل المراد به نحو الزيت فانه مأمور به في البلاد الحارة كما يدل عليه حديث كلوا الزيت وادهنوا به قوله (ويمس من طيب بيته) الموجود فيه أو المرد إن لم يجد طيب الرجال يمس من طيب أهله مما له رائحة لا لون كمسك وكافور . قوله: (فلا يفرق بين اثنين أفاد بهذا النهي عنه قال : من تخطى رقاب الناس اتخذ جسراً إلى جهنم وعن ابن عمر قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : يحضر الجمعة ثلاثة نفر رجل حضرها يلغو فهو حظه منها ورجل حضرها يدعو فهو رجل دعا الله عز وجل إن شاء أعطاه وإن شاء منعه، ورجل حضرها بإنصات وسكوت ولم يتخط رقبة مسلم ولم يؤذ أحداً فهو كفارة إلى الجمعة التي تليها، وزيادة ثلاثة أيام وذلك بأن الله تعالى يقول من جاء بالحسنة فله عشر أمثالها قال الحلبي : وينبغي أن يقيد النهي عن التخطي بما إذا وجد بدأ أما إذا لم يجد بدأ بأن لم يكن في الوراء موضع وفي المقدم موضع فله أن يتخطى اليه للضرورة، وفي الخلاصة : إذا دخل الرجل الجامع، وهو ملآن إن كان تخطيه يؤذي الناس لم يتخط، وإن كان لا يؤذي أحداً بأن لا يطأ ثوباً، ولا جسداً فلا بأس أن يتخطى، ويدنو من الإمام، وروى الفقيه أبو جعفر عن أصحابنا أنه لا بأس بالتخطي ما لم يخرج الإمام، أو يؤذي أحداً اهـ، وحاصله أن التخطي جائز بشرطين عدم الإيذاء وعدم خروج الإمام لأن الإيذاء حرام والتخطية عمل وهو بعد خروج الإمام حرام، فلا يرتكبه لفضيلة الدنو من الإمام، بل يستقر في موضعه من المسجد، وما ذكره في البحر وغيره من أن من وجد فرجة في المقدم له أن يخرق الثاني لأنه لا حرمة لهم لتقصيرهم يحمل على الضرورة، أو على عدم الإيذاء أو على الاستئذان قبل خروج الإمام جمعاً بين الروايات، ومن زحزح رجلين وجلس بينهما مع ضيق الموضع دخل في النهي عن التفرقة بين اثنين، وفي البحر، وأما التخطي للسؤال فمكروه في جميع الأحوال بالإجماع، ويكره أشد كراهة أن يقيم الرجل أخاه فيجلس في موضعه في الجمعة وغيرها، قال الكرماني، وظاهر النهي الوارد فيه التحريم لأن من سبق إلى مباح فهو أحق به بخلاف ما لو قام الجالس باختياره، وأجلس غيره فلا كراهة في جلوس غيره لكن ان انتقل القائم إلى مكان أقرب لسماع الخطبة، فلا بأس وإن انتقل إلى دونه كره ولو اثر شخصاً بمكانه لم يجر لغيره ان يسبقه إليه لأن الحق للجالس اثر به غيره فقام مقامه في استحقاقه، ولو بعث من يقعد له في مكانه عنه إذا جاء هو حاز أيضاً من غير كراهة ولو فرش له نحو سجادة ففيه وجهان فقيل: يجوز لغيره تنحيتها والجلوس في موضعها لأن السبق بالأجسام لا بما يفرش ولا يجوز الجلوس عليها
And he is given the choice between jahr and ikhfa, and he said: A man should not perform ghusl on Friday, but he should perform wudu as much as he can from his purity, and anoint himself with his oil, and apply perfume from his house's perfume, then go out, and he should not separate between two people, then he should pray what is prescribed. That he should sit after two rak'ahs and recite in all rak'ahs due to the possibility of it being supererogatory. His saying: (and he performs wudu) perhaps the waw is meant as 'or' and the intent is wudu, as is narrated that whoever performs wudu on Friday, it is good, and whoever performs ghusl, then ghusl is better. His saying: 'and anoints himself with his oil' perhaps meaning olive oil, for it is commanded in hot lands as indicated by the hadith 'Eat olive oil and anoint yourselves with it.' His saying: 'and applies perfume from his house's perfume' that which is present, or if he cannot find men's perfume, he applies from his family's perfume, such as musk and camphor, which have scent but no color. His saying: 'so he does not separate between two people' he specifies the prohibition of it. He said: Whoever steps over the necks of people, he will make a bridge to hell. And from Ibn Umar: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: Three types of people attend Friday: a man who attends and engages in idle talk, so his share is that; a man who attends and prays, so he is a man who called upon Allah, if He wills He gives him and if He wills He prevents him; and a man who attends with attentiveness and silence, and does not step over the neck of a Muslim and does not harm anyone, so it becomes an expiation until the next Friday, plus three days, because Allah says: Whoever brings a good deed will have ten times the like thereof. Al-Halabi said: The prohibition of stepping should be restricted to when there is an alternative; but if there is no alternative, such that there is no place in the back and there is a spot in the front, then he may step over to it out of necessity. In al-Khulasa: If a man enters the mosque and it is full, if his stepping harms people, he should not step; if he does not harm anyone, such as not stepping on any garment or body, then there is no harm in stepping to get closer to the imam. Abu Ja'far narrated from our companions that there is no harm in stepping as long as the imam has not come out or he does not harm anyone. The summary is that stepping is permissible with two conditions: no harm and before the imam comes out, because harm is haram and stepping is an action, and after the imam comes out it is haram, so one should not commit it for the virtue of being close to the imam; rather, he stays in his place in the mosque. What is mentioned in al-Bahr and others that whoever finds a gap in the front may proceed to it because others have no sanctity due to their negligence, this is interpreted as necessity, or no harm, or seeking permission before the imam comes out, to reconcile the narrations. And whoever moves two people apart and sits between them when the space is tight falls under the prohibition of separating between two people. In al-Bahr: As for stepping for begging, it is disliked in all cases by consensus. It is severely disliked for a man to make his brother stand and sit in his place, especially on Friday and other days. Al-Kirmani said: The apparent prohibition in that is prohibition, because whoever precedes to a permissible thing has more right to it. But if the sitting person stands voluntarily and seats another, there is no dislike in that person sitting. However, if the one who stands moves to a place closer to hearing the sermon, there is no harm; if he moves to a place further away, it is disliked. And if a person gives his place to someone, it is not permissible for another to take it before him, because the right is for the one who gave his place to the other, so the other takes his place in entitlement. And if one sends someone to sit in his place until he comes, it is also permissible without dislike. And if one spreads a prayer mat, there are two opinions: some say it is permissible for another to remove it and sit in its place because precedence is by bodies not by what is spread, and some say it is not permissible to sit on it.
Source pages p. 523

Commentary
This passage discusses the etiquettes and rulings related to Friday prayer. It begins with a discussion of the recommended actions: ghusl (full bath) is better but wudu is sufficient; the use of oil and perfume is recommended. The hadith encourages using olive oil in hot climates. Then it discusses the prohibition of stepping over people's necks and separating between two seated individuals, citing serious warnings from the Prophet (peace be upon him). The commentary details exceptions: stepping is permissible if there is no alternative, if it does not harm anyone, and before the imam comes out. After the imam comes out, stepping is prohibited because the sermon has started. The passage also covers rulings on moving people from their seats, giving place to others, and spreading prayer mats. The general principle is that the first person to reach a spot has more right to it, but there are exceptions for necessity and for moving to a better position for hearing the sermon. Overall, the emphasis is on maintaining harmony and avoiding disturbance during the Jumu'ah prayer.

Key Terms
الاغتسال (al-ightisāl): The full ritual bath.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as explained in the passage, what is the status of ghusl on Friday?
A) Wajib
B) Sunnah mu'akkadah
C) Mubah
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
Ghusl for Jumu'ah is a strongly recommended sunnah, not an obligation; wudu is sufficient.

The Prohibition of Stepping Over Necks and Separating Pairs on Jumu'ah
Ruling on stepping over necks and separating pairs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on stepping over necks and separating pairs during Jumu'ah and identify the conditions under which stepping becomes permissible.

Core Idea
Stepping over necks is generally prohibited but allowed if it causes no harm and before the imam enters.

The passage delves into the prohibition of stepping over the necks of congregants and separating two seated individuals. It cites severe warnings from the Prophet, but also provides exceptions, such as when there is no alternative and before the imam begins the sermon. The commentary reconciles various reports to give a balanced ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited act
The base text prohibits separating between two seated people and stepping over necks. The commentary expands on this prohibition.
The prohibition is explicit in the hadith.
2
Analyze the dalil
Two hadith are cited: one warning that whoever steps over necks makes a bridge to hell, and another listing three types of attendees, emphasizing silence and not stepping over necks.
The second hadith also mentions expiation for those who follow etiquettes.
3
Recognize the exceptions
Al-Halabi and al-Khulasa state conditions: stepping is permissible if no harm and before the imam comes out. After imam's entry, it is prohibited.
Even when allowed, one should not harm others.
4
Apply to related scenarios
The passage also covers moving people from their seats, giving place, and spreading mats. The ruling is based on priority to the first comer.
5
Understand the consensus
Stepping for begging is disliked in all cases by consensus.

D) It is permissible only during the sermon

Key Takeaway
Stepping over necks is generally prohibited but becomes permissible if it causes no harm and is done before the imam begins the sermon.

Salah — Prayer
beginner

Friday Etiquette: Ghusl, Adornment, and the Reward of Silence
Explains Friday sunan and the hadith of three types of attendees

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Friday ghusl and explain why silence and avoiding stepping over are necessary for complete reward.

Core Idea
Ghusl is sunnah muakkadah; the Friday reward requires silence, no harm, and no stepping over.

This lesson examines the recommended acts for Friday as outlined in the Hanafi school. We will learn the ruling on ghusl, the use of oil and perfume, and the important hadith of three types of Friday attendees, which teaches that the full expiation for sins is only achieved through silence and proper conduct.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended acts
List the acts mentioned: ghusl, wudu, oiling, perfuming, avoiding separation between two people, and praying as much as possible.
These are sunnah muakkadah or mustahabb.
2
Understand the Hanafi ruling on ghusl
Distinguish between wudu and ghusl: wudu is sufficient, but ghusl is more beloved (sunnah muakkadah).
The text clarifies that the waw in 'yatatahhar' may mean 'or'.
3
Analyze the hadith of three types
Read the hadith from Ibn 'Umar: three categories of attendees. Note that the one who listens silently, does not step over necks, and does not harm anyone receives expiation until the next Friday plus three days.
This hadith is the proof for the prohibition of stepping over and idle talk.
4
Connect the acts to the reward
Understand that the recommended acts (ghusl, etc.) are virtuous, but the expiation is contingent on proper behavior during the khutbah and prayer.
The hadith shows that idle talk (laghw) reduces reward to nothing.

الركعات لاحتمال النفلية. قوله: (ويتطهر) لعل الواو بمعنى أو ويكون المراد به الوضوء لما . ورد ما معناه من توضأ . يوم الجمعة فيها ونعمت ومن اغتسل، فالغسل أحب . قوله : ويدهن من دهنه لعل المراد به نحو الزيت فانه مأمور به في البلاد الحارة كما يدل عليه حديث كلوا الزيت وادهنوا به قوله (ويمس من طيب بيته) الموجود فيه أو المرد إن لم يجد طيب الرجال يمس من طيب أهله مما له رائحة لا لون كمسك وكافور . قوله: (فلا يفرق بين اثنين أفاد بهذا النهي عنه قال : من تخطى رقاب الناس اتخذ جسراً إلى جهنم وعن ابن عمر قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : يحضر الجمعة ثلاثة نفر رجل حضرها يلغو فهو حظه منها ورجل حضرها يدعو فهو رجل دعا الله عز وجل إن شاء أعطاه وإن شاء منعه، ورجل حضرها بإنصات وسكوت ولم يتخط رقبة مسلم ولم يؤذ أحداً فهو كفارة إلى الجمعة التي تليها، وزيادة ثلاثة أيام وذلك بأن الله تعالى يقول من جاء بالحسنة فله عشر أمثالها قال الحلبي : وينبغي أن يقيد النهي عن التخطي بما إذا وجد بدأ أما إذا لم يجد بدأ بأن لم يكن في الوراء موضع وفي المقدم موضع فله أن يتخطى اليه للضرورة، وفي الخلاصة : إذا دخل الرجل الجامع، وهو ملآن إن كان تخطيه يؤذي الناس لم يتخط، وإن كان لا يؤذي أحداً بأن لا يطأ ثوباً، ولا جسداً فلا بأس أن يتخطى، ويدنو من الإمام، وروى الفقيه أبو جعفر عن أصحابنا أنه لا بأس بالتخطي ما لم يخرج الإمام، أو يؤذي أحداً اهـ، وحاصله أن التخطي جائز بشرطين عدم الإيذاء وعدم خروج الإمام لأن الإيذاء حرام والتخطية عمل وهو بعد خروج الإمام حرام، فلا يرتكبه لفضيلة الدنو من الإمام، بل يستقر في موضعه من المسجد، وما ذكره في البحر وغيره من أن من وجد فرجة في المقدم له أن يخرق الثاني لأنه لا حرمة لهم لتقصيرهم يحمل على الضرورة، أو على عدم الإيذاء أو على الاستئذان قبل خروج الإمام جمعاً بين الروايات، ومن زحزح رجلين وجلس بينهما مع ضيق الموضع دخل في النهي عن التفرقة بين اثنين، وفي البحر، وأما التخطي للسؤال فمكروه في جميع الأحوال بالإجماع، ويكره أشد كراهة أن يقيم الرجل أخاه فيجلس في موضعه في الجمعة وغيرها، قال الكرماني، وظاهر النهي الوارد فيه التحريم لأن من سبق إلى مباح فهو أحق به بخلاف ما لو قام الجالس باختياره، وأجلس غيره فلا كراهة في جلوس غيره لكن ان انتقل القائم إلى مكان أقرب لسماع الخطبة، فلا بأس وإن انتقل إلى دونه كره ولو اثر شخصاً بمكانه لم يجر لغيره ان يسبقه إليه لأن الحق للجالس اثر به غيره فقام مقامه في استحقاقه، ولو بعث من يقعد له في مكانه عنه إذا جاء هو حاز أيضاً من غير كراهة ولو فرش له نحو سجادة ففيه وجهان فقيل: يجوز لغيره تنحيتها والجلوس في موضعها لأن السبق بالأجسام لا بما يفرش ولا يجوز الجلوس عليها له ثم يسكت إذا تكلم الخطيب إلا غفر له ما بينه وبين الجمعة الأخرى» رواه البخاري يعصمهم من عذاب القبر، المؤذن والشهيد والمتوفى ليلة الجمعة لكن ذكر ابن وهبان أنه لا بأس به وأشار إليه بقوله ومن شاء تنويراً فقالوا : ينوّر. وقال : ثلاثة من يعصمهم الله) أي يحفظهم الله تعالى. قوله : (المؤذن) ظاهره ولو غير محتسب قوله (والشهيد) ظاهره ولو شهيد آخرة فقط . قوله: (والمتوفى ليلة الجمعة) قال أبو المعين في أصوله : قال أهل السنة والجماعة عذاب القبر وسؤال منكر ونكير حق لكن إن كان كافراً فعذابه يدوم في القبر إلى يوم القيامة، ويرفع عنهم العذاب الجمعة وشهر رمضان الحرمة النبي الله ، ثم المؤمن على ضر بين ا مطيعاً لا يكون له عذاب القبر ويكون له ضغطة فيجد هول ذلك، وخوفه لما أنه كان يتنعم بنعمة الله تعالى، ولم يشكر النعمة وإن كان عاصياً يكون له عذاب وضغطة القبر لكن ينقطع عنه العذاب يوم الجمعة وليلة الجمعة ولا يعود العذاب إلى يوم القيامة وإن مات ليلة الجمعة يكون له العذاب ساعة واحدة، وضغطة، ثم ينقطع. عنه العذاب ولا يوم أن كان الجمعة، أو يوم يعود إلى يوم القيامة من مجمع الروايات والتتارخانية كذا في الشرح وناقش فيه المنلا علي وقال : إن ذلك غير ثابت في الأحاديث .
He chooses between loud and quiet recitation, and he said: A man should bathe on Friday, and perform wudu as much as he can, and oil himself with his oil, and apply perfume from his house, then go out, and not separate between two people, then pray as much as is written. That he sits at the end of two rak'ahs and recites in all rak'ahs due to the possibility of it being supererogatory. His saying: 'and performs wudu' – perhaps the waw is in the sense of 'or' and what is meant is wudu, because it has been reported meaning: whoever performs wudu on Friday has done well and done a good deed, and whoever bathes, then bathing is more beloved. His saying: 'and oils himself with his oil' – perhaps what is meant is something like olive oil, for it is commanded in hot countries as indicated by the hadith: 'Eat olive oil and anoint yourselves with it.' His saying: 'and applies perfume from his house' – what is available in his house or what his wife uses, if he cannot find men's perfume, he applies perfume from his family's perfume that has a scent but no color, like musk and camphor. His saying: 'then he does not separate between two people' – he indicated by this the prohibition of it. He said: Whoever steps over the necks of people makes a bridge to Hell. And from Ibn 'Umar: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'Three persons attend Friday: a man who attends and engages in idle talk – that is his share; a man who attends and supplicates – he is a man who calls upon Allah; if He wills He gives him, if He wills He prevents him; and a man who attends with attentiveness and silence, and does not step over the neck of a Muslim, and does not harm anyone – it is an expiation for the following Friday and an increase of three days.' That is because Allah says: 'Whoever comes with a good deed shall have ten times its like.' Al-Halabi said: The prohibition of stepping over should be restricted to when one finds a space. But if he does not find a space – i.e., there is no place behind and there is a place in front – then he may step over out of necessity. In al-Khulasa: If a man enters the mosque and it is full, if his stepping over harms people he should not step over; if it does not harm anyone – meaning he does not step on clothing or a body – then there is no harm in stepping over and approaching the imam. Al-Faqih Abu Ja'far reported from our companions that there is no harm in stepping over as long as the imam has not come out or he harms someone. The summary is that stepping over is permissible with two conditions: no harm and that the imam has not come out, because harming is forbidden and stepping over is an action, and it is forbidden after the imam has come out, so one should not commit it for the virtue of nearing the imam, but rather he stays in his place in the mosque. What is mentioned in al-Bahr and elsewhere, that whoever finds a gap in the front may split the [rows] because they have no sanctity due to their negligence, is interpreted as necessity, or as not causing harm, or as seeking permission before the imam comes out, to reconcile the narrations. Whoever displaces two men and sits between them when the place is narrow falls under the prohibition of separating between two. In al-Bahr: Stepping over for the purpose of begging is disliked in all cases by consensus. It is more severely disliked that a man makes his brother stand up and sits in his place on Friday and other days. Al-Kirmani said: The apparent meaning of the prohibition is that it is unlawful because whoever precedes to a permissible thing has more right to it, unlike if the sitter stands up by his choice and seats someone else, then there is no dislike in the other sitting. But if the one who stands moves to a place closer to hear the sermon, then there is no harm; if he moves to a place farther, it is disliked. If he designates someone for his place, another may not precede him to it because the right belongs to the sitter, and he designated another, so that other takes his place in deserving it. If he sends someone to sit in his place for him, when he comes he also acquires it without dislike. If he spreads a prayer mat or the like for himself, there are two opinions: It is said that another may remove it and sit in its place because precedence is by bodies not by what is spread, and it is not permissible to sit on it without his consent. However, he should not lift it with his hand or otherwise lest he become liable. It is also said that he may not remove it because it might lead to dispute and because he has preceded to it with a stone, so it becomes like dead land. It is permissible to make a man stand in three cases: when he sits in the imam's place, or in a path that prevents people from passing, or in front of the row, as in al-'Ayni on al-Bukhari and others. His saying: 'except that it is forgiven for him what is between him and the next Friday' – meaning the past or the future, and forgiveness applies to the future as it does to the past. Ibn Hibban added from the hadith of Abu Huraira: 'and an increase of three days after it.' His saying: 'Allah protects them' – i.e., Allah preserves them. His saying: 'the mu'adhdhin' – apparently even if he is not a volunteer. His saying: 'the martyr' – apparently even if he is a martyr of the Hereafter only. His saying: 'the one who dies on Friday night' – Abu al-Mu'in said in his Usul: Ahl al-Sunnah wal-Jama'ah hold that the punishment of the grave and the questioning of Munkar and Nakir are true. But if he is a disbeliever, his punishment continues in the grave until the Day of Resurrection, and the punishment is lifted from them on Friday and the month of Ramadan due to the sanctity of the Prophet ﷺ. Then concerning the believer: if he is obedient, he will not have punishment of the grave, but he will have pressure and find its horror and fear because he was enjoying Allah's blessings and did not thank for the blessing; if he is disobedient, he will have punishment and pressure of the grave, but the punishment is cut off from him on Friday and Friday night, and the punishment does not return until the Day of Resurrection. If he dies on Friday night, he will have punishment for one hour and pressure, then the punishment is cut off and does not return. This is from Majma' al-Riwayat and al-Tatarakhaniyya, as in the sharh. And Mullah 'Ali discussed it and said: That is not established in the hadith.
Source pages p. 523

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya explains the recommended acts for Friday and the prohibition of stepping over people. The author begins with the matn stating that one should bathe, perform wudu, oil, apply perfume, then go out and not separate between two people. The commentary clarifies that 'wudu' is sufficient but ghusl is better. Oiling with olive oil is recommended for hot countries. Perfume should be from one's own home, using women's perfume if necessary. The prohibition of stepping over necks is emphasized with a hadith about three types of Friday attendees, showing that stepping over and idle talk reduce reward. The commentator then details when stepping over is permissible: if there is no space behind and a gap ahead, and if one does not harm others or the imam has not yet come out. Displacing two people to sit between them is also prohibited. Making someone stand and taking his seat is severely disliked, except in three cases: sitting in the imam's place, blocking a path, or in front of the row. The passage concludes with a discussion on those protected from grave punishment: the mu'adhdhin, martyr, and one who dies on Friday night. However, Mullah 'Ali notes that this protection is not established in authentic hadiths.

Key Terms
الغسل (al-ghusl): Full body wash, specifically recommended for Friday.
التخطي (al-takhatti): Stepping over the shoulders or necks of seated people in the mosque.
الجمعة (al-jumu'ah): Friday congregational prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith in this lesson, which person receives expiation until the next Friday and three extra days?
A) The one who makes many supplications.
B) The one who arrives early and sits in the front.
C) The one who listens silently, does not step over necks, and does not harm anyone.
D) The one who performs ghusl and wears perfume.

Key Takeaway
Friday ghusl is sunnah muakkadah; the full reward requires silence, no stepping over, and no harm.

Stepping Over in the Mosque: Prohibition, Permissibility, and Related Rulings
Detailed analysis of stepping over with conditions and related rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the conditions for permissible stepping over in the mosque on Friday and distinguish between prohibited, permissible, and disliked cases.

Core Idea
Stepping over is prohibited when it harms others or after the imam has come out; permissible only without harm and with space ahead.

This lesson delves into the detailed fiqh of stepping over (takhatti) during Friday congregational prayer. The passage presents the general prohibition, then refines it with conditions from later Hanafi authorities, and also covers related issues like displacing people, making someone stand, and the reward for proper conduct.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling on stepping over
The hadith of Ibn 'Umar prohibits stepping over necks and ties expiation to avoiding it. The text begins with a strong warning: 'Whoever steps over necks makes a bridge to Hell.'
This is the basic prohibition.
2
Understand the exceptions from later jurists
Al-Halabi restricts the prohibition to when one finds a space. If there is no space behind and a gap ahead, stepping over is permissible out of necessity.
Al-Khulasa adds the condition of no harm and the imam not having come out.
3
Analyze the two conditions for permissibility
The summary from the text: stepping over is permissible with two conditions – no harm and the imam has not yet come out. Harm includes stepping on clothing or bodies.
After the imam appears, stepping over is forbidden because it is an action that distracts.
4
Differentiate between types of stepping over
Stepping over for begging is always disliked (makruh). Making someone stand to take their seat is severely disliked, except in three specific cases: sitting in the imam's place, blocking a path, or sitting in front of the row.
These exceptions show that the ruling is nuanced.
5
Note the discussion on grave punishment
The passage ends with a discussion on those protected from grave punishment (mu'adhdhin, martyr, one who dies Friday night), but Mullah 'Ali notes this is not established in hadith.
This is a tangential point but shows the commentator's critical approach.
