قوله : (المؤذن) ظاهره ولو غير محتسب قوله (والشهيد) ظاهره ولو شهيد آخرة فقط . قوله: (والمتوفى ليلة الجمعة) قال أبو المعين في أصوله : قال أهل السنة والجماعة عذاب القبر وسؤال منكر ونكير حق لكن إن كان كافراً فعذابه يدوم في القبر إلى يوم القيامة، ويرفع عنهم العذاب الجمعة وشهر رمضان الحرمة النبي الله ، ثم المؤمن على ضر بين ا مطيعاً لا يكون له عذاب القبر ويكون له ضغطة فيجد هول ذلك، وخوفه لما أنه كان يتنعم بنعمة الله تعالى، ولم يشكر النعمة وإن كان عاصياً يكون له عذاب وضغطة القبر لكن ينقطع عنه العذاب يوم الجمعة وليلة الجمعة ولا يعود العذاب إلى يوم القيامة وإن مات ليلة الجمعة يكون له العذاب ساعة واحدة، وضغطة، ثم ينقطع. عنه العذاب ولا يوم أن كان الجمعة، أو يوم يعود إلى يوم القيامة من مجمع الروايات والتتارخانية كذا في الشرح وناقش فيه المنلا علي وقال : إن ذلك غير ثابت في الأحاديث .
He chooses between loud and quiet recitation, and he said: A man should bathe on Friday, and perform wudu as much as he can, and oil himself with his oil, and apply perfume from his house, then go out, and not separate between two people, then pray as much as is written. That he sits at the end of two rak'ahs and recites in all rak'ahs due to the possibility of it being supererogatory. His saying: 'and performs wudu' – perhaps the waw is in the sense of 'or' and what is meant is wudu, because it has been reported meaning: whoever performs wudu on Friday has done well and done a good deed, and whoever bathes, then bathing is more beloved. His saying: 'and oils himself with his oil' – perhaps what is meant is something like olive oil, for it is commanded in hot countries as indicated by the hadith: 'Eat olive oil and anoint yourselves with it.' His saying: 'and applies perfume from his house' – what is available in his house or what his wife uses, if he cannot find men's perfume, he applies perfume from his family's perfume that has a scent but no color, like musk and camphor. His saying: 'then he does not separate between two people' – he indicated by this the prohibition of it. He said: Whoever steps over the necks of people makes a bridge to Hell. And from Ibn 'Umar: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'Three persons attend Friday: a man who attends and engages in idle talk – that is his share; a man who attends and supplicates – he is a man who calls upon Allah; if He wills He gives him, if He wills He prevents him; and a man who attends with attentiveness and silence, and does not step over the neck of a Muslim, and does not harm anyone – it is an expiation for the following Friday and an increase of three days.' That is because Allah says: 'Whoever comes with a good deed shall have ten times its like.' Al-Halabi said: The prohibition of stepping over should be restricted to when one finds a space. But if he does not find a space – i.e., there is no place behind and there is a place in front – then he may step over out of necessity. In al-Khulasa: If a man enters the mosque and it is full, if his stepping over harms people he should not step over; if it does not harm anyone – meaning he does not step on clothing or a body – then there is no harm in stepping over and approaching the imam. Al-Faqih Abu Ja'far reported from our companions that there is no harm in stepping over as long as the imam has not come out or he harms someone. The summary is that stepping over is permissible with two conditions: no harm and that the imam has not come out, because harming is forbidden and stepping over is an action, and it is forbidden after the imam has come out, so one should not commit it for the virtue of nearing the imam, but rather he stays in his place in the mosque. What is mentioned in al-Bahr and elsewhere, that whoever finds a gap in the front may split the [rows] because they have no sanctity due to their negligence, is interpreted as necessity, or as not causing harm, or as seeking permission before the imam comes out, to reconcile the narrations. Whoever displaces two men and sits between them when the place is narrow falls under the prohibition of separating between two. In al-Bahr: Stepping over for the purpose of begging is disliked in all cases by consensus. It is more severely disliked that a man makes his brother stand up and sits in his place on Friday and other days. Al-Kirmani said: The apparent meaning of the prohibition is that it is unlawful because whoever precedes to a permissible thing has more right to it, unlike if the sitter stands up by his choice and seats someone else, then there is no dislike in the other sitting. But if the one who stands moves to a place closer to hear the sermon, then there is no harm; if he moves to a place farther, it is disliked. If he designates someone for his place, another may not precede him to it because the right belongs to the sitter, and he designated another, so that other takes his place in deserving it. If he sends someone to sit in his place for him, when he comes he also acquires it without dislike. If he spreads a prayer mat or the like for himself, there are two opinions: It is said that another may remove it and sit in its place because precedence is by bodies not by what is spread, and it is not permissible to sit on it without his consent. However, he should not lift it with his hand or otherwise lest he become liable. It is also said that he may not remove it because it might lead to dispute and because he has preceded to it with a stone, so it becomes like dead land. It is permissible to make a man stand in three cases: when he sits in the imam's place, or in a path that prevents people from passing, or in front of the row, as in al-'Ayni on al-Bukhari and others. His saying: 'except that it is forgiven for him what is between him and the next Friday' – meaning the past or the future, and forgiveness applies to the future as it does to the past. Ibn Hibban added from the hadith of Abu Huraira: 'and an increase of three days after it.' His saying: 'Allah protects them' – i.e., Allah preserves them. His saying: 'the mu'adhdhin' – apparently even if he is not a volunteer. His saying: 'the martyr' – apparently even if he is a martyr of the Hereafter only. His saying: 'the one who dies on Friday night' – Abu al-Mu'in said in his Usul: Ahl al-Sunnah wal-Jama'ah hold that the punishment of the grave and the questioning of Munkar and Nakir are true. But if he is a disbeliever, his punishment continues in the grave until the Day of Resurrection, and the punishment is lifted from them on Friday and the month of Ramadan due to the sanctity of the Prophet ﷺ. Then concerning the believer: if he is obedient, he will not have punishment of the grave, but he will have pressure and find its horror and fear because he was enjoying Allah's blessings and did not thank for the blessing; if he is disobedient, he will have punishment and pressure of the grave, but the punishment is cut off from him on Friday and Friday night, and the punishment does not return until the Day of Resurrection. If he dies on Friday night, he will have punishment for one hour and pressure, then the punishment is cut off and does not return. This is from Majma' al-Riwayat and al-Tatarakhaniyya, as in the sharh. And Mullah 'Ali discussed it and said: That is not established in the hadith.
Source pages p. 523

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya explains the recommended acts for Friday and the prohibition of stepping over people. The author begins with the matn stating that one should bathe, perform wudu, oil, apply perfume, then go out and not separate between two people. The commentary clarifies that 'wudu' is sufficient but ghusl is better. Oiling with olive oil is recommended for hot countries. Perfume should be from one's own home, using women's perfume if necessary. The prohibition of stepping over necks is emphasized with a hadith about three types of Friday attendees, showing that stepping over and idle talk reduce reward. The commentator then details when stepping over is permissible: if there is no space behind and a gap ahead, and if one does not harm others or the imam has not yet come out. Displacing two people to sit between them is also prohibited. Making someone stand and taking his seat is severely disliked, except in three cases: sitting in the imam's place, blocking a path, or in front of the row. The passage concludes with a discussion on those protected from grave punishment: the mu'adhdhin, martyr, and one who dies on Friday night. However, Mullah 'Ali notes that this protection is not established in authentic hadiths.

Key Terms
التخطي (al-takhatti): Stepping over the shoulders or necks of seated people in the mosque.
الإمام (al-imam): The prayer leader; in the context of Friday, the one who delivers the khutbah and leads the salah.
المكروه تحريماً (makruh tahrimi): Disliked to the point of prohibition; an act that is prohibited by a speculative proof but not definitively.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is stepping over (takhatti) in the mosque on Friday permissible?
A) Always permissible if you are in a hurry.
B) Permissible only if you do not harm anyone and the imam has not yet come out.
C) Permissible only after the imam has finished the khutbah.
D) Never permissible.

Key Takeaway
Stepping over is prohibited when harmful or after the imam appears; permissible with necessity and no harm before the imam.

Salah — Prayer

Eid Prayer is Wajib: The Hanafi Ruling and Its Proof
Definition of Eid and ruling on Eid prayer as wajib.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Eid prayer (wajib) and explain the proof and the distinction from fard.

Core Idea
Eid prayer is wajib, not fard, because its evidence is zanni in transmission.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi establishes the Hanafi position that Eid prayer is wajib (obligatory) but not fard. The author clarifies the legal basis, explains the etymology of 'Eid, and connects the chapter to Jumu'ah. Understanding this distinction is crucial because it affects the degree of obligation and the consequence of omission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Eid prayer is the act under discussion. The passage explicitly states: 'صلاة العيدين واجبة' – the prayer of the two Eids is wajib.
2
Locate the evidence (dalil)
The author cites the hadith from Anas (narrated by Abu Dawud) where the Prophet replaced the pre-Islamic days of play with the two Eids. This hadith serves as the proof for the prayer's establishment.
The hadith is ahad (single-chain narration), not mutawatir.
3
Analyze the type of evidence
In Hanafi usul, rulings are classified based on the strength of evidence. Fard requires qat'i evidence (Quran or mutawatir sunnah). Since this hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), the resulting obligation is wajib, not fard.
The command (amr) in the hadith implies obligation (wujub) per Hanafi principle.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Unlike Hanafis, the Shafi'i school classifies Eid prayer as sunnah mu'akkadah because they do not differentiate between fard and wajib based on thubut; they consider any Shar'i obligation as fard.
This difference stems from usul principles rather than the primary texts.
5
Understand the practical consequence
Since it is wajib, omitting the Eid prayer without a valid excuse is sinful, but it does not affect one's faith or require a fresh iman. The prayer is performed in congregation, and there is no substitute adhan or iqamah.
The ruling impacts fatwa and daily practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب أحكام (العيدين) من الصلاة وغيرها سمى عيداً لأن الله تعالى فيه عوائد الإحسان لي عباده صلاة العيدين واجبة) وليست فرضاً ورد والمناسبة بين البابين ظاهرة، وهي اشتراكهما في الآداب والشرائط إلا الخطبة، والجمعة تسمى عيداً أيضاً قال : لكل مؤمن في كل شهر أربعة أعياد، أو خمسة أعياد، وقدمت الجمعة لفرضيتها وكثرة وجودها، وأصل عيد عود من العود بمعنى الرجوع قلبت الواو ياء لسكونها بعد كسرة كميزان وميقات، وقيل من عيد بفتحتين إذا جمع ويجمع على أعياد والقياس على الأول أعواد لأنه من العود، إلا أنه جمع بهذا اللفظ للزوم الياء في المفرد، فلم ينظر إلى الأصل، وقيل للفرق بينه وبين أعواد جمع عودا للهو وأما عود الخشب فجمعه عيدان قال في البحر وصلاة العيد شرعت في السنة الأولى من الهجرة كما رواه أبو داود عن أنس قال: قدم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم المدينة ولهم يومان يلعبون فيهما فقال : ما هذان اليومان قالوا : كنا نلعب فيهما في الجاهلية فقال رسول الله : إن الله قد أبدلكما بهما خيراً منهما يوم الأضحى ويوم الفطره اهـ. قوله : (لأن الله تعالى فيه عوائد الإحسان دينية ودنيوية أو لأنه يعود، ويتكرر بالفرح والسرور وتفاؤلاً بالعود على من أدركه كما سميت القافلة تفاؤلاً بقفولها أي رجوعها أو لاجتماع الناس فيه ويطلق على كل يوم مسرة ولذا قيل : عيد وعيد وعيد صرن مجتمعه وجه الحبيب ويوم العيد والجمعة
Chapter on the rulings of the two Eids, regarding prayer and other matters. It is called 'Eid because Allah (Exalted) in it returns favors of goodness to His servants. The prayer of the two Eids is wajib (obligatory) and not fard (a stronger obligation). The suitability between the two chapters (Eid and Jumu'ah) is apparent: they share etiquettes and conditions except the sermon. Jumu'ah is also called an 'Eid. He said: For every believer, in every month there are four or five Eids. Jumu'ah is given precedence due to its fard status and greater frequency. The root of 'Eid is 'awd from al-'awd meaning return; the waw is changed to ya because it is sukun after a kasra, like mizan and miqat. It is also said from 'ayd (with two fatha) meaning gather. It is pluralized as a'yad; by analogy with the first it would be a'wad because it is from 'awd, but it is pluralized with this word due to the permanence of the ya in the singular, so the origin is not considered. It is also said to differentiate between it and a'wad, plural of 'ud (a musical instrument). As for wood (khashab), its plural is 'idan. He said in al-Bahr: The Eid prayer was prescribed in the first year of the Hijrah, as Abu Dawud narrated from Anas: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) came to Medina, and they had two days of play. He said: 'What are these two days?' They said: 'We used to play on them in the Jahiliyyah.' The Messenger of Allah said: 'Allah has replaced them with something better: the Day of Adha and the Day of Fitr.' End. His saying: (Because Allah therein returns favors of goodness, religious and worldly, or because it returns and recurs with joy and happiness, and as an augury of return for those who experience it, just as the caravan is called qafilah as an augury of its return, or because people gather on it. It is used for every day of happiness. Hence it is said: 'Eid, Eid, Eid — they have become a gathering of the beloved's face, and the day of Eid and Jumu'ah.)
Source pages p. 527

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on the two Eids in Hashiya al-Tahtawi. It begins by stating the legal ruling: Eid prayer is wajib (obligatory) but not fard. This distinction is important in the Hanafi school: wajib is established by evidence that is zanni (speculative) in its transmission or meaning, while fard is established by qat'i (definitive) evidence. The author then explains the suitability of placing this chapter after the chapter on Jumu'ah, as both share etiquettes and conditions, except that Jumu'ah includes a sermon (khutbah). The etymology of 'Eid is given: it is from 'awd (return) because the day returns annually, or from 'ayd (gathering) because people gather. The prayer was legislated in the first year of Hijrah, as proven by the hadith of Anas (narrated by Abu Dawud) where the Prophet replaced the two pre-Islamic days of play with the two Eids. Thus, the passage establishes both the ruling and its basis.

Key Terms
عيد ('eid): A day of recurring happiness and divine favors; specifically, the two Eids: al-Fitr and al-Adha.
واجب (wajib): An obligation established by zanni evidence; omission is sinful but faith is not necessarily negated.
عوائد الإحسان ('awa'id al-ihsan): The recurring favors and goodness from Allah, both religious and worldly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is Eid prayer considered wajib rather than fard in the Hanafi school?
A) Because it is only recommended and not obligatory.
B) Because the evidence for it is zanni (speculative) and not qat'i (definitive).
C) Because it was prescribed later than other prayers.
D) Because it is performed only twice a year.

Key Takeaway
Eid prayer is wajib in the Hanafi school because the evidence is from ahad hadith, not qat'i sources.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Eid Prayer: Wajib Ruling, Conditions, and the Khutbah
Establishes Eid prayer as wajib and details conditions and the role of the khutbah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Eid prayer, identify the conditions for its obligation, and explain why the khutbah is not a condition for validity.

Core Idea
Eid prayer is wajib by continuous prophetic practice, valid without khutbah but with offense, and its conditions mirror Jumu'ah except for the khutbah.

Many assume Eid prayer is a sunnah. The Hanafi school, however, holds it as wajib based on the Prophet's unbroken practice. In this lesson, we unpack the dalil, clarify the distinction between wajib and fard, and explain the role of the khutbah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its level
Locate the explicit statement that Eid prayer is wajib, not fard. Note the passage's emphasis that it is the relied-upon position and that the term 'sunnah' in al-Jami' al-Saghir does not negate obligation.
Wajib in Hanafi usul is established by zanni dalil, while fard requires qati' dalil.
2
Examine the proof (dalil)
Identify the two proofs: (1) The Prophet's continuous practice without omission, transmitted widely; (2) Quranic indications from Surah al-Kawthar and the verse on takbir. Understand that continuous practice (fi'l mutawātir ma'nawī) indicates obligation.
The term 'wajib' is derived from the Prophet's action, not from an explicit command.
3
Analyze the conditions
List the conditions of obligation: same as Jumu'ah (e.g., residency, health, freedom). For validity, note that congregation is required but the imam alone suffices as a congregation. The khutbah is not a condition.
Conditions of validity differ from conditions of obligation.
4
Understand the khutbah's status
The khutbah is a sunnah that must be delivered after the prayer. Delivering it before is makruh, and the prayer is valid without it but with offense. This contrasts with Jumu'ah where the khutbah is a condition.
The ruling is based on the Prophet's consistent practice of delaying the khutbah.
5
Note the intra-madhhab difference
Recognize that some Hanafi narrations (e.g., from Abu Musa al-Darir) consider it fard kifayah, but the majority and the mufta bihi position is wajib. The passage resolves this by stating the most authentic view.
Intra-madhhab ikhtilaf does not affect the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب أحكام العيدين لأنه لظهور المناسبة بين البابين ظاهرة، وهي اشتراكهما في الآداب والشرائط إلا الخطبة، والجمعة تسمى عيداً أيضاً قال : لكل مؤمن في كل شهر أربعة أعياد، أو خمسة أعياد، وقدمت الجمعة لفرضيتها وكثرة وجودها، وأصل عيد عود من العود بمعنى الرجوع قلبت الواو ياء لسكونها بعد كسرة كميزان وميقات، وقيل من عيد بفتحتين إذا جمع ويجمع على أعياد والقياس على الأول أعواد لأنه من العود، إلا أنه جمع بهذا اللفظ للزوم الياء في المفرد، فلم ينظر إلى الأصل، وقيل للفرق بينه وبين أعواد جمع عودا للهو وأما عود الخشب فجمعه عيدان قال في البحر وصلاة العيد شرعت في السنة الأولى من الهجرة كما رواه أبو داود عن الفطره اهـ. قوله : (لأن الله تعالى فيه عوائد الإحسان دينية ودنيوية أو لأنه يعود، ويتكرر بالفرح والسرور وتفاؤلاً بالعود على من أدركه كما سميت القافلة تفاؤلاً بقفولها أي رجوعها أو لاجتماع الناس فيه الأكثرون، وتسميتها في الجامع الصغير سنة لأنه ثبت الوجوب بها لمواظبة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم على صلاة العيدين من غير ترك فتجب على من تجب عليه الجمعة بشرائطها وقد علمتها فلا بد من شرائط الوجوب جميعها، النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم (وندب) أي استحب لمصلي العيد (في) يوم الفطر) ثلاثة عشر شيئاً أن يأكل) بعد الفجر قبل ذهابه للمصلي شيئاً حلوا كالسكر (و) ندب أن يكون المأكول تمراً) إن وجد (و) أن يكون عدده ومذهب الإمام أحمد أن وقت الجمعة يدخل بدخول وقت صلاة العيد قال في متن المنتهي: وشرحه للشيخ منصور الحنبلي، وإذا وقع عيد في يوم الجمعة سقطت عمن حضر العيد ذلك اليوم سقوط حضور لا سقوط وجوب لأنه صلى العيد وقال : شاء أن من يجمع، فليجمع أفاده السيد. قوله : (وهي الأصح (رواية) عن الإمام وعليه الجمهور كافي، وهو المختار خلاصه، ونص عليه محمد في الأصل . قوله : ( ودراية) لأنه ثبت بالنقل المستفيض عنه أنه كان يصلي صلاة العيدين من حين شرعيتها إلى أن توفاه الله تعالى من غير ترك، وكذا الخلفاء الراشدون، والأئمة المجتهدون، وهذا دليل الوجوب، وبإشارة الكتاب العزيز وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿ولتكبروا الله على ما هداكم) وقوله تعالى : فصل لربك) [الكوثر : ۱۰۸] وانحر فان الأولى إشارة إلى صلاة عيد الفطر، والثانية إلى صلاة الأضحى. قوله: (وتسميتها في الجامع الصغير سنة الخ) عبارته عيدان اجتمعا في يوم واحد فالأول سنة، والثاني فريضة ولا يترك واحد منهما اهـ قال في العناية هذا لا ينافي الوجوب ألا ترى إلى قوله، ولا يترك واحد منهما فإنه ينفي الترك والإخبار في عبارة المشايخ والأئمة يفيد الوجوب كذا في الحلبي على أن الوجوب قريب من السنة لأن السنة المؤكدة في قوة الواجب، ولهذا كان الأصح أنه يأثم بتركها كالواجب بحر، وقال أبو موسى الضرير في مختصره : إنها فرض كفاية كما في شرح الزاهدي، ومسكين وهو رواية عن الإمام وبه قال أحمد كما في البرهان قوله: (وشرائط الصحة ظاهره أنه لا بد من الجماعة المذكورة في الجمعة على خلاف فيها، وليس كذلك، فإن الواحد هنا الإمام جماعة، فيكف يصح أن يقال بشرائطها؟ . قوله : (لم تكن شرطاً لها) لأن شرط الشيء يسبقه أو يقارنه قوله : (لو قدمت الخطبة على الصلاة) اعلم ان الخطبة سنة وتأخيرها إلى ما بعد الصلاة سنة أيضاً نهر عن الظهيرية وكونه مسيئاً بالتقديم لا يدل على نفي سنية أصلها مطلقاً لأن الإساءة لترك سنة التأخير، وهي غير أصل السنة، وفي الدرة المنيفة : لو خطب قبل الصلاة جاز، وترك الفضيلة ولا تعاد ومثله في مسكين .اهـ.
Chapter on the rulings of the two Eids. Because the appropriateness between the two chapters is apparent, namely their sharing of etiquettes and conditions except the khutbah. Friday is also called Eid. He said: For every believer, every month there are four or five Eids. Friday is given precedence due to its obligation and frequent occurrence. The root of 'Eid is 'awd meaning return; the waw is changed to ya due to sukun after kasra like mizan and miqat. It is also said from 'ayd (with two faths) meaning to gather. It is pluralized as a'yaad. By analogy with the first it would be a'waad, but this plural is used due to the ya in the singular. It is also said to differentiate from a'waad (plural of 'ud for entertainment). As for wood, its plural is 'eedan. It is said in al-Bahr: The Eid prayer was legislated in the first year of Hijra as narrated by Abu Dawud from Anas: The Prophet arrived in Madinah while they had two days of playing. He asked: 'What are these two days?' They said: 'We used to play on them in Jahiliyyah.' The Prophet said: 'Allah has replaced them with two better days: the day of Adha and the day of Fitr.' His statement: 'Because Allah in it has blessings of beneficence, religious and worldly, or because it returns and repeats with joy and glad tidings, and by way of optimism for return for those who experience it, just as the caravan is named optimistically for its return. Or because people gather on it. It is applied to every day of happiness, hence it is said: 'Eid, Eid, and Eid, they all gather together, the face of the beloved and the day of Eid and Friday.' His statement: 'The Eid prayer is wajib' and not fard. The text of obligation from the Imam is in one narration, and it is the most authentic in transmission and reasoning, and the majority hold it. Its being called sunnah in al-Jami' al-Saghir is because the obligation is established by it due to the Prophet's continuous adherence to the Eid prayer without ever leaving it. So it becomes obligatory on those for whom Jumu'ah is obligatory, with its conditions as you have learned. Therefore all conditions of obligation are necessary, and conditions of validity except the khutbah, because it was delayed after the prayer so it is not a condition for it but rather sunnah. So the Eid prayer is valid without it, i.e., the khutbah, but with offense for leaving a sunnah, just as one would be offensive if he delivered the khutbah before the prayer due to contradicting the Prophet's practice. And it is recommended for the one praying Eid on the day of Fitr: thirteen things: to eat something sweet like sugar after Fajr before going to the prayer place, and it is recommended that the food be dates if available, and that the number be... And the school of Imam Ahmad is that the time of Jumu'ah enters with the time of Eid prayer. He said in Matn al-Muntaha and its commentary by Sheikh Mansur al-Hanbali: If Eid falls on Friday, it falls for those who attend the Eid that day, a fall of attendance not of obligation, because he prayed Eid and said: 'Whoever wishes may attend Jumu'ah, so let him attend.' This was beneficial from al-Sayyid. His statement: 'It is the most authentic (narration) from the Imam, and the majority are upon it, as in al-Kafi, and it is the chosen position in al-Khulasa, and Muhammad stated it in al-Asl.' His statement: 'And by reasoning' because it is established through widespread transmission that he used to pray the Eid prayer from its legislation until his death without ever leaving it, and likewise the Rightly Guided Caliphs and the Mujtahid Imams. This is proof of obligation. Also by indication of the noble Book, His statement: 'And that you magnify Allah for having guided you' and His statement: 'So pray to your Lord and sacrifice [al-Kawthar:108]. The first is an indication of the Fitr prayer, the second of the Adha prayer. His statement: 'And its being called sunnah in al-Jami' al-Saghir...' His expression: 'Two Eids coincide on one day, the first is sunnah, the second is fard, and neither is to be left.' It is said in al-Inayah: This does not contradict obligation. Do you not see his statement 'neither is to be left' which negates leaving, and informing in the words of the mashayikh and imams indicates obligation... As in al-Halabi, that obligation is close to sunnah because mu'akkadah sunnah is in the strength of wajib. Hence the most correct is that one sins by leaving it like a wajib, as in al-Bahr. Abu Musa al-Darir said in his Mukhtasar: It is fard kifayah as in Sharh al-Zahidi, and it is a narration from the Imam, and Ahmad held it as in al-Burhan. His statement: 'Conditions of validity' - apparently it requires the congregation mentioned in Jumu'ah, but there is a difference. It is not so, for the single person here, the imam, is a congregation, so how can it be said that its conditions are like that? His statement: 'It was not a condition for it' because the condition of a thing precedes or accompanies it. His statement: 'If he delivered the khutbah before the prayer' - know that the khutbah is sunnah and its delay until after the prayer is also sunnah, as in al-Zahiriyyah. His being offensive by delivering it early does not indicate negation of its sunniyyah in absolute terms, because the offense is for leaving the sunnah of delay, which is separate from the original sunnah. In al-Durrah al-Manifah: If he delivered the khutbah before the prayer, it is permissible, but he leaves virtue and it is not repeated. Similarly in Miskin...
Source pages p. 527

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hashiya) on the ruling of Eid prayer. The author affirms that Eid prayer is wajib (obligatory) but not fard, based on the Prophet's continuous practice and the majority of scholars. He addresses the term 'sunnah' used in al-Jami' al-Saghir, clarifying that it does not negate obligation because the Prophet never omitted it. Conditions for Eid prayer mirror those of Jumu'ah (e.g., residence, health, etc.) except the khutbah, which is a sunnah that can be performed after the prayer. Delivering the khutbah before the prayer is makruh and sinful. The author also mentions that if Eid and Jumu'ah coincide, Jumu'ah attendance is not obligatory for those who prayed Eid. There is an intra-madhhab dispute: Abu Hanifa's authentic position is wajib, but some narrations suggest fard kifayah. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that it is wajib. The khutbah is a sunnah, not a condition, so the prayer is valid without it but with offense.

Key Terms
عيد (‘īd): A recurring day of celebration; specifically the two Islamic festivals.
واجبة (wājibah): Obligatory but not at the level of fard; established by zanni dalil.
خطبة (khutbah): The sermon delivered on Eids and Fridays. For Eid, it is sunnah to deliver after the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling of the Eid prayer according to the relied-upon Hanafi position?
A) Fard 'ayn
B) Fard kifayah
C) Wajib
D) Sunnah mu'akkadah

Key Takeaway
Eid prayer is wajib by continuous prophetic practice, valid without khutbah but with offense, and its conditions mirror Jumu'ah except for the khutbah.

The Obligation of Eid Prayer: Wajib or Sunnah?
Critical refinement of the ruling on Eid prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Eid prayer and explain the proof from continuous practice (tawatur 'amali) that establishes its wajib status.

Core Idea
Eid prayer is wajib, not sunnah — proven by the Prophet's unwavering practice and Quranic command.

Many assume Eid prayer is merely a recommended sunnah, but the Hanafi school holds it to be wajib (obligatory). This passage from al-Tahtawi's commentary critically refines the earlier label of 'sunnah' used by Imam Muhammad, demonstrating that the continuous practice of the Prophet ﷺ and the Quranic verses raise it to the level of obligation. Understanding this distinction is crucial for knowing the sin incurred by neglecting it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its level
The commentator opens by stating that the correct view is that Eid prayer is wajib. Note that in Hanafi usul, wajib is a level below fard, established by zanni (non-definitive) evidence, but still binding.
2
Examine the proof: tawatur 'amali
The primary evidence is the Prophet's continuous performance of the two Eid prayers without ever omitting them, along with the practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs. This recurrent practice (tawatur 'amali) is a strong proof of obligation.
The commentator cites Quranic verses: 'So pray to your Lord and sacrifice' (al-Kawthar) and '…that you may magnify Allah for His guidance' (al-Baqarah).
3
Reconcile the term 'sunnah' in al-Jami' al-Saghir
Imam Muhammad called it sunnah, but this is interpreted as 'sunnah mu'akkadah' (emphasized sunnah), which in the Hanafi school carries the force of wajib. The passage explicitly says the term does not negate obligation.
He points to the phrase 'nor should it be omitted' from al-Jami' al-Saghir as evidence of obligation.
4
List the conditions for Eid prayer
The conditions of obligation and validity are the same as for Jumu'ah: residency, health, absence of impediments, etc. However, the khutbah is not a condition for validity; it is a sunnah to be performed after the prayer.
If the khutbah is given before the prayer, it is valid but makruh (offensive) for contradicting the Prophet's practice.
5
Note the dispute with other schools
Shafi'is and Hanbalis consider Eid prayer merely sunnah mu'akkadah. The commentator shows that the Hanafi position, resting on continuous practice, is stronger. The practical consequence: leaving it without excuse is sinful in the Hanafi school.
The passage also mentions a weak Hanafi narration that it is fard kifayah, but the relied-upon view is wajib.

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement of the ruling on Eid prayer. The commentator begins by establishing that the correct Hanafi view is that Eid prayer is wajib (obligatory), based on the continuous practice of the Prophet and the caliphs. He addresses the objection that it is called 'sunnah' in al-Jami' al-Saghir, explaining that this does not negate obligation; rather, the term 'sunnah' there means a highly emphasized sunnah that has the force of wajib. He then lists the conditions for Eid prayer: they are the same as for Jumu'ah (including residency, health, etc.) except that the khutbah is not a condition for validity but is a sunnah that should be performed after the prayer. If one gives the khutbah before the prayer, it is valid but offensive because it contradicts the Prophet's practice. The passage also includes an aside on the ruling when Eid falls on Friday, citing Imam Ahmad's view that Jumu'ah attendance is waived for those who attend Eid. The commentator clarifies that the waiver is of attendance, not of obligation. The overall teaching is that Eid prayer carries a level of obligation that must be taken seriously.

Key Terms
الوجوب (al-wujub): A level of obligation less than fard, established by zanni evidence; neglecting it is sinful.
السنة المؤكدة (al-sunnah al-mu'akkadah): A highly emphasized sunnah that is in the strength of wajib; leaving it is blameworthy.
الخطبة (al-khutbah): The sermon delivered for Eid prayer, which is sunnah and not a condition for validity.
التواتر العملي (al-tawatur al-'amali): Continuous, unbroken practice of the Prophet that serves as proof of obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) An explicit verse in the Quran stating it is fard.
B) The Prophet's continuous practice of praying Eid without omission.
C) The consensus of all four madhhabs.
D) A hadith that says 'Eid prayer is wajib'.

Key Takeaway
Eid prayer is wajib in the Hanafi school; neglecting it without excuse is sinful, proven by the Prophet's continuous practice and Quranic commands.

Recommended Acts on Eid al-Fitr
Listing the thirteen recommended acts for Eid al-Fitr with details and evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state at least three recommended acts for Eid al-Fitr and explain the Hanafi position on their legal status and evidence.

Core Idea
The Prophet's practice on Eid is a detailed sunnah—eating odd dates, ghusl, perfume, best clothes—all recommended but not obligatory.

In this passage, al-Tahtawi expands on the matn's listing of recommended acts for Eid al-Fitr. He explains the wisdom behind each act and clarifies that they are sunnah, not sinful to omit. You will learn the specifics of these acts, their evidence from the Prophet's practice, and the degree of their legal strength in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first recommended act
The passage begins with the act of eating after dawn on Eid al-Fitr. Note that the wisdom is to hasten to comply with the command and to mark the abrogation of the earlier prohibition of eating before the Eid prayer.
Drinking is also included by analogy.
2
Examine the details of eating
The eating should be of dates if possible, in an odd number (three, five, seven, etc.). If dates are unavailable, any sweet suffices. The Prophet's practice demonstrates this.
The odd number symbolizes divine unity and is a general prophetic preference.
3
Identify the second act: ghusl (ritual bath)
Ghusl is recommended for the day of Eid itself, not specifically for the prayer. This is because Eid is a day of joy and gathering. The text notes that this view agrees with the Maliki and Shafi'i schools.
Some later Hanafis like al-Sarukhsi confirm this position.
4
Note the remaining acts: perfume, best clothes, and others
Applying perfume and wearing one's best clothes (avoiding deep red) are also sunnah. The passage implies other acts like using miswak and going early to the prayer place.
The list of thirteen is not fully enumerated here, but these are representative.
5
Understand the overall legal status
All these acts are sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized recommended). Leaving them is not sinful, but it is blameworthy if done without excuse. Some scholars (like al-Qahistani) mention the possibility of punishment for habitually neglecting them.
The mufta bihi is that they are rewardable, not obligatory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

يفعل ذلك قبل خروجه ينبغي أن يفعله في الطريق، أو في المصلى إن تيسر كما في شروح الحديث، فإن لم يفعل فلا كراهة في الأصح كذا في الحلبي قوله : ( ويأكلهن وتراً) زاد ابن حبان ثلاثاً أو خمساً أو سبعاً، أو أقل من ذلك، أو أكثر بعد أن يكون وتراً، وقال شارحوه الحكمة في تخصيص التمر لما في الحلو من تقوية البصر الذي أضعف الصوم، وترقيق القلب وهو أيسر من غيره ومن ثمة استحب بعض التابعين أن يفطر على الحلو مطلقاً الفجر فإن فعل قبله أجزأه ، ويستوي في ذلك الذاهب إلى الصلاة والقاعد لأنه يوم زينة واجتماع بخلاف الجمعة. قال السروجي، وهذا صحيح وبه قالت المالكية والشافعية كما في الحلبي، واختار في الدرر أيضاً كون الخالص لأن الأحمر القانيء أي شديد الحمرة مكروه كذا في شرح السيد بزيادة .
His saying: 'thirteen things' – the fifteen? His saying: 'that he eat after dawn' – the wisdom is to hasten to comply with the command, and to know the abrogation of the prohibition of eating before the Eid prayer, for it was prohibited in early Islam. Drinking is like eating. If he does not do that before leaving, he should do it on the way or at the prayer place if possible. If he does not do it, there is no dislike in the correct view. His saying: 'and he eats them odd in number' – Ibn Hibban added three, five, seven, or less or more as long as odd. The commentators said the wisdom in specifying dates is due to the sweetness strengthening the eyesight weakened by fasting, and softening the heart...
Source pages p. 528

Commentary
This passage expands on the recommended acts (mandubat) for Eid al-Fitr. The commentator explains the first act: eating something sweet, preferably dates, in an odd number before going to the Eid prayer. This is to hasten compliance with the command and to mark the end of fasting. He details the wisdom behind eating dates and odd numbers, including the Prophet's love for odd numbers. If dates are unavailable, any sweet suffices. He then discusses ghusl (ritual bath) for Eid, noting that it is recommended for the day itself, not specifically for the prayer, as it is a day of adornment and gathering. This view is supported by the Malikis and Shafi'is. Next, he covers the use of miswak (toothstick) and perfume, and finally the wearing of one's best clothes, avoiding deep red which is disliked. The underlying theme is that all these acts are sunnah, not obligatory, but performing them follows the Prophet's example and enhances the joy of Eid.

Key Terms
الوتر (al-witr): Odd number, specifically eating an odd number of dates (three, five, seven, etc.) as a recommended practice.
الغسل (al-ghusl): The ritual bath recommended for Eid day, not specifically for the prayer but for the day itself due to the general joy.
المندوب (al-mandub): Synonymous with sunnah (recommended); doing it is rewardable, leaving it is not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on eating dates before the Eid prayer according to this passage?
A) It is wajib
B) It is sunnah mu'akkadah
C) It is mustahabb (recommended)
D) It is mubah

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's practice on Eid provides a model of sunnah acts that enhance the celebration; they are recommended, not obligatory, and following them brings reward.

Recommended Acts for Eid Day for Men
Enumeration of sunan acts for Eid with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended acts for men on Eid day according to the Hanafi school, classify their hukm, and identify the preferred time for zakat al-fitr.

Core Idea
Eid sunnah acts are meritorious, not obligatory – except zakat al-fitr which is wajib.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi lists the sunnah practices for men on Eid. Understanding these acts helps you follow the Prophet's practice and avoid considering them fard. We will focus on the list and their legal status.

Guided Path
1
List the recommended acts
Scan the passage and list each act: wearing a special cloak, giving zakat al-fitr before prayer, showing joy, wearing a ring, cheerfulness, increasing charity, early rising (tabeer), hastening to the musalla (ibtikaar), praying Fajr in neighborhood masjid, going solely for worship.
The text also mentions the takbir dispute, which will be covered in the next lesson.
2
Classify the hukm of each act
Most acts are sunnah mu'akkadah; zakat al-fitr is wajib. Use the hanafi_position_box to confirm the overall hukm.
Note that the acts are recommended, not obligatory, except zakat.
3
Identify the timings for zakat al-fitr
The text mentions four categories: before the day (ja'iz), on the day before prayer (mustahabb), after prayer (ja'iz), after the day (sinful but valid).
The preferred time is before the Eid prayer.
4
Note the takbir dispute
There is an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether takbir should be silent or loud. This will be detailed in the next lesson.
For now, note that the mufta bihi is silent per Abu Hanifa.

من مروان بن الحكم في خلافة معاوية كذا يعلم من البخاري وشرحه
And it is recommended for men: The Prophet had a cloak of fanak (fur) that he would wear for the Friday congregation and the two Eids; and he should give zakat al-fitr if it is due upon him, because the Prophet ordered its payment before people go out to the prayer; and he should show joy by obeying Allah and thanking for His blessing; and he should wear a ring; and show cheerfulness in the face of the believers he meets; and increase voluntary charity according to his capacity beyond his usual habit; and tabeer (early rising), which is promptness to rise at the beginning of the time or before to perform worship actively; and ibtikaar (hastening to the musalla) to attain its merit and the first row; and he should pray Fajr in his neighborhood masjid to fulfill its right; and his going should be solely for a specific worship. Then his saying: (The Prophet had a fanak cloak...)...
Source pages p. 530

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya enumerates the recommended acts (mandubat) for men on Eid day as detailed by the Hanafi school. The text begins by listing items such as wearing a special cloak (jubbat fanak), giving zakat al-fitr before the prayer, showing joy, wearing a ring, cheerfulness, increasing charity, early rising (tabeer), hastening to the prayer ground (ibtikaar), praying Fajr in one's neighborhood masjid, and devoting one's going solely to worship. The commentary then expands on each, providing proofs: the hadith about the Prophet's cloak, the ruling on zakat al-fitr times (four categories: before the day, on the day before prayer (mustahabb), after prayer (ja'iz), and after the day (sinful but removed by payment)), the virtue of wearing a ring on Eid, and the Islamic greeting 'Taqabbal Allah minna wa minkum' which is mustahabb. A key intra-Hanafi dispute arises over the takbir while walking to the musalla: Imam Abu Hanifa holds it should be recited silently (sirr), relying on the general Quranic command 'and remember your Lord within yourself' and the hadith 'the best of remembrance is the hidden one'. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold it should be loud (jahr), citing the practice of Ibn Umar and many early Muslims. The author sides with the Imam's view, noting that the practice of a single Companion (Ibn Umar) cannot override the definitive textual evidence for silence. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the silent recitation.

Key Terms
فنك (fanak): A type of fur garment, specifically a cloak made from the fur of a fox-like animal.
حبرة (hibarah): A striped Yemeni garment (burd) with decorative patterns.
الابتكار (al-ibtikaar): Hastening to the musalla (prayer ground) early to attain its merit and the first row.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling for giving zakat al-fitr after the Eid prayer on the same day?
A) It is forbidden (haram)
B) It is obligatory (wajib) but incomplete
C) It is permissible (ja'iz)
D) It is recommended (mustahabb)

Key Takeaway
Eid acts are recommended sunnah mu'akkadah to follow the Prophet's example, with zakat al-fitr being wajib and best paid before the Eid prayer.

The Dispute on Takbir: Silent vs Loud for Eid
Dispute on takbir method with proofs and resolution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the recitation of takbir on the way to the Eid prayer, contrast the proofs of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa holds silent takbir is best; the Sahibayn prefer loud – the difference hinges on textual interpretation vs. practice.

While walking to the Eid prayer ground, one should recite takbir. But should it be loud or silent? This lesson unpacks the Hanafi internal disagreement and the evidence each side uses. The passage explicitly presents both views and their proofs.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
The exact point of dispute: should takbir be recited silently (sirr) or loudly (jahr) on the way to the musalla?
Both positions agree that reciting takbir is sunnah.
2
Identify Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Abu Hanifa says sirr is preferable. His proof: Quran 7:205 ('...and remember your Lord within yourself...') and the hadith 'the best remembrance is the hidden one.'
The text considers this the stronger evidence.
3
Identify the Sahibayn's position and proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say jahr is mustahabb. Their proof: the practice of Ibn Umar and many early Muslims who raised their voices.
The text lists numerous early scholars who practiced loud takbir.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa responds: the practice of a single Companion (qawl sahabi) cannot override the general (umum) Quranic command for hidden remembrance.
This is a classic usul al-fiqh issue: an action of a Companion vs. a definitive text.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The commentator (al-Tahtawi) sides with Abu Hanifa, indicating that silent recitation is the relied-upon position.
The mufta bihi is silent takbir, though the other view is valid within the school.

في كراهته وعدمها فعندهما يستحب، وعنده الإخفاء أفضل، وذلك لأن الجهر قد نقل عن كثير من السلف كابن عمر وعلي وأبي أمامة الباهلي، والنخعي، وابن جبير وعمر بن عبد العزيز وابن أبي ليلى وأبان بن عثمان، والحكم وحماد، ومالك والشافعي، وأحمد وأبي ثور كما ذكره ابن المنذر في الإشراق اهـ. قوله: (وكان ابن عمر يرفع صوته بالتكبير) أجيب من طرف الإمام بأنه قول صحابي فلا يعارض به عموم ا القطعية أعني قوله تعالى: (وإذكر ربك إلى قوله ودون الجهر قوله : ( وتكثيراً للشهود) لأن مكان القربة يشهد لصاحبه اهـ ،سراج ولا بأس ببناء منبر في المصلى، ولم يكن في زمنه لها منبر، وإنما كان يخطب وهو واقف، وكذا الخلفاء الراشدون بعده وأول من مروان بن الحكم في خلافة معاوية كذا يعلم من البخاري وشرحه
And it is recommended for men: The Prophet had a cloak of fanak (fur) that he would wear for the Friday congregation and the two Eids; and he should give zakat al-fitr if it is due upon him, because the Prophet ordered its payment before people go out to the prayer; and he should show joy by obeying Allah and thanking for His blessing; and he should wear a ring; and show cheerfulness in the face of the believers he meets; and increase voluntary charity according to his capacity beyond his usual habit; and tabeer (early rising), which is promptness to rise at the beginning of the time or before to perform worship actively; and ibtikaar (hastening to the musalla) to attain its merit and the first row; and he should pray Fajr in his neighborhood masjid to fulfill its right; and his going should be solely for a specific worship. Then his saying: (The Prophet had a fanak cloak...)...
Source pages p. 530

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya enumerates the recommended acts (mandubat) for men on Eid day as detailed by the Hanafi school. The text begins by listing items such as wearing a special cloak (jubbat fanak), giving zakat al-fitr before the prayer, showing joy, wearing a ring, cheerfulness, increasing charity, early rising (tabeer), hastening to the prayer ground (ibtikaar), praying Fajr in one's neighborhood masjid, and devoting one's going solely to worship. The commentary then expands on each, providing proofs: the hadith about the Prophet's cloak, the ruling on zakat al-fitr times (four categories: before the day, on the day before prayer (mustahabb), after prayer (ja'iz), and after the day (sinful but removed by payment)), the virtue of wearing a ring on Eid, and the Islamic greeting 'Taqabbal Allah minna wa minkum' which is mustahabb. A key intra-Hanafi dispute arises over the takbir while walking to the musalla: Imam Abu Hanifa holds it should be recited silently (sirr), relying on the general Quranic command 'and remember your Lord within yourself' and the hadith 'the best of remembrance is the hidden one'. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold it should be loud (jahr), citing the practice of Ibn Umar and many early Muslims. The author sides with the Imam's view, noting that the practice of a single Companion (Ibn Umar) cannot override the definitive textual evidence for silence. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the silent recitation.

Key Terms
فنك (fanak): A type of fur garment, specifically a cloak made from the fur of a fox-like animal.
حبرة (hibarah): A striped Yemeni garment (burd) with decorative patterns.
الابتكار (al-ibtikaar): Hastening to the musalla (prayer ground) early to attain its merit and the first row.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The hadith is weak
B) Ibn Umar's action is a single Companion's practice and cannot override a definitive Quranic command
C) Both practices are equally valid, no preference
D) Loud takbir is actually forbidden

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi is silent takbir on Eid, based on the general command of hidden remembrance, despite the Sahibayn relying on Companion practice.

Dislike of Voluntary Prayers Before Eid Prayer at the Musalla
Ruling on the karahah of Sunnah prayers before Eid prayer at the musalla

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing voluntary prayers before the Eid prayer at the musalla and identify the scope of the ruling and the exception that is disregarded.

Core Idea
All voluntary prayers before Eid prayer at the musalla are disliked, without exception.

This lesson examines a specific fiqh ruling concerning supererogatory prayers before the Eid prayer at the outdoor prayer ground (musalla). The Hanafi school holds a clear position that such prayers are disliked (makruh tanzihi). Despite a minor internal disagreement reported from Ibn Muqatil, the established view is absolute karahah, applying to all types of voluntary prayers and all individuals alike.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing any voluntary prayer (nafl) before the Eid prayer at the musalla. The ruling is karahah (dislike), specifically makruh tanzihi.
The dislike is not severe enough to be haram, but it should be avoided.
2
Understand the scope of the ruling
The ruling applies to all voluntary prayers, including the forenoon prayer (Duha) and the greeting of the masjid (tahiyyat al-masjid). It also applies to all individuals, whether the Eid prayer is obligatory for them or not, including women.
The text explicitly mentions Duha and tahiyyat al-masjid as examples.
3
Analyze the dissenting opinion
Ibn Muqatil reportedly held that it is not disliked in a corner of the masjid. However, the commentator dismisses this view, stating that it is as if his disagreement was not considered.
The dismissal indicates that the dissenting opinion is weak and not relied upon.
4
Confirm the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is absolute dislike for all voluntary prayers before the Eid prayer at the musalla, regardless of the type of prayer or the person performing it.
This is the view that should be followed in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويكره التنفل قبل صلاة العيد في المصلى) اتفاقاً ) في القهستاني عن المضمرات أنها لا تكره في ناحية المسجد عند ابن مقاتل فكأنه لم يعتبر خلافه والكراهة تثبت مطلقاً، ولو في صلاة الضحى، أو تحية المسجد، وسواء من تجب عليه صلاة العيد، وغيره حتى يكره للنساء أن يصلين الضحى يوم العيد قبل صلاة الإمام كما في.
And it is disliked to perform voluntary prayer before the Eid prayer at the musalla, by agreement [of the scholars]. In al-Qahistani from al-Mudmarat that it is not disliked in a corner of the masjid according to Ibn Muqatil, so it is as if he did not consider his disagreement, and the dislike is established absolutely, even for the forenoon prayer (Duha) or the greeting of the masjid (tahiyyat al-masjid), and equally for those upon whom the Eid prayer is obligatory and others, to the point that it is disliked for women to pray Duha on the day of Eid before the Imam's prayer, as in...
Source pages p. 531

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya presents the ruling that performing voluntary prayers (nafl) before the Eid prayer at the musalla (the designated outdoor prayer ground) is makruh (disliked). The commentator notes that this is by agreement (ittifaqan) of the scholars. However, he records a dissenting opinion from Ibn Muqatil, who held that it is not disliked in a corner of the masjid. The commentator dismisses this as practically disregarded, affirming that karahah is absolute. This dislike applies to any voluntary prayer, including the forenoon prayer (Duha) and the greeting of the masjid (tahiyyat al-masjid), and it applies equally to men and women, and to those upon whom the Eid prayer is obligatory as well as others (e.g., travellers). The rule is strict: no supererogatory prayers should be offered at the musalla before the Eid prayer.

Key Terms
كراهة (karahah): Dislike (legal discouragement), here tanzihi (close to permissible).
المصلى (al-musalla): The outdoor prayer ground designated for Eid prayers, distinct from the masjid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Only prayers for those who missed Eid

Key Takeaway
All voluntary prayers before the Eid prayer at the musalla are disliked, and this ruling applies universally.

Manners of Going to Eid Prayer and Takbir Audibility
Fiqh ruling with proof on Eid prayer journey etiquette

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended manner of proceeding to the Eid prayer according to the Hanafi school, including the ruling on takbir audibility, and identify the intra-Hanafi difference on whether the takbir is said quietly or audibly.

Core Idea
Walking to Eid prayer with humility and saying takbir is sunnah; Abu Hanifa preferred quiet takbir, but the Sahibayn preferred audible — both are valid.

This passage from the Hanafi fiqh text details the etiquette of going to the Eid prayer. It instructs the believer to walk with tranquility and lowered gaze, to say a specific supplication, and to recite takbir. A key point of internal debate is whether the takbir should be said quietly or audibly. Additionally, it is sunnah to return from a different path. Understanding these rulings helps one embody the spirit of Eid and follow the Sunna of the Prophet (peace be upon him).

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended acts before and during the journey
List the actions prescribed in the passage: walking with dignity and lowered gaze, saying a supplication, reciting takbir, and returning via a different route.
These are sunnah acts, not obligatory.
2
Recognize the proofs cited for each act
Note that walking with tranquility is based on the Prophet's practice. The supplication and quiet takbir are supported by the hadith 'The best remembrance is the hidden one.' The act of returning via a different path is also from the Prophet's practice.
The proofs are from Sunnah (fi'l and qawl).
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi difference on takbir audibility
Abu Hanifa prefers quiet takbir, citing the hadith about hidden dhikr. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad prefer audible takbir, citing the practice of Ibn 'Umar and a narration from Abu Hanifa himself. Identify the arguments and counterarguments.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different weight given to general vs. specific proofs.
4
Understand the tarjih (relied-upon position)
The text notes that 'people act upon' the narration of stopping takbir at the musalla, implying that the practice of the community is considered. For audibility, the mufta bihi is that quiet is better, but both are acceptable.
The tarjih here is from the later Hanafi scholars (e.g., al-Tahtawi).
5
Note the additional sunnah of returning by a different path
The Prophet would return from Eid prayer via a different route to increase the number of witnesses to the prayer. This is a recommended practice.
The wisdom is to spread the blessings and make the prayer more visible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يتوجه إلى المصلى إشارة إلى تقديم ما تقدم على الذهاب إلى المصلى (ماشياً) بسكون ووقار وغض بصر روي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام خرج ماشياً، وكان يقول عند خروجه: اللهم إني خرجت إليك مخرج العبد الذليل (مكبراً) سراً) قال عليه السلام: خير الذكر الخفي وخير الرزق ما يكفي، وعندهما جهراً وهو رواية عن الإمام، وكان ابن عمر يرفع صوته بالتكبير (ويقطعه) أي التكبير إذا انتهى إلى المصلى في رواية جزم بها في الدراية (وفي رواية إذا افتتح الصلاة) كذا في الكافي وعليه عمل الناس قال أبو جعفر، وبه نأخذ (ويرجع من طريق آخر) اقتداء بالنبي وتكثيراً للشهود
He proceeds to the prayer place indicating what precedes before going to the musalla (walking) with tranquility, dignity, and lowering the gaze. It is narrated that he (peace be upon him) went out walking, and he used to say when leaving: 'O Allah, I have come out to You as the exit of a humble servant.' (saying takbir quietly) for he said: 'The best remembrance is the hidden one and the best provision is what suffices.' According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) audibly, which is a narration from Abu Hanifa. Ibn 'Umar used to raise his voice with takbir. (And he stops) the takbir when he reaches the musalla in one narration affirmed in al-Diraya. (And in another narration, when he begins the prayer). Thus in al-Kafi, and people act upon it. Abu Ja'far said: 'We take this.' (And he returns from a different path) following the Prophet and to increase witnesses.
Source pages p. 531

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the recommended manner of going to the Eid prayer. The author explains that one should proceed to the musalla walking with calmness and lowered gaze, based on the Prophet's practice. The takbir (saying 'Allahu Akbar') should be said quietly according to Abu Hanifa, but audibly according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), which is also a narration from Abu Hanifa. The author notes that Ibn 'Umar raised his voice, but the Hanafi response is that his practice as a Companion does not override the general Qur'anic command to remember Allah without raising the voice excessively. The takbir is stopped when reaching the musalla or when starting the prayer, and people act on the first narration. It is also sunnah to return from a different path to increase witnesses for the prayer.

Key Terms
مصلى (musalla): The place designated for Eid prayer outside the mosque, typically an open ground.
تكبير (takbir): The act of saying 'Allahu Akbar' during the journey to Eid prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Continue until the prayer ends
D) Stop when entering the mosque

Key Takeaway
Walking to the Eid prayer with humility and reciting takbir quietly (or audibly) is a recommended sunnah, and returning by a different path is a beloved practice of the Prophet.

Voluntary Prayer Before and After Eid: Ruling and Location
Ruling with proof on voluntary prayer before/after Eid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on voluntary prayer before and after the Eid prayer, distinguish between the musalla and home, and cite the evidence from hadith.

Core Idea
Voluntary prayer in the musalla before Eid is disliked universally; after Eid it is disliked only in the musalla, not at home.

This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position on performing nafl prayers in connection with the Eid prayer. While some schools encourage extra prayers, the Hanafi school holds that it is makruh tanzihi to pray voluntarily in the musalla before or after the Eid prayer. However, at home it is permissible, especially after the prayer, based on the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
Determine what act is being discussed (voluntary prayer) and where it occurs (musalla vs. home, before vs. after Eid).
The passage distinguishes two times (before and after) and two locations (musalla and home).
2
State the ruling for each combination
Based on the text, state whether it is makruh or not for each of the four scenarios.
Before: makruh in musalla and at home (majority view). After: makruh only in musalla, not at home.
3
Locate the proof (dalil)
Find the hadith evidence cited: the Prophet did not pray before or after in the musalla, and he prayed two rak'ahs at home after returning.
The hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri is the key evidence for the permissibility at home.
4
Identify the ikhtilaf and the mufta bihi
Note that some Hanafis differ about praying at home before Eid, but the majority view (and mufta bihi) is that it is makruh. Also note the cross-madhhab difference.
Shafi'is allow voluntary prayer in the musalla; Hanafis do not.
5
Apply the ruling to a real scenario
Consider a person attending Eid in the musalla; what should they do regarding nafl prayers?
Avoid nafl in the musalla; at home, it is fine to pray after Eid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويكره التنفل قبل صلاة العيد في المصلى) بالكسر اتفاقاً (و) في (البيت) عند عامتهم وهو الأصح لأن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم خرج فصلى بهم العيد لم يصل قبلها ولا بعدها متفق عليه (و) يكره التنفل (بعدها) أي بعد صلاة العيد (في المصلى فقط) فلا يكره في البيت (على اختيار الجمهور) لقول أبي سعيد الخدري رضي الله عنه : كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لا يصلي قبل العيد شيئاً فإذا رجع إلى منزله صلى ركعتين
And it is disliked (makruh) to perform voluntary prayer before Eid prayer in the musalla by agreement, and (also) in the house according to the majority of them, and this is the most correct, because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) went out and led them in the Eid prayer; he did not pray before it nor after it (agreed upon). And it is disliked to perform voluntary prayer after it, i.e., after the Eid prayer, only in the musalla; it is not disliked in the house according to the choice of the majority, due to the saying of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) would not pray anything before the Eid, and when he returned to his home, he would pray two rak'ahs.'
Source pages p. 531

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the dislike (karaha) of supererogatory prayers before and after the Eid prayer. It is agreed upon that it is makruh to pray nafl before the Eid prayer in the musalla (outdoor prayer ground). There is a difference concerning praying at home before the Eid prayer; according to the majority it is also makruh because the Prophet did not pray any nafl before the Eid. After the Eid prayer, it is only makruh in the musalla, but not at home, based on the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri that the Prophet would pray two rak'ahs at home after returning. The preferred position (mu'tamad) is that it is makruh tanzihan to pray nafl in the musalla before and after, but at home it is permissible, especially after the Eid prayer. Some later scholars, like Qadikhan and the author of al-Tuhfa, mention that it is permissible to pray four rak'ahs after Eid, but this is interpreted as at home.

Key Terms
التنفل (al-tanafful): Performing voluntary (nafl) prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) In the musalla
B) At home
C) Both
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
Voluntary prayer before and after Eid is disliked in the musalla but permitted at home, especially after the prayer.

The Time and Performance of Eid Prayer
Defining the time and manner of Eid prayer with extra takbirs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the valid time for Eid prayer and describe the sequence of its performance, including the extra takbirs and the refinement regarding the pause between them.

Core Idea
Eid prayer time: sunrise plus a spear-length until noon; three extra takbirs after thana, with a flexible pause.

Eid prayer is a special annual worship with unique rulings. This passage clarifies its time window and the specific sequence of actions, especially the extra takbirs that distinguish it. Understanding both the time and the manner ensures the prayer is valid and follows the Hanafi tradition. We will walk through the conditions and the recommended steps.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Valid Time Window
Find the beginning and end of the time for Eid prayer as stated in the text. The time starts when the sun rises by the measure of a spear or two, and ends shortly before noon.
The spear measurement corresponds to approximately 20-30 minutes after sunrise.
2
Understand the Prohibition Premise
Recognize why prayer is not valid before that time: because prayer during sunrise is prohibited (makruh tahrimi). The text explicitly says that if performed earlier, it becomes a forbidden voluntary prayer.
This ties to the general rule of prohibited prayer times.
3
Trace the Sequence of Actions
Follow the prescribed order: intention, takbirat al-ihram, thana, three extra takbirs, then recitation and the rest of the prayer. The extra takbirs come after thana, before recitation in the first rak'ah.
The text does not detail the second rak'ah here; Hanafi fiqh adds three extra takbirs in the second rak'ah after recitation.
4
Note the Extra Takbirs and Pause
The extra takbirs are three in number, based on the madhhab of Ibn Mas'ud. Imam Abu Hanifa recommends a pause equivalent to three takbirs between each, but Al-Mabsut clarifies that this duration is not fixed; it depends on removing confusion for the followers.
This is the critical refinement: the pause is flexible according to need.
5
Apply the Ruling to a Scenario
Imagine a congregation in a large hall where followers are distant. How long should the imam pause between extra takbirs? According to Al-Mabsut, the imam should pause enough for the followers to complete the takbir, which may be longer or shorter than three takbirs.
The principle is facilitation, not rigid adherence to an estimation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وابتداء (وقت) صحة (صلاة العيد من ارتفاع الشمس قدر رمح أو رمحين) حتى تبيض للنهي عن الصلاة وقت الطلوع إلى أن تبيض لأنه كان يصلي العيد حين ترتفع الشمس قدر رمح، أو رمحين فلو صلوا قبل ذلك لا تكون صلاة عيد بل نفلاً محرماً (إلى) قبيل (زوالها) أي الشمس كما ورد به الأثر وكيفية صلاتها) أي العيدين أن ينوي عند أداء كل منهما (صلاة العيد) بقلبه ويقول بلسانه : أصلي صلاة العيد الله تعالى المقتدي ينوي المتابعة أيضاً (ثم يكبر للتحريمة ثم يقرأ الإمام والمؤتم (الثناء) سبحانك اللهم وبحمدك الخ لأنه شرع في أول الصلاة فيقدم على تكبيرات الزوائد في ظاهر الرواية (ثم يكبر ) الإمام والقوم (تكبيرات الزوائد) سميت بها لزيادتها على تكبير الإحرام والركوع يكررها (ثلاثاً) وهو مذهب ابن مسعود رضي الله عنه، ويسكت بعد كل تكبيرة مقدار ثلاث تكبيرات في رواية عن أبي حنيفة، وقال في المبسوط : هذا التقدير ليس بلازم لأن المقصود منه إزالة الاشتباه عن القوم وهو يختلف بكثرة الزحام وقلته اهـ
And the beginning of the valid time for Eid prayer is from the rising of the sun by the measure of a spear or two spears, until it becomes bright, due to the prohibition of prayer at the time of sunrise until it becomes bright. Because he (peace be upon him) used to pray the Eid when the sun rose by a spear or two spears. So if they pray before that, it is not an Eid prayer but rather a forbidden supererogatory prayer. (Until) shortly before its zenith, as reported in the tradition. And the manner of its prayer: that he intends when performing each of them (the two Eids) 'Eid prayer' in his heart, and he says with his tongue: 'I pray the Eid prayer for Allah Almighty' — the follower must also intend following the imam. Then he says the takbir of prohibition (takbirat al-ihram). Then the imam and the follower recite the Thana' (Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika...) because it is prescribed at the beginning of the prayer, so it is presented before the additional takbirs in the apparent narration. Then the imam and the people say the additional takbirs (takbirat al-zawa'id), so named for being additional to the takbir of ihram and bowing, repeating them three times. This is the madhhab of Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him). And he (Abu Hanifa) pauses after each takbir for the measure of three takbirs in one narration. Al-Mabsut says: This estimation is not binding because the purpose is to remove confusion from the people, which varies with the number of people and their lack.
Source pages p. 532

Commentary
This passage provides the time and method of performing Eid prayer. The time begins when the sun has risen approximately one or two spear lengths (about 12-24 finger widths) above the horizon, i.e., after sunrise by about 20-30 minutes, and lasts until before noon (zawal). If performed before that time, it does not count as Eid prayer and is considered a forbidden voluntary prayer. The performance: one makes intention in the heart and optionally says it verbally. The imam and followers recite the Thana' (Subhanaka) after the opening takbir. Then three extra takbirs are said, raising the hands each time. The pause between each takbir should be enough for three takbirs, but this is not fixed; the imam should pause enough for people to respond without confusion. The extra takbirs are a distinguishing feature of Eid prayer and are based on the practice of Companions like Ibn Mas'ud.

Key Terms
رمح (rumh): A spear; used as a measure of length (about 12 handspans) to indicate the sun's elevation after sunrise.
تكبيرات الزوائد (takbirat al-zawa'id): The additional takbirs said in Eid prayer beyond the regular takbirs of the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does the time for Eid prayer begin?
A) Exactly at sunrise
B) When the sun rises by one or two spear-lengths
C) After the sun has fully risen and turned white (ishraq)
D) At the time of Duha (forenoon)

Key Takeaway
Eid prayer time is after sunrise by a spear-length until before noon; the prayer includes three extra takbirs after thana, and the pause between them is flexible to suit the congregation.

Sunnah Acts of Eid Prayer and Intra-Hanafi Disputes
Critical refinement of Eid prayer sunnah acts and intra-Hanafi disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah acts of Eid prayer according to the Hanafi school and distinguish the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on the order of ta'awwudh and additional takbirs.

Core Idea
The order of ta'awwudh and takbirs in Eid prayer is a matter of priority, not validity.

This lesson unpacks the sunnah acts of Eid prayer, focusing on the recitation of specific surahs and the additional takbirs. It then delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad regarding the timing of ta'awwudh (seeking refuge) relative to the takbirs. Understanding this dispute clarifies that differences among Hanafi imams often revolve around optimal practice, not essential conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunnah acts of Eid prayer
From the text, extract the recommended recitations and actions: surahs to recite, number of additional takbirs, and raising hands.
Focus on what is sunnah muakkadah, not fard or wajib.
2
Trace the evidence for the preferred recitation
Note the hadith from Abu Hanifa and the athar of Ibn Mas'ud that support reciting Surah al-A'la and al-Ghashiyah.
The dalil is zanni al-thubut and dalalah, indicating sunnah.
3
Analyze the dispute on the order of ta'awwudh
Contrast Abu Yusuf's view (ta'awwudh before takbirs) with Muhammad's (ta'awwudh after takbirs). Understand their respective reasons.
Abu Yusuf links ta'awwudh to thana'; Muhammad links it to recitation.
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
Consult the tarjih provided by al-Tahtawi, who cites al-Bahr and Majma' al-Anhur favoring Muhammad's view.
The chosen view is that ta'awwudh comes after the opening takbir and before recitation.
5
Apply the ruling on following the imam in extra takbirs
The text explains that if the imam says more than three takbirs, the follower follows up to sixteen; beyond that, he does not. Understand the reasoning based on ijtihad and caution.
This shows the boundary between following the imam and preserving the sunnah.

Then he seeks refuge (the imam), then he says the basmalah silently, then the imam recites al-Fatihah, then recites a surah, and it is recommended that the surah be 'Sabbih isma rabbika al-a'la' in full. Then he bows (the imam), and the followers follow him. When he stands for the second [rak'ah], he begins with the basmalah, then al-Fatihah, then the surah, to connect the two recitations, and that is the best in our view, and it is recommended that the surah be 'Hal ataka hadith al-ghashiyah'. It is narrated by Imam Abu Hanifah raising it to the Prophet, peace be upon him, that he used to recite in the two 'Eids, Friday, and the day of [something] with 'Sabbih isma rabbika al-a'la' and 'Hal ataka hadith al-ghashiyah', and he also narrated it only for the two 'Eids. Then the imam and the people say the additional takbirs three times, and the imam and the people raise their hands in them as in the first rak'ah. This action, which is connecting the two recitations and saying the takbir three times in each rak'ah, is better than increasing the takbirs beyond three in each rak'ah and than placing the additional takbirs in the second rak'ah before recitation, due to the athar of Ibn Mas'ud, may Allah be pleased with him, and the agreement of a group of the Companions with him in word and deed, and its freedom from inconsistency. And his saying is preferred because of the Prophet's saying: 'I am pleased for my ummah with what Ibn Umm Abd is pleased with.' If he places the takbirs in the second rak'ah before recitation, it is permissible, because the difference is in priority, not permissibility or lack thereof. Hence, if the imam says more than what we said, the follower follows him up to sixteen takbirs; if he increases beyond that, the follower is not obliged to follow him, because after that it is definitely prohibited, exceeding what has been reported in the traditions. His saying: (and his saying is preferred) for that reason, the imam's agreement with him is frequent. His saying: (because the difference is in priority) He said in al-Bahr: The difference is in priority, and there is no difference in permissibility, because of Muhammad's saying in al-Muwatta' after mentioning the narrations: 'Whatever I have adopted, it is good; and if there were abrogating and abrogated, Muhammad would be more knowledgeable of them.' His saying: (hence if the imam says more) i.e., because the difference is in priority. His saying: (the follower follows him) because he has committed to his prayer, so he must act according to his opinion. His saying: (because after that) i.e., he has left the realm of ijtihad, so it becomes like acting upon the abrogated. Then they said: This is if he heard from the imam; but if he only heard from the muballigh, then he follows him even if he exceeds this number, due to the possibility of error by the muballigh in what preceded, so he does not leave the obligatory as a precaution. Hence it is said: He intends the opening with each takbir due to the possibility of preceding the imam in each takbir.

Commentary
This passage from at-Tahtawi's Hashiya on Maraqi al-Falah is a critical refinement of rulings on Eid prayer. It first outlines the recommended sunnah acts: the imam recites Surah al-A'la in the first rak'ah and Surah al-Ghashiyah in the second, based on a hadith transmitted by Abu Hanifa. The additional takbirs (takbeerat al-zawa'id) are three in each rak'ah, and raising the hands is sunnah. The commentary then discusses the order: it is preferable to recite the surah after the takbirs in the second rak'ah, but if the imam places the takbirs before recitation, it is still valid. The preferred view is supported by an athar from Ibn Mas'ud and the Prophet's approval of him. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Muhammad holds that ta'awwudh (seeking refuge) is recited after the opening takbir, while Abu Yusuf places it before the additional takbirs because it follows the thana'. The chosen view is Muhammad's. The commentary also addresses the follower who exceeds sixteen takbirs: he is not obliged to follow beyond that, as additional ones are prohibited. If the follower only hears the muballigh, he follows even if more, to be cautious. Also, if the imam does not raise his hands in bowing, the follower still raises them, not following the imam in leaving the sunnah. The passage emphasizes that differences are in priority, not permissibility, and provides scriptural evidence.

Key Terms
تكبيرات الزوائد (takbeerat al-zawa'id): Additional takbirs said in Eid prayer, three in each rak'ah after the opening takbir.
الموالاة بين القراءتين (al-muwalat bayn al-qira'atayn): Connecting the recitation of the surah in the first rak'ah to the second rak'ah without interruption by sunnah acts.
التعوذ (al-ta'awwudh): Saying 'A'udhu billahi min al-shaytan al-rajim' before recitation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on the order of additional takbirs and recitation in the second rak'ah of Eid prayer?
A) Recitation must be before takbirs; the prayer is invalid otherwise.
B) Takbirs must be before recitation; it is wajib.
C) Recitation before takbirs is preferred, but takbirs first is permissible.
D) The order does not matter; both are equally good.

Key Takeaway
The sunnah acts of Eid prayer are clearly defined, and intra-Hanafi differences revolve around priority, not validity; the follower must follow the imam in permissible variations up to a limit.
