How the Masbuq Makes Up Missed Takbirs in Eid Prayer
Intra-Hanafi dispute on masbuq takbirs in Eid prayer makeup

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Abu Hanifa's ruling on whether a masbuq says additional takbirs while bowing and distinguish it from Abu Yusuf's position, identifying the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
A masbuq follows his own opinion in makeup; Abu Hanifa permits takbirs in bowing, Abu Yusuf omits them.

In Eid prayer, the additional takbirs are sunnah, but when a masbuq (latecomer) makes up a missed rak'ah, a dispute arises: should he say those takbirs while bowing if necessary? Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf differ, and the preferred view allows takbirs in bowing. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and practical scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the masbuq and his makeup status
Determine that the masbuq is making up a missed rak'ah and is considered individually in that makeup, following his own madhhab opinion.
2
Apply the general principle for makeup order
According to Abu Hanifa, the masbuq begins makeup with recitation (Fatihah + surah) before the extra takbirs, based on the practice of Imam Ali.
3
Analyze the scenario when catching the imam in bowing
If the masbuq catches the imam bowing and fears missing the rak'ah, he says the extra takbirs while bowing (Abu Hanifa) or omits them and recites tasbih (Abu Yusuf). Evaluate the practical consequence.
4
Assess the when the imam moves on
If the imam raises his head before the masbuq finishes takbirs, the remaining takbirs are dropped to preserve obligatory following (wajib).
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The later authorities (Fath al-Qadir, al-Muhit) prefer Abu Hanifa's view: the masbuq says takbirs while bowing according to his own opinion.

He says takbirs in what he makes up, according to Abu Hanifa's saying: If he is preceded by one rak'ah, he begins in making it up with recitation, then he says takbirs, because if he began with takbirs, he would connect the takbirs, and none of the Companions said that, so he agrees with the opinion of Imam Ali ibn Abi Talib, so it is better, and it specifies their saying that the masbuq prays the beginning of his prayer in terms of dhikr. If he catches the imam in bowing, he says the ihram takbir standing, and says the additional takbirs also standing if he is safe from missing the rak'ah by joining the imam in bowing. Otherwise, he says the ihram takbir standing, then bows joining the imam in bowing, and says the takbirs for the additional (takbirs) while bowing, without raising his hands. The missing dhikr is made up before the imam finishes, unlike action. Raising the hands then is a sunnah not in its place, and it misses the sunnah that is in its place, which is placing the hands on the knees. If the imam raises his head, what remains of the takbirs is dropped from the follower, because if he does it in bowing, he would necessarily miss the obligatory following for what is wajib. If he catches him after he raised his head standing, he does not perform the takbirs because he prays the rak'ah with its takbirs. This is in Fath al-Qadir. If he catches the imam and he has said some takbirs, he follows him and makes up what he missed immediately, then follows his imam. If he catches him and he has started recitation, he says the ihram takbir and performs the additional takbirs according to his own opinion because he is masbuq. If he catches him standing and he hasn't said takbir until he bowed, he does not say takbirs according to what is preferred in al-Muhit. If he catches him after he raised his head from bowing, he does not say takbirs by agreement. If the imam bowed before he said takbir, he says takbir while bowing, and he does not return to standing to say takbir in the apparent riwayah; if he returns, it does not invalidate. As in Sharh al-Sayyid. His saying: (he would necessarily miss the obligatory following) therein is that following here is wajib. His saying: (after the prayer) this is a statement of preference. His saying: (he teaches in them the rulings of sadaqat al-fitr) i.e., in one of them, the first, and this is about the khutbah of Fitr. The ruling of udhiyah will come later. And likewise every ruling that is needed. His saying: because the khutbah is prescribed for that purpose i.e., for teaching. The author of al-Bahr said as a discussion: It is fitting for the khatib to teach them the rulings in Jumu'ah before 'Eid because the recommended in sadaqat al-fitr...
Source pages p. 534

Commentary
This passage continues at-Tahtawi's Hashiya, focusing on the masbuq (latecomer) in Eid prayer. The masbuq is one who misses part of the prayer and makes it up. According to Abu Hanifa, if the masbuq misses one rak'ah, he begins his makeup with recitation (al-Fatihah and surah) before the additional takbirs, because beginning with takbirs would connect them without any Companion's precedent, whereas starting with recitation follows Ali ibn Abi Talib's opinion. This specifies the general rule that the masbuq prays the beginning of his prayer in terms of dhikr (i.e., the order of his own prayer). If the masbuq catches the imam in bowing, he says the opening takbir standing and also says the additional takbirs standing if he is sure not to miss the rak'ah by joining the imam in the bow. Otherwise, he says only the opening takbir standing, then bows and says the additional takbirs while bowing (without raising hands). If he raises his hands while bowing, it is a sunnah not in its place. There is a dispute: Abu Yusuf says the masbuq should skip the additional takbirs and occupy himself with the tasbih of bowing, because that is the actual place. The author prefers Abu Hanifa's view. If the imam raises his head before the masbuq finishes his takbirs, the remaining takbirs are dropped. The masbuq must avoid missing the obligatory following of the imam (which is wajib). The passage also covers various scenarios (catching the imam in different states). Finally, it discusses the khutbah after Eid prayer: the imam gives two khutbahs after the prayer, teaching the rulings of sadaqat al-fitr (and other necessary matters), as the khutbah is prescribed for teaching. The commentary notes that it is better to teach these rulings in the Friday before Eid as well.

Key Terms
مسبوق (masbuq): A person who joins the prayer late and misses one or more rak'ahs, making them up after the imam.
لاحق (lahiq): A person who is behind the imam due to a delay but still within the same prayer, not a latecomer.
المتابعة المفروضة (al-mutaba'ah al-mafrudah): Obligatory following of the imam in actions like bowing and prostrating, which is wajib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a masbuq cannot say the extra takbirs standing without missing the rak'ah, he should:
A) Skip the takbirs entirely and just recite tasbih.
B) Say the takbirs while bowing.
C) Recite the takbirs after the imam's salam.
D) Raise his hands and say takbirs while bowing.

Key Takeaway
The masbuq in Eid prayer says additional takbirs according to his own opinion (Abu Hanifa), even if bowing, and the obligatory following does not constrain his makeup.

The Masbuq's Sequence in Making Up Eid Prayer: Recitation Before Takbir
Explains the proper sequence for the masbuq in Eid prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the masbuq in Eid prayer begins his qada with recitation, then performs takbir, and identify the proof from the Companion 'Ali ibn Abi Talib.

Core Idea
The masbuq in Eid prayer begins qada with recitation, then takbir — following the opinion of 'Ali (ra), not other Companions.

When a person joins the Eid prayer late (masbuq) and misses a rak'ah, there is a specific sequence he must follow when making it up. The Hanafi school, based on the practice of 'Ali ibn Abi Talib, instructs him to begin with recitation, then perform the additional takbirs. This lesson explores that ruling and its evidence from the text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the masbuq making up a missed rak'ah in Eid prayer. The ruling: he must start with recitation (qira'ah), then say the takbir (additional takbirs).
This sequence applies to the qada portion of the masbuq's prayer.
2
Locate the dalil
The text cites the opinion of Imam 'Ali ibn Abi Talib (ra) and notes that no other Companion said otherwise. This is used as a proof for the sequence.
The Hanafi school accepts qawl sahabi as a valid source under certain conditions.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The proof is that if the masbuq started with takbir, he would perform all takbirs consecutively without recitation, which no Companion advocated. Following 'Ali (ra) is thus the most appropriate.
The text says 'fakan awla' (so it is more appropriate).
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf differs regarding the scenario when the masbuq catches the imam in ruku': he prefers dropping the takbir and occupying with tasbih. However, the text prefers Abu Hanifa's view.
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's position.

Book of Prayer. He says takbir in which according to Abu Hanifa: If he missed a rak'ah, he begins in his qada with recitation, then he says takbir, because if he started with takbir and joined between the takbirs, no Companion said that, so it agrees with the opinion of Imam Ali ibn Abi Talib, so it is more appropriate, and it specifies their statement that the masbuq makes up the first of his prayer with respect to remembrances. And if he catches the imam bowing, he makes ihram standing, and says the additional takbirs standing also if he is safe from missing the rak'ah by joining the imam in bowing; otherwise he says takbir for ihram standing, then bows participating with the imam in bowing and says the additional takbirs bent over, without raising his hands. The missed dhikr he makes up before the imam finishes, unlike action. And raising the hands then is a sunnah not in its place, and he misses the sunnah that is in its place, which is placing the hands on the knees. And if the imam raises his head, the follower is relieved of the remaining takbirs, because if he performed them in bowing, he would necessarily abandon the obligatory following for a wajib. And if he catches him after he has raised his head standing, he does not perform the takbir because he makes up the rak'ah with its takbirs, thus in Fath al-Qadir. His statement: (And if he is a masbuq etc.) He said in al-Siraj: The masbuq performs takbir in what he makes up according to his own opinion, and opposes his imam's opinion because he is alone, unlike the lahiq, for he performs takbir according to his imam's opinion and opposes his own opinion because he is behind the imam legally. His statement: (And if he missed a rak'ah) i.e., and he was among those who hold the view of Abu Hanifa. His statement: (So he agrees with the opinion of Imam Ali i.e., by beginning in the qada with recitation, then he says takbir. His statement: (So it is more appropriate) than departing from all their statements, i.e., if he began with takbir then recited. His statement: (by his joining) is connected to 'is safe from'. His statement: (And he says the additional takbirs bent over according to his own opinion because he is a masbuq, and Abu Yusuf said: he occupies himself with the tasbih of bowing because that is its proper place, and the takbir is dropped from him. His statement: because the missed dhikr etc.) as when he catches him in the prayer upon the Prophet, he begins with the tashahhud he missed, and as when he catches him in the third rak'ah of witr bowing, he performs the qunut if safe from missing the bowing, and likewise he performs the thana' likewise. His statement: (and he misses) from tafwit. His statement: (the follower is relieved of what remains) i.e., if he did not perform any takbir, and he does not perform them in the second. And if he catches the imam having performed some of the takbirs, he follows him and makes up what he missed immediately, then follows his imam. And if he catches him having started recitation, he says the opening takbir, and performs the additional ones according to his own opinion because he is a masbuq. And if he catches him standing, and did not say takbir until he bowed, he does not say takbir according to what is chosen in al-Muhit. And if he catches him after he raised his head from bowing, and did not say takbir by agreement. And if the imam bowed before he said takbir, he says takbir while bowing, and does not return to standing to say takbir in the apparent narration, and if he returns, it does not invalidate as in the commentary of al-Sayyid. His statement: (he necessarily abandons the obligatory following) in it is that following here is wajib.

Commentary
This passage discusses the rulings for a masbuq (latecomer) in Eid prayer. According to Abu Hanifa, when the masbuq makes up the missed rak'ah, he begins with recitation (qira'ah) and then performs the takbirat, because if he started with takbir, he would be performing all the takbirat consecutively without recitation, which no Companion said. Thus he follows the opinion of 'Ali ibn Abi Talib. This is preferable and specifies the general rule that the masbuq makes up the first part of his prayer with respect to dhikr (remembrances). If he catches the imam in ruku', he should make the opening takbir standing, and also the additional takbirat standing if he fears missing the rak'ah by joining the imam in ruku'; otherwise, he bows and performs the additional takbir while bowing. The commentary elaborates on the details of when to perform the takbirat, including scenarios where the imam has already performed some takbirs or has started recitation. It also mentions the opinion of Abu Yusuf, who says to occupy oneself with the tasbih of bowing instead of the additional takbirs if catching the imam in bowing. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) follows the view of Abu Hanifa, as indicated by the text's preference.

Key Terms
مسبوق (masbuq): A person who joins the congregational prayer after the imam has already begun, missing one or more rak'ahs.
قضاء (qada): The act of performing the missed portion of prayer after the imam has completed it.
تكبيرات الزوائد (takbirat al-zawa'id): The additional takbirs performed in 'Eid prayer, beyond the opening takbir, which are wajib in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The masbuq in Eid prayer must begin his qada with recitation, then perform the additional takbirs, based on the practice of Imam 'Ali (ra).

Rulings for the Masbuq in Eid Prayer: Practical Scenarios
Explains practical scenarios for the masbuq in Eid prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings for the masbuq in Eid prayer to different scenarios: catching the imam standing, bowing, or after rising from bowing, and distinguish between the views of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
The masbuq's takbir placement depends on when he catches the imam — priority of following the imam over performing all takbirs.

The masbuq in Eid prayer faces different situations depending on the imam's actions. Should he perform additional takbirs while bowing? What if the imam raises his head? This lesson covers the detailed scenarios and the preferred Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenarios
Three main cases: catching the imam standing (before ruku'), catching the imam in ruku', and catching the imam after ruku' (i.e., after raising head).
Each scenario has a different ruling for the additional takbirs.
2
Apply the ruling for catching imam standing
If the masbuq catches the imam standing (before ruku'), he says the opening takbir and the additional takbirs standing, then follows the imam.
He should also recite (Fatiha + surah) in his own qada later.
3
Apply the ruling for catching imam in ruku'
Two sub-cases: if he is safe from missing the rak'ah (imam has not yet risen), he says the additional takbirs standing then bows; otherwise, he bows and says them while bowing. Abu Yusuf says drop them and do tasbih.
The text prefers Abu Hanifa's view of performing takbirs while bowing.
4
Apply the ruling for catching imam after ruku'
If the imam has raised his head, the masbuq does not say the additional takbirs at all. He makes up the rak'ah later with its takbirs.
This is to maintain the obligation of following the imam (mutaba'ah).

Source Text

Key Terms
متابعة (mutaba'ah): The obligation of the follower (ma'mum) to closely follow the imam's actions without delay.
تكبيرات الزوائد (takbirat al-zawa'id): The additional takbirs in 'Eid prayer, three in the first rak'ah and three in the second, excluding the opening takbir.

Checkpoint
If a masbuq catches the imam in 'Eid prayer while the imam is bowing and the masbuq fears missing the rak'ah, what should he do according to the Hanafi school?
A) Perform the additional takbirs standing, then bow.
B) Bow and perform the additional takbirs while bowing.
C) Drop the additional takbirs and do tasbih in bowing.
D) Perform the additional takbirs after joining the bowing.

Key Takeaway
The masbuq in Eid prayer must adjust his performance of the additional takbirs based on when he catches the imam, prioritizing the obligation of following the imam (mutaba'ah).

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Ruling on Missing the Eid Prayer
Ruling statement with alternatives and reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a missed Eid prayer and apply the appropriate alternative (nafl or joining another congregation).

Core Idea
The missed Eid prayer is not made up; one prays nafl or joins another congregation.

What happens if you arrive late for Eid prayer and miss the congregation? This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position that the Eid prayer, being a sunnah muakkadah with conditions requiring the imam, is not subject to qada. Instead, the school provides clear alternatives to ensure you still gain reward.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its nature
Recognize that the act in question is the Eid prayer (salat al-'idayn), a sunnah muakkadah prayer that requires congregation and a valid imam (sultan or deputy).
2
State the ruling on missing it
The passage explicitly says 'la yaqdiha' – he does not make it up. Understand that qada is not prescribed for this prayer.
This distinguishes it from obligations like the five daily prayers.
3
Understand the reasoning
The reason given is that the Eid prayer is only valid (qurba) with conditions that require the imam. Without the imam, the conditions cannot be fulfilled, so no qada.
The imam refers to the state-appointed leader or his deputy.
4
Identify the alternatives
The person has two options: leave (no action) or pray a voluntary prayer (nafl). The best is to pray four rak'ahs with the intention of duha.
Some later Hanafis also mention joining another congregation if possible.
5
Note the practical implications
If another congregation is found, one should join it because multiple Eid congregations are permissible. Otherwise, the nafl prayer suffices.
This is derived from the later part of the text about 'adrakaha ma'a ghayrihi'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن فاتته الصلاة فلم يدركها مع الإمام لا يقضيها لأنها لم تعرف قربة إلا بشرائط لا تتم بدون الإمام أي السلطان أو مأموره فإن شاء انصرف وإن شاء صلى نفلاً والأفضل أربع فيكون له صلاة الضحى لما روي عن ابن مسعود رضي الله عنه أنه قال: من يعم خطب الحج الثلاث مع أداؤها قبل الخروج إلى المصلي، وابتداء تكبير التشريف من فجر يوم عرفة، فلا يفيد هنا التعليم اهـ. قال والعلم أمانة في عنق العلماء اهـ ويقوي هذا البحث ما يأتي في صدقة الفطر أنه كان يخطب قبل العيد بيومين خطبة يبين فيها أحكام صدقة الفطر اهـ. قوله : (من تجب عليه وهو الحر المسلم المالك للنصاب، ولو غير تام قوله : (ولمن تجب) هو مصرف الزكاة قوله : (ومم (تجب من البر وسويقيه ودقيقه والشعير كذلك والتمر والزبيب وما سوها بالقيمة . قوله : ( ومقدار الواجب هو نصف صاع من بر أو صاع من تمر أو شعير أو زبيب قوله: (ووقت الوجوب) هو طلوع الفجر من يوم الفطر. قوله : (ويجلس بين الخطبتين) لا قبلهما عندنا كذا في الدر. قوله: (وليس) لذلك أي للتكبير الواقع في أثناء الخطبة عدد فلا ينافي قوله بعد، ويستحب أن يستفتح الخ. قوله : (وغيرها) هذا . أنه يبدؤها بالتكبير إلا أن التي بمكة وعرفة يبدو فيهما بالتكبير، ثم بالتلبية، ثم بالخطبة كما ذكره في الدر. قوله : (تترى) أي متتابعات، ويكبر قبل النزول أربعة عشر كذا في الشرح . قوله : ( في أنفسهم المراد أنهم يسرون به كما تقدم، والظاهر أنه متعلق بالتكبير، والصلاة لأنه يجب الإنصات لجميعها، وقوله سنة الإنصات الأولى أن يقول وواجب الإنصات. قوله : (ومن مع الإمام أو بخروج وقتها سواء كان لعذر أم لا إلا أنه يأثم في الثاني دون الأول، وكما إذا لم يشرع أصلاً، أو شرع، ثم أفسده اتفاقاً على الأصح، وفيها يلغز أي رجل أفسد صلاة واجبة عليه، ولا قضاء عليه در ولو قدر بعد الفوات مع الإمام على إدراكها مع غيره فعل للاتفاق على جواز تعددها قوله لا تتم بدون الإمام أي السلطان، أو مأموره) أي وقد صلاها الإمام، أو مأموره فإن كان مأموراً بإقامتها له أن يقيمها قوله : (وإن شاء صلى نفلا) لعله محمول على الصلاة في غير المصلى لما تقدم من كراهة الصلاة فيه بعدها. قوله: (فيكون) أي ما صلاه له صلاة الضحى قال في العناية : فإن قيل : هي قائمة مقام صلاة الضحى، ولهذا تكره صلاة الضحى قبل صلاة العيد، فإذا عجز عنها يصير إلى الأصل كالجمعة إذا فاتت فانه يصير فاتته الصلاة
And whoever misses the prayer and does not catch it with the imam does not make it up, because it is not known as an act of worship except with conditions that are not complete without the imam, i.e., the sultan or his deputy. If he wishes, he may leave, and if he wishes, he may pray nafl, and the best is four, so it becomes for him the duha prayer, due to what was narrated from Ibn Mas'ud that he said: 'Whoever ... the three Hajj sermons with its performance before going out to the musalla, and the beginning of the takbir of tashrif from Fajr of the day of Arafah, so it does not benefit here the teaching.' He said: 'And knowledge is a trust on the necks of the scholars.' And this research is strengthened by what comes in sadaqat al-fitr that he used to deliver a khutbah two days before Eid explaining the rulings of sadaqat al-fitr. His statement: (upon whom it is obligatory) he is the free Muslim who owns the nisab, even if incomplete. His statement: (and for whom it is obligatory) it is the recipient of zakat. His statement: (and from what it is obligatory) from wheat and its sawiq and its flour, and barley likewise, and dates, raisins, and what is equivalent in value. His statement: (and the amount of the wajib) it is half a sa' of wheat or a sa' of dates or barley or raisins. His statement: (and the time of obligation) it is dawn of the day of Fitr. His statement: (and he sits between the two khutbahs) not before them according to us, thus in al-Durr. His statement: (and there is not) for that, i.e., for the takbir occurring during the khutbah, a number, so it does not contradict his later statement that it is mustahabb to open etc. His statement: (and other than it) this. That he begins them with takbir except those in Makkah and Arafah: he begins in them with takbir, then talbiyah, then the khutbah, as mentioned in al-Durr. His statement: (consecutive) i.e., consecutive, and he says takbir before descending fourteen, thus in the commentary. His statement: (in themselves) means they do it quietly as before, and apparently it is connected to takbir and salat because it is wajib to listen attentively to all of it, and his statement 'sunnah of attentiveness' should rather be 'wajib of attentiveness'. His statement: (and whoever) with the imam or by the exit of its time, whether with an excuse or not, except that he sins in the second without the first, and as if he did not start at all, or started and then invalidated it by agreement according to the most correct, and in it there is an enigma: a man who invalidates a prayer wajib upon him, and there is no qada upon him. And if he is able after the prayer with the imam to catch it with another, he does so due to agreement on permissibility of multiple prayers. His statement: (is not complete without the imam) i.e., the sultan or his deputy, and he has already prayed the imam or his deputy, so if he is deputed to establish it, he may do so. His statement: (and if he wishes, he prays nafl) perhaps it is understood as praying in other than the musalla due to the earlier dislike of praying in it after it. His statement: (so it becomes) i.e., what he prays becomes duha prayer. He said in al-'Inayah: If it is said, it stands in place of duha prayer, and for this reason duha prayer is disliked before Eid prayer, so if he is unable, he returns to the original, like Jumu'ah if missed, then it becomes... 'missed prayer'.
Source pages p. 535

Commentary
This passage deals with the situation of someone who misses the Eid prayer (either 'Eid al-Fitr or 'Eid al-Adha) with the congregation. According to the Hanafi school, such a person does not make up the prayer as qada because the Eid prayer is only valid with specific conditions that require the imam (the sultan or his deputy) to lead it. However, he has two options: either leave or pray a nafl (voluntary) prayer. The best option is to pray four rak'ahs with the intention of duha prayer, as this substitutes for the missed Eid prayer. The text also contains extensive commentary on related issues, including the rulings of sadaqat al-fitr, the sitting between khutbahs, the number of takbirs in the khutbah, and the practice in Makkah and Arafah. The commentator clarifies that the Eid prayer is not like Jumu'ah; one cannot make it up individually. However, if one can catch the same Eid prayer with another congregation, he should do so, as multiple Eid congregations are permissible.

Key Terms
صلاة العيد (salat al-'idayn): The Eid prayer, a sunnah muakkadah prayer consisting of two rak'ahs with additional takbirs, performed in congregation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the best action for a person who misses the Eid prayer and has no other congregation to join?
A) Make it up as qada
B) Pray four rak'ahs of nafl with intention of duha
C) Pray two rak'ahs of nafl
D) Leave without praying

Key Takeaway
The missed Eid prayer is not made up; instead, one prays nafl (preferably four rak'ahs of duha) or joins another congregation if available.
